601 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Mower County Board of Comm'rs v. Board of Trustees


No. 39,504


Supreme Court of Minnesota


271 Minn. 505; 136 N.W.2d 671; 1965 Minn. LEXIS 753



July 9, 1965 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Ramsey County District Court brought by the Mower County Board of Commissioners and Mower County for a declaratory judgment concerning their obligations to defendant, the Board of Trustees of the Public Employees Retirement Association. Said defendant counterclaimed, alleging that plaintiffs were indebted to defendant in the sum of $ 5,082.99, and the court, Harold W. Schultz, Judge, granted defendant's motion for summary judgment. Plaintiffs appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff County Board of Commissioners appealed the decision of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which held that defendant Public Employees Retirement Association's (PERA) claims were lawful. PERA found that the board was liable for certain employer contributions under Minn. Stat. § 353.60 (1), (2) (1961), 1957 Minn. Laws 935, § 7. The board argued that it was not required to make the contributions under Minn. Const. art. 9, § 1.


OVERVIEW: The Public Employees Retirement Association (PERA) found that a county board was liable for employer contributions on the salaries of certain public employees pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 353.60(1), (2) (1961), 1957 Minn. Laws ch. 935, § 7, which made governmental subdivisions liable for employer contributions based on salaries derived from fees. The county board asserted that if they were required to make the contributions under § 353.60(1), (2) this would violate Minn. Const. art. 9, § 1. The trial court awarded judgment to PERA and this decision was affirmed by the court. Generally, an official charged with the performance of a ministerial duty was not allowed to question the constitutionality of a law under which it was charged to act. The court found that the county board's duties under Minn. Stat. § 353.60(1), (2) were ministerial and held that the public interest in this matter was not so great as to demand constitutional review of that statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision that found that the county board lacked standing.

 

602 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


In re Cold Spring Granite Co.


Nos. 39,408, 39,409, 39,410


Supreme Court of Minnesota


271 Minn. 460; 136 N.W.2d 782; 1965 Minn. LEXIS 747



July 2, 1965 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Three appeals by two taxpayers, Cold Spring Granite Company and Granit-Bronz, Inc., from an order of the Stearns County District Court, Byron R. Wilson, Judge, denying a motion for a new trial after adverse findings in proceedings brought by them to have certain taxes levied against their real and personal property declared invalid.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers appealed from a decision of the Stearns County District Court (Minnesota), which denied the taxpayers' motion for a new trial after judgment was rendered against them in their action to have certain taxes levied against their real and personal property declared invalid.


OVERVIEW: Minn. Stat. § 124.51 provided a method for taxation, collection, and payment of tuition by school districts not maintaining classified secondary schools. The taxpayers contended that § 124.51, as construed and applied, was invalid as being contrary to the uniformity clause of the state constitution, Minn. Const. art. IX, § 1, and art. I, §§ 2, 7, and 8, and to the equal protection and due process clauses of U.S. Const. Amend. XIV. The court rejected those contentions. The court referred to other holdings concerning the uniformity clause that stated that perfect uniformity and perfect equality of taxation was impossible and not the goal. Uniformity did not require the equal application of a tax to all who might come within its operation. The statute was entitled to respect from the judiciary because the statute's predecessor had been given a similar construction by the attorney general, the department of education, and the public examiner has been consistent since 1947.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

603 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Adelman v. Onischuk


Nos. 39,569, 39,608


Supreme Court of Minnesota


271 Minn. 216; 135 N.W.2d 670; 1965 Minn. LEXIS 719



May 18, 1965 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certified to U.S. Supreme Court August 27, 1965.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action in the Dakota County District Court brought by Joseph A. Adelman and Joseph W. Kennealy, individually and as representatives of all persons in said county owning land in the Lower Minnesota River Watershed District, to enjoin the county auditor, the county board, and said watershed district from proceeding with certain improvements. The court, Robert J. Breunig, Judge, granted the injunction, and defendant district appealed from said order.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant watershed district sought review of a decision of the Dakota County District Court (Minnesota), which granted respondent landowners' injunction that enjoined the watershed district from proceeding further in carrying out a planned improvement of a portion of the Minnesota River.


OVERVIEW: The landowners contended that the Minnesota Watershed Act, Minn. Stat. ch. 112, was unconstitutional and sought an injunction enjoining the watershed district from proceeding with a project to improve the Minnesota River channel. The trial court granted the injunction and enjoined the watershed district from doing any act in connection with the levy, collection, or enforcement of assessments. The trial court held that the Minnesota Watershed Act was unconstitutional because it was vague, ambiguous, discriminatory, and inconsistent and was incapable of any reasonable interpretation or enforcement. On appeal, the court found that the landowners had several opportunities to assert their objections to the creation of the district and to the assessments levied for the channel-improvement project. Any proceedings in equity thereafter were untimely. Failure to exhaust available administrative remedies in a timely manner when those remedies were simple, direct, and expedient constituted a bar to an unseasonable action in equity. It could not be said that the opportunities for the landowners to raise objections were either impractical or inadequate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

 

604 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Bolin Lumber Co. v. Chicago & N. W. R. Co.


Nos. 39,450, 39,451, 39,452


Supreme Court of Minnesota


270 Minn. 516; 134 N.W.2d 312; 1965 Minn. LEXIS 823



April 2, 1965 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Three appeals in the Cottonwood County District Court by Chicago and North Western Railway Company from orders of the Railroad and Warehouse Commission fixing rents on properties owned by said company and leased to complainants, Bolin Lumber Company, Jesse O. Olson, and M. J. Gjertson, d.b.a. Gjertson Farm Supply. The cases were heard together before L. J. Irvine, Judge, and appellant appealed from an order affirming the commission.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant railway company disputed an order of the Cottonwood County District Court (Minnesota), which affirmed three orders by the Railroad and Warehouse Commission (Minnesota) fixing rents on properties owned by the company and leased to respondent lessees. The main issue was whether the Commission had jurisdiction under any or all of Minn. Stat. §§ 230.09, 230.10, 230.11 to fix the level of rents to be paid for the leased properties.


OVERVIEW: All three properties were separated from the main railroad tracks by a city street. One of the lessees, a lumberyard, received only cement goods via rail. Its other shipments were by truck. Another lessee made rare use of railroad facilities. The third lessee's business had declined and it was no longer feasible for that lessee to order in freight carload shipments. On appeal, the court held that it was intended that railroad properties subject to rent-control jurisdiction by the Commission be devoted to a public use. The power granted by §§ 230.09, 230.10, 230.11 was in the nature of eminent domain and, as such, could only be exercised under Minn. Const. art. I, § 13 where the expropriation was for a public use. To preserve the constitutionality of the statutes, the court construed them as including that qualification. Thus, property taken under the statutes had to be open to members of the general public to aid them in shipping and receiving their own goods, which requirement the lessees did not meet. The court held that §§ 230.09, 230.10, 230.11 were not intended to apply to cases such as the one at bar. Nor could the leased properties be considered part of the right of way.


OUTCOME: The court reversed with directions to enter an order vacating and setting aside the order of the Commission.

 

605 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Construction & General Laborers Union v. St. Paul


No. 39,357


Supreme Court of Minnesota


270 Minn. 427; 134 N.W.2d 26; 1965 Minn. LEXIS 811; 51 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P51,279



March 19, 1965 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Ramsey County District Court by Construction and General Laborers Union, Local 563, AFL-CIO; LeRoy Larson; and John L. Miller for a declaratory judgment invalidating an ordinance of the city of St. Paul and enjoining its enforcement. Defendants named were said city; its Board of Education; its commissioner of parks, recreation, and public buildings; its architect; and McGough Construction Company, Inc. The court, Leonard J. Keyes, Judge, granted plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment, and defendants other than the Board of Education and the construction company appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a city and others, sought review of a decision of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment in favor of plaintiffs, a union local and two members, on their action, under the Uniform Declaratory Judgments Act, Minn. Stat. ch. 555, seeking a judgment declaring St. Paul, Minn. Legislative Code, ch. 104, unconstitutional and void.


OVERVIEW: The city passed an ordinance that compelled all contractors performing work for the city to employ only county residents, which included residents of the city. The employees were required to obtain from the city clerk a resident identification card which certified that he was a resident of the county. The sanction imposed against a contractor who violated the requirement was the loss of his contract. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the union local, and on appeal, the court affirmed. Under the city's charter, the activity of laborers was a statewide matter and not one for local regulation so long as the activity was not inherently dangerous to the health, welfare, safety, or morals of the people of the city. The ordinance was partial and discriminatory both upon its face and in its operation for, by its very terms, the performance of the occupation of a laborer was permitted in the city if he lived in the county but was prohibited to him if he lived elsewhere. The ordinance was, in so far as it discriminated between resident and nonresident citizens, unconstitutional and void.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment in favor of the union local and the members on the action against the city and declaring the ordinance unconstitutional was affirmed.

 

606 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Webster v. Marshall


No. 39,426


Supreme Court of Minnesota


270 Minn. 292; 133 N.W.2d 533; 1965 Minn. LEXIS 793



February 11, 1965 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari in the Ramsey County District Court upon the relation of Richard S. Webster to review an order of the commissioner of highways dismissing said relator from the highway patrol. The court, Harold W. Schultz, Judge, ordered that relator be suspended for 4 months and then reinstated, and the commissioner appealed from said order.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Commissioner of Highways sought review by certiorari of the order of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which modified the discipline the Commissioner imposed upon respondent patrolman.


OVERVIEW: The Commissioner repealed his policy of permitting patrolmen to perform work as truckers outside of their law enforcement duties. The patrolman needed part-time trucking work to meet his court imposed family obligations and continued to work as a trucker even though he had been ordered not to work. The Commissioner dismissed the patrolman for the willful violation of a work rule under the authority granted to him by Minn. Stat. 161.47 Subd. 8(2). Before the lower court, the patrolman introduced evidence that other officers routinely received less punishment for more serious violations. The lower court ordered that the patrolman's dismissal be vacated and that his punishment be reduced to a suspension. The court reversed the lower court's order, holding that the lower court's function was to ascertain whether there was any substantial evidence supporting the Commissioner's decision, not to arrive at an independent conclusion pertaining to the propriety of the discipline imposed by the Commissioner. The court ruled that by substituting its judgment for that of the Commissioner, the lower court had violated Minn. Const. art. 3, § 1, dealing with the division of governmental powers.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's order, which held that the patrolman should have been suspended and reinstated, and the court sustained the Commissioner's action in dismissing the patrolman.

 

607 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Grobe v. Oak Center Creamery Co.


No. 39,527


Supreme Court of Minnesota


269 Minn. 505; 131 N.W.2d 621; 1964 Minn. LEXIS 807



November 25, 1964 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari upon the relation of Elwood B. Grobe and Arlene M. Grobe to review an order of the Wabasha County District Court, Leo F. Murphy, Judge, denying their motion to vacate a judgment in a condemnation proceeding brought by Oak Center Creamery Company to acquire an easement against relators' property.



DISPOSITION: Writ quashed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A writ of certiorari was granted for a review of an order of the Wabasha County District Court (Minnesota) that denied relator owners' motion to vacate a judgment of condemnation of their property in favor of respondent creamery.


OVERVIEW: The creamery sought an easement in the owners' property so that it could construct a sewer drain for disposal of waste flowage from its structures. The owners orally challenged the constitutionality of Minn. Stat. § 308.39, but after a hearing the trial court granted the creamery's petition and appointed commissioners to establish the value of the condemned property. The value was established at $ 1000, but was rejected by the owners. The owners obtained a writ of certiorari from the court that sought reversal of the trial court's order on the grounds of the unconstitutionality of § 308.39, which was dismissed as not being ripe. A check was deposited with the trial court, after which judgment was entered in favor of the creamery. After a failed appeal, the owners obtained certiorari and challenged the trial court's jurisdiction over the condemnation proceedings. The owners asserted that because they had failed to notify the attorney general of their appeal of the statute's constitutionality, the trial court lost jurisdiction over the condemnation proceedings. The court quashed the writ and held that the trial court retained jurisdiction over other condemnation related matters.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the writ of certiorari.

 

608 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Edwards


No. 39,024


Supreme Court of Minnesota


269 Minn. 343; 130 N.W.2d 623; 1964 Minn. LEXIS 787



September 25, 1964 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Defendant was convicted in the Blue Earth County District Court of having in his possession burglarious tools, and he appealed from an order, Milton D. Mason, Judge, denying his alternative motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict or for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and new trial granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Blue Earth County District Court (Minnesota) that denied his alternative motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict or for a new trial after a jury convicted him of possession of burglars' tools in violation of Minn. Stat. § 621.13.


OVERVIEW: Police responding to a burglar alarm at a drugstore apprehended defendant after he fled from the area of the building. He was carrying a loaded pistol and a two-way radio, and gloves and a flashlight were found nearby. Just before he was caught, he was heard to use the radio to give a warning to another person. Inside the building, damage was discovered to a narcotics vault, and another two-way radio, a punch, a sledge hammer, and a crowbar were found. On appeal, in addition to other issues determined by the court to be without substance, defendant objected to an instruction that told the jury that possession of tools was prima facie evidence of intent and that explained prima facie evidence in terms of a mandatory presumption. The court reversed the order, holding that an instruction as to a presumptions of law that directed a jury to draw an inference was impermissible in a criminal case. Although the circumstantial evidence was sufficient to permit an inference of intent, the instruction improperly required the jury to find in accordance with the presumption. When specific intent was an essential element of an offense, it was never to be presumed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and granted defendant a new trial.

 

609 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Port Authority of St. Paul v. Fisher


No. 39,411


Supreme Court of Minnesota


269 Minn. 276; 132 N.W.2d 183; 1964 Minn. LEXIS 780



September 11, 1964 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Ramsey County District Court for a declaratory judgment brought by the Port Authority of the City of St. Paul, its commissioners, and the American Hoist & Derrick Company against Fred W. Fisher, as commissioner and president of the Authority, to determine the validity of a contract between said Authority and said company and of the bonds to be issued pursuant thereto. The court, Harold W. Schultz, Judge, granted plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment, and defendant appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant President of the Port Authority of the City of St. Paul challenged the decision of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which entered summary judgment in favor of plaintiff company and Commissioners of the authority in a declaratory judgment action for the validity of a contract between the authority and the company.


OVERVIEW: The President refused to execute an agreement that would require the authority to issue bonds to finance the purchase of land and construct an office building to be leased by the company. The President contended that the project agreed to by the Commissioners and the company constituted an unlawful expenditure of public funds for a private purpose. All parties conceded that the land was "marginal land" within the meaning of Minn. Stat. § 458.191(4). The court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the company and the Commissioners for the validity of the agreement because a genuine issue of material fact existed as to whether the project constituted a public purpose under Minn. Stat. §§ 458.191 to 458.1991.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision in favor of the Commissioners and the company against the President, and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

 

610 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Perry


No. 39,099


Supreme Court of Minnesota


269 Minn. 204; 130 N.W.2d 343; 1964 Minn. LEXIS 768



August 28, 1964 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Stewart R. Perry who was convicted in the Hennepin County District Court, Tom Bergin, Judge, of violation of a parking ordinance of the city of Minneapolis.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), convicting him of a violation of a parking ordinance of the Minneapolis, Minn., Code of Ordinances § 411.131(c).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of violating a city ordinance prohibiting parking on a city street for more than two hours between the hours of 8:00 a.m. and 6:00 p.m., unless otherwise designated. On review, he attacked the ordinance by arguing that two other provisions of the ordinance, prohibiting parking on public streets between the hours of 2:00 a.m. and 6:00 a.m., were invalid because there was no valid purpose and that residents living in the city had no other place to park their cars. The court held that it was unnecessary to consider the constitutionality of the other provisions because defendant was not charged with violating them. Section 411.131(c) served the valid public purpose of permitting free passage of vehicles on a public highway. No constitutional violation occurred merely because no signs were posted warning motorists. The public was presumed to know the traffic laws, and the absence of signs was not an impediment to the valid enforcement of the parking ordinance in question.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State ex rel. Cole v. Tahash


No. 39,235


Supreme Court of Minnesota


269 Minn. 1; 129 N.W.2d 903; 1964 Minn. LEXIS 746



July 24, 1964 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Robert Lee Cole from an order of the Washington County District Court, Rollin G. Johnson, Judge, denying his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner appealed an order of the Washington County District Court (Minnesota), which denied the prisoner's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Relator prisoner was arrested and charged with the crime of being an accessory to a robbery. The prisoner was convicted and was sentenced to a term of not less than 10 or more than 80 years in a State reformatory. The prisoner sought a writ of habeas corpus on the basis that he suffered cruel and unusual treatment while incarcerated. The trial court denied the prisoner's petition and the prisoner appealed and claimed that the trial court erred in denying his petition for a writ of habeas corpus without a hearing and without first appointing counsel to assist him or without advising him of his privilege to apply to the state supreme court for appointment of counsel to assist him where it appeared that he was indigent. The court affirmed and held that the allegations in the petition were not sufficient to make a prima facie showing of the kind of cruelty which was enjoined by the Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

 

612 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Chicago, M., S. P. & P. R. Co. v. Chicago G. W. R. Co.


No. 39,010


Supreme Court of Minnesota


268 Minn. 500; 130 N.W.2d 56; 1964 Minn. LEXIS 736



July 17, 1964 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Chicago, Milwaukee, St. Paul and Pacific Railroad Company from an order of the Ramsey County District Court, Clayton Parks, Judge, affirming an order of the Railroad and Warehouse Commission granting a petition by Chicago Great Western Railway Company for joint use of a side track.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant railroad track owner challenged an order of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which affirmed an order of a railroad commission that granted a petition by appellee railroad for joint use of a side track that was owned by appellant and was needed to serve an industrial plant.


OVERVIEW: The industrial plant served by the track at issue was originally served by appellee railroad on a different track. When the plant's business exceeded the capacity of the first track, the plant petitioned the railway commission to require the track owner to build the track at issue and to divide the cost of the track with the plant. When the railroad service available to the plant became inadequate for its requirements, the railroad initiated the instant action to authorize it to jointly use the new track with the track owner to serve the plant. At the hearing the track owner's motion for dismissal on the ground that the commission lacked jurisdiction therein was denied, and the track owner appealed. The court affirmed and held Minn. Stat. § 218.041 provided authority for the commission's order. The court held that the commission's authority to make this prior order was at no time challenged by the track owner. The commission's order did not direct taking of the side track in its entirety without compensation in violation of constitutional guarantees because it did not deprive the track owner of the use of such track but merely directed a joint user thereof with the railroad.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, which had affirmed the railroad commission's grant of the railroad's petition for joint use of the track owner's side track.

 

613 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Anderson v. U. S. Veterans Hospital


No. 39,102


Supreme Court of Minnesota


268 Minn. 213; 128 N.W.2d 710; 1964 Minn. LEXIS 701



May 15, 1964 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the state from an order of the Stearns County District Court, Byron R. Wilson, Judge, discharging Dr. John T. Anderson from the custody of the United States Veterans Hospital.



DISPOSITION: Remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review from an order of the Stearns County District Court (Minnesota), which discharged respondent patient from the custody of the United States Veterans Hospital.


OVERVIEW: A petition for habeas corpus was filed on behalf of the patient, contending that his attorney was not allowed to cross-examine two doctors who assisted at his commitment hearing and that some writings were presented for the first time and the attorney could not take time to examine them adequately. The trial court entered an order which discharged the patient from custody of the superintendent of the United States Veterans Hospital. The court held that the patient failed to establish that the order of commitment was invalid either because of lack of jurisdiction in the probate court or because the statute pursuant to which the probate court acted was unconstitutional and therefore void, or because of failure of the probate court to conform its procedures to the minimal constitutional requirements of due process. The court determined that the rights of the patient could be adequately protected by a petition filed in the court of commitment for restoration to capacity pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 525.78.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the cause with directions to appoint a guardian ad litem, hold a hearing and afford the patient's attorney a full opportunity to present evidence and to cross-examine any witnesses whose testimony was taken to support commitment.

 

614 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Anderson v. Commissioner of Highways


No. 39,028


Supreme Court of Minnesota


267 Minn. 308; 126 N.W.2d 778; 1964 Minn. LEXIS 641; 9 A.L.R.2d 746



February 14, 1964 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition in the Scott County District Court by James Herman Anderson for vacation of an order of the commissioner of highways suspending said petitioner's driver's license. The court, Harold E. Flynn, Judge, denied said petition, and petitioner appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner driver appealed a judgment of the Scott County District Court (Minnesota), which denied the driver's motion to set aside an order of respondent commissioner of highways suspending the driver's license for one year under the authority of Minn. Stat. § 171.18 on the ground that he was a habitual violator of the traffic laws.


OVERVIEW: After the commissioner suspended the driver's license, the driver instituted proceedings in the district court for an order vacating and cancelling the order of suspension. The district court denied the driver's petition and he appealed. The appellate court affirmed. The court held that the term "habitual violator," as used in § 171.18, subd. 4, was not unconstitutionally vague. The court found that the commissioner had a broad, flexible standard and, considering the numerous relative factors to making the decision, there was not an unreasonable delegation of authority to the commissioner. The commissioner properly considered the driver's violations of the drivers' license laws, contained in Minn. Stat. ch. 171, because those laws regulated vehicular traffic and could properly be considered traffic laws within the meaning of Minn. Stat. § 171.18. There was no violation of double jeopardy because the suspension or revocation of a license was not a punishment, but an exercise of the state's police power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order suspending the driver's license for one year.

 

615 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Fabio v. St. Paul


No. 39,020


Supreme Court of Minnesota


267 Minn. 273; 126 N.W.2d 259; 1964 Minn. LEXIS 637



February 7, 1964 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Ramsey County District Court for a declaratory judgment invalidating a statute and to enjoin defendant city and its officials from enforcing it. The court, Edward D. Mulally, Judge, granted defendants' motion for summary judgment, and plaintiff appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff police officer challenged a decision of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) granting a motion for summary judgment filed by defendants, city and others. The police officer sought a declaratory judgment enjoining defendants from enforcing Minn. Stat. § 423.075, which required him to retire from the police department at the age of 65, and declaring § 423.075 unconstitutional as applied to the administrative practices of the city.


OVERVIEW: The issue before the court was whether the police officer's compulsory retirement at age 65 under Minn. Stat. § 423.075 denied his constitutional rights under Minn. Const. art. I, § 2, and art. IV, §§ 33 and 34, and U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The police officer's only claim was that he was accorded unconstitutional treatment under an otherwise valid statute as he was required to retire while others similarly situated had been permitted to remain employed on different payrolls, i.e. administrative, police and fire alarm, parks, and playgrounds payrolls. He argued that the classification by payroll was arbitrary and unreasonable. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment and held that a valid classification did not depend on ironclad uniformity. The fact that measures taken were not directed at all of the evils to be corrected did not invalidate the application of the statute as the state was dealing with the problem of officers retiring from hazardous duty at age 65 according to practical exigencies and experience in a manner that was germane to its solution. There was no evidence in the record that the police officer was qualified for any available nonhazardous duty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the police officer's action against the city and others.

 

616 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Arcadia Development Corp. v. Bloomington


No. 39,001


Supreme Court of Minnesota


267 Minn. 221; 125 N.W.2d 846; 1964 Minn. LEXIS 630



January 17, 1964 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Hennepin County District Court to compel the city of Bloomington and the superintendent of its building department to issue a permit for the erection of a sign. After findings for plaintiff, John A. Weeks, Judge, defendants appealed from an order directing that the permit be issued.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city sought review of the decision of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which entered an order directing the city to issue a permit to plaintiff developer so that it could erect a sign.


OVERVIEW: The developer sought to place a sign at the entrance of its mobile home park. The permit that had been issued for the mobile home park was a variance from the terms of the zoning ordinance. The developer applied for a permit to erect the sign, and the city refused to issue the permit under City of Bloomington Minn. Ordinance § 10.03(C). Several appeals followed and new ordinances were proposed in order to allow the developer to erect the sign. The city still voted to deny the developer's application. The trial court determining that the city's action in denying the permit was arbitrary, capricious, and in violation of the developer's rights and ordered the permit issued. The court determined that the city had the authority to regulate the use, size, and position of business signs. However, the court reasoned that the regulations must bear a reasonable relation to the purpose that they were meant for. The court held that it would not overrule the trial court's finding that the city's denial of the sign did not reasonably relate to the purposes of the ordinances. The court stated that the city's denial was based solely on a violation of the ordinance and that was unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision that ordered the city to issue the developer its permit.

 

617 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Youngstown Mines Corp. v. Prout


No. 38,615


Supreme Court of Minnesota


266 Minn. 450; 124 N.W.2d 328; 1963 Minn. LEXIS 753



October 18, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari in the Ramsey County District Court, to the state auditor and the commissioner of conservation, upon the relation of The Youngstown Mines Corporation to review a decision of the commissioner denying its claim for refund of rentals paid the state under a mining lease. The commissioner appealed from the court's order, John W. Graff, Judge, quashing the writ as to the state auditor but finding that Youngstown was entitled to the refund and remanding the claim to the commissioner.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Commissioner of Conservation, sought review of the decision of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which, reviewing the decision of the commissioner denying a claim for refunds of rentals to the state under a mining lease, quashed a writ of certiorari as to the state auditor but remanded the claim to the commissioner with instructions to refund the rentals to plaintiff mining company.


OVERVIEW: In 1924, the mining company entered into a 50-year lease with the state to mine iron ore in a lake bed. Starting in 1943, litigation continued for 15 years. In 1958, pursuant to a final judgment, the mining company submitted a claim to the commissioner of conservation for a refund of royalties under a mineral lease after the action determined that the state had no title to the land. The commissioner denied the claim. The mining company petitioned, and the trial court issued a writ of certiorari against the commissioner and the state auditor to review the claim. The state filed a motion for summary judgment. The trial court quashed the writ as to the auditor, but the trial court vacated the commissioner's disapproval of the claim and remanded the claim to the commissioner. The commissioner appealed. The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, ordering the refund. The court determined that the state did not own the mineral rights, that the lease provided for refunds if the state were determined not to own the rights, and that title to the property was not finally determined until 1958, so laches and other theories did not preclude recovery by the mining company.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court. The court remanded the complaint to the commissioner with instructions to refund rentals from the mining lease to the mining company. The court determined that the state did not own the rights, the lease required refunds if the state were determined not to own the rights, and that laches and other theories did not preclude the mining company from recovery of the refund.

 

618 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kuluvar


No. 38,903


Supreme Court of Minnesota


266 Minn. 408; 123 N.W.2d 699; 1963 Minn. LEXIS 749



October 4, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by H. L. Kuluvar from a judgment of the Koochiching County District Court, Paul A. Lundgren, Judge, whereby he was convicted of interference with public waters.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and new trial ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction in the Koochiching County District Court (Minnesota), for interfering with public waters in violation of Minn. Stat. § 105.42.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a partner in the operation of a resort that owned certain lakefront property. Pursuant to a treaty, the lake waters were international boundary waters. Under a federal permit, defendant dug a channel adjacent to the boundary of resort property to provide a flotation way for watercraft. Later, he dredged the channel without a permit and was prosecuted under § 105.42 for interfering with public waters. Upon his conviction, he was fined and sentence to jail. He paid the fine. On review, the court reversed and remanded for a new trial, holding, inter alia, that the State of Minnesota had jurisdiction to proceed against defendant because the treaty did not expressly excluded state jurisdiction and there was no showing that the state regulatory measures conflicted with the exercise of power vested in a joint international commission by the treaty. Also, § 105.42 was not unconstitutional vague and did not unconstitutionally interfere with the property rights of riparian owners. However, the evidence was insufficient to convict defendant because there was no showing that defendant's acts resulted in a detriment to the public in its use of the waters.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for interfering with public waters and remanded for a new trial.

 

619 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


In re Trust of Gardner


No. 38,878


Supreme Court of Minnesota


266 Minn. 127; 123 N.W.2d 69; 1963 Minn. LEXIS 717



July 19, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Proceeding brought by First Trust Company of St. Paul and McNeil V. Seymour, trustees, in the Ramsey County District Court for the allowance of their accounts in the matter of the trust for George H. Gardner under the last will and testament of Claribel H. Gardner, deceased, in which proceeding objections were filed by said George H. Gardner, life beneficiary, and on behalf of John Gardner, a remainderman, by his guardian ad litem, Francis D. Butler. The life beneficiary appealed from an order, Ronald E. Hachey, Judge, determining that certain dividends should be allocated to interest and others to principal.



DISPOSITION: Reversed as to capital gain dividends allocated to principal; otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant life beneficiary challenged the decision of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which entered a judgment in favor of respondent trustees determining that certain dividends should have been allocated to interest and others paid to principal.


OVERVIEW: Decedent died leaving a last will and testament and a codicil under which the testamentary trust at issue became operative. Neither the will nor codicil contained any provisions directing the manner in which stock dividend shares or capital gains from investment trusts should have been allocated between principal and interest beneficiaries. The trial court held that all stock dividends, with the exception of 10 shares of an oil corporation, should have been allocated to principal with the aforementioned 10 shares allocated to income. The life beneficiary challenged the trial court's assignment of dividends to the principal. The court held that application of Minn. Stat. § 501.47 retroactively to a trust created prior to its enactment was not violative of the constitutional rights of income beneficiaries of such trust. The court concluded that where capital dividends were distributed by a regulated investment company and received by the trustee at his option either in cash or in shares of the investment fund, such capital gain dividends constituted income and were to be distributed to the income beneficiary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the portion of the trial court's judgment that directed that stock dividends received from corporations whose stock was held by the trustees be allocated to the principal. The court reversed the portion of the trial court's order that directed capital gain dividends receivable in cash or stock from regulated investment companies be allocated to the principal.

 

620 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Oman


No. 38,716


Supreme Court of Minnesota


265 Minn. 277; 121 N.W.2d 616; 1963 Minn. LEXIS 663



April 26, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Arvid Oman from a judgment of the Waseca County District Court, John F. Cahill, Judge, whereby he was convicted of selling and possessing obscene or indecent literature.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Waseca County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of selling and possessing obscene or indecent literature in violation of Minn. Stat. § 617.24 (1957).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with unlawfully selling and having in his possession with intent to sell certain obscene or indecent magazines, pamphlets, or story papers in violation of § 617.24. The information did not charge defendant with having committed the acts prohibited with knowledge of the obscene character of the materials involved. The court reversed the trial court's judgment. The court determined that the information did not state a public offense because the element of scienter was a necessary part of the offense. The court explained that an information could have charged the commission of the statutory offense in the language of the statute without greater particularity when by that means all that was essential to constitute the offense was stated fully and directly. The court noted that the statute did not set forth all of the elements necessary to constitute the offense intended to be punished, so the information, which simply followed the words of the statute, was not sufficient. The court concluded that the information had to go further and allege with certainty all of the particular facts necessary to bring the case within the intent and meaning of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the district court, which convicted defendant of selling and possessing obscene or indecent literature. The court remanded the case with leave to amend the information so as properly to allege the offense.

 

621 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Zieman v. Zieman


No. 38,636


Supreme Court of Minnesota


265 Minn. 190; 121 N.W.2d 77; 1963 Minn. LEXIS 649



April 5, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by defendant from an order and judgment of the Ramsey County District Court, Albin S. Pearson, Judge, whereby he was adjudged to be in contempt of court for failure to make payments required by a prior divorce decree.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant former husband appealed from an order and judgment of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which held him in contempt of court for failure to make payments required by a prior divorce decree, which dissolved the marriage of the husband and plaintiff former wife.


OVERVIEW: The judgment awarded the wife accrued alimony, support payments, and attorney's fees based on the divorce decree, which gave the wife custody of the parties' child, ordered child support, and ordered monthly alimony and attorney fees. In addition, the judgment declared the husband to be in contempt for failure to make the payments when due and sentenced him to 60 days in the county jail with execution stayed for 15 days to give him an opportunity to purge himself of contempt by making payments to the wife. The husband failed to make the payments. The court first held that, in so far as the judgment incorporated the delinquent child support, reversal was compelled because the district court did not have jurisdiction to enforce by contempt proceedings the payment of delinquent support money because the child had reached majority. Furthermore, apart from the overdue child support, the record failed to sustain an essential finding to the effect that the husband was able to make the payments required by the judgment. Such a finding was necessary before the husband could be found in contempt. Therefore, the judgment was reversed, and the matter remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's judgment and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

Sabes v. Minneapolis


No. 39,000


Supreme Court of Minnesota


265 Minn. 166; 120 N.W.2d 871; 1963 Minn. LEXIS 646



March 22, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Proceeding by Henry Sabes in the Hennepin County District Court to enjoin the city of Minneapolis and its council, superintendent of police, and license inspector from revocation of certain licenses held by said plaintiff. After findings for defendants, William D. Gunn, Judge, plaintiff appealed from an order denying his motion for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a licensee, sought review of the judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which denied his motion for amended findings or a new trial in an action he filed against defendants, a city, that sought an injunction against the revocation of various licenses for a restaurant and bar.


OVERVIEW: The licensee had been a long-time owner of a restaurant and bar. Neither he nor his employees had ever been convicted of any offense that arose from its operation. Each year the city issued an on-sale liquor license, as well as licenses for nonintoxicating beverages, food, cigarettes, and for the operation of a dance hall and a tavern. A council committee recommended to the city council that all of the licenses for the operation of the premises be revoked, and the city council adopted the recommendation. The licensee filed his action that sought an injunction against the revocation. The court held that: (1) the notice was wholly inadequate but that the licensee was not materially prejudiced by the insufficiency of the notice he received; (2) written reports of members of a city police morals squad that recited their personal observations and experiences were admissible; and (3) the licensee was charged with knowledge of such activities and further proof was not required to sustain the revocation where evidence disclosed that the licensee knew prostitutes were frequenting his establishment and numerous convictions resulted from acts of prostitution solicited on his premises.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court.

Lowe v. Patterson


No. 38,740


Supreme Court of Minnesota


265 Minn. 42; 120 N.W.2d 313; 1963 Minn. LEXIS 628



February 21, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Dakota County District Court for partition of certain real estate by sale thereof, which action was brought by Mary Katherine Lowe, formerly Mary K. Mills, against the owner of the other undivided half, Helen A. Patterson, formerly Helen A. Kleis, and against Hastings National Bank of Hastings, owner of a mortgage on the property. The court, R.C. Nelsen, Judge, confirmed the sale of said property, and defendant Patterson appealed from said order and from other orders denying her motions to vacate the confirmation and for other relief.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant co-owner sought review of orders of the Dakota County District Court (Minnesota), which confirmed the sale of the property to be partitioned and denied her motions to vacate the confirmation and for other relief in respondent co-owner's action for partition.


OVERVIEW: Respondent sought to partition the premises by sale and requested that appellant's interest be charged with the reasonable value of rental arising out of her exclusive occupancy of the property. Appellant requested partition by sale and sought to have the proceeds divided according to the parties' interests. Appellant filed a notice discharging her attorney. The referee sold the property, and appellant's substituted counsel objected to the order to show cause why the sale should not be consummated. The trial court confirmed the sale and denied appellant's request to vacate the order. In affirming, the court held that (1) appellant showed no prejudice affecting the merits of the case because of the trial court's refusal to order the discharge of her attorney; (2) appellant's husband, who had an inchoate interest at most, was not an indispensable party to the action; (3) appellant's counsel had implied authority to stipulate that a partition sale could proceed and appellant ratified the procedure; and (4) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in failing to vacate the stipulation. The court declined to determine the validity of Minn. Stat. § 558.17.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders, which confirmed the sale of the property to be partitioned and denied appellant's various motions to set aside the proceedings.

 

624 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dietz


Nos. 38,754, 38,755


Supreme Court of Minnesota


264 Minn. 551; 119 N.W.2d 833; 1963 Minn. LEXIS 623



February 15, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Defendants, Donald Dietz and John A. Kotek, were charged in the Rice County District Court with grand larceny in the second degree. They demurred to the informations, and the court, John F. Cahill, Judge, certified certain questions as important and doubtful.



DISPOSITION: Questions answered in the negative.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, charged in the Rice County District Court (Minnesota) with grand larceny in the second degree, demurred to the informations based on a claim that Minn. Stat. § 622.06, which defined grand larceny in the second degree, was unconstitutional under Minn. Const. art. 1, § 5, or U.S. Const. amends. V or XIV, § 1. Pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 632.10, the district court certified the resulting questions to the court as "important" or "doubtful."


OVERVIEW: Defendants claimed that Minn. Stat. § 622.06 was unconstitutional because it imposed cruel and unusual punishment contrary to Minn. Const. art. 1, § 5; deprived them of life, liberty, and property without due process of law, contrary to U.S. Const. amends. V and XIV; and was so uncertain of meaning that it could not be reasonably understood by a person of ordinary intelligence. The court answered the three questions certified to it under § 632.10 in the negative. The court rejected the cruel and unusual punishment claim. Even though an amendment to § 622.06 had created an anomaly under which penalties for more serious thefts were actually less onerous than those imposed for thefts of lesser magnitude, the anomaly might work to defendants' advantage but, in any event, the statutory penalty was not unconstitutional. Nor were defendants deprived of equal protection because the legislature was entitled to classify crimes and prescribe punishment based on the value of the stolen property. Finally, the court found no merit to defendants' claim that the statute was unclear; the anomaly did not affect its clarity, only the relationship between offenses and penalties.


OUTCOME: The court held that the larceny statute did not violate state or federal proscriptions against cruel or unusual punishment, that the statute did not violate defendants' equal protection rights, and that the statute was not void for vagueness.

 

625 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Oak Center Creamery Co. v. Grobe


No. 38,837


Supreme Court of Minnesota


264 Minn. 435; 119 N.W.2d 729; 1963 Minn. LEXIS 610



January 18, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Elwood B. Grobe and Arlene M. Grobe from a judgment of the Wabasha County District Court, Leo F. Murphy, Judge, decreeing an easement against their property in favor of Oak Center Creamery Company.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners challenged the judgment from the Wabasha County District Court (Minnesota) which decreed an easement against their property in favor of respondent creamery company. The appeal also constituted a direct attack upon the constitutionality of Minn. Stat. § 308.39, which gave creamery associations the right to acquire easements for sewers and sites for filtration plants.


OVERVIEW: Landowners contended that the taking of an easement on their land by a creamery association constituted a taking of private property for private purposes and violated Minn. Const. art. 1, § 13, and that it constituted a denial to them of due process of law in violation of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1.While conceding that they did not serve notice of appeal on the attorney general, the landowners contended that condemnation actions were "special proceedings" to which the Rules of Civil Procedure did not apply by reason of Minn. R. Civ. P. 81.01 and Appendix A. On appeal, the court did not find any such inconsistencies or conflicts. The court held that while the eminent domain proceeding in the case may have had the aspect of "special proceedings" at the outset, nevertheless, even though no appeal was taken from the viewers' award, the appeal from the judgment entered pursuant thereto became adversary and judicial in nature, making the Rules of Civil Procedure applicable. Therefore, because the appeal directly challenged the constitutionality of Minn. St. 308.39 and notice of the appeal was not served upon the attorney general, the appeal had to be dismissed for want of jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The landowners' appeal was dismissed.

Pearce v. Edina


No. 38,464


Supreme Court of Minnesota


263 Minn. 553; 118 N.W.2d 659; 1962 Minn. LEXIS 813



October 5, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Hennepin County District Court by Katherine Elizabeth Pearce and Marie Elizabeth Pearce for a declaratory judgment and injunctive relief on the ground that a zoning ordinance of defendant village is unconstitutional. After findings for plaintiffs, John A. Weeks, Judge, defendant appealed from the judgments entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed judgments of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) entered in favor of plaintiff landowners in a declaratory judgment action challenging certain zoning ordinances affecting the landowners' property.


OVERVIEW: The landowners petitioned the city to have their property rezoned to permit retail uses. The city denied the petitions. The properties were surrounded by property zoned for commercial uses. The trial court found that the city's zoning ordinances were arbitrary, discriminatory, confiscatory, and unreasonable as applied to the landowners and ordered the city to rezone the property. The city rezoned one property to allow office buildings, but refused to rezone the other property. The trial court determined that the city did not comply with its initial decision. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgments. The court discussed the standards of review applied to appeals from decisions invalidating zoning ordinances. The court held; (1) the new zoning ordinance had no valid relationship to issues of public welfare, health, or safety; (2) the zoning ordinances as they related to landowner's property rendered it practically valueless; and (3) the city's actions in denying the landowners the right to use their property in the same manner permitted for other properties in the area constituted a complete and willful disregard of the trial court's initial decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of the district court entered in favor of the landowners. The court remanded the cause with directions that the district court insure that the city comply with its judgments.

Haaland v. Pomush


No. 38,339


Supreme Court of Minnesota


263 Minn. 506; 117 N.W.2d 194; 1962 Minn. LEXIS 809; 45 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P50,626



September 14, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari in the Hubbard County District Court upon the relation of Paul Haaland and L. Patricia Haaland, copartners; Cecil Thompson and Carol Thompson, copartners; and Jack Clifford to review an order of the Industrial Commission determining the minimum wage for women and minor workers in the public housekeeping industry. The case was heard before Arnold C. Forbes, Judge, who ordered the minimum wage order vacated, and respondents, James Pomush, William T. Holzinger, and Lewis Intihar, commissioners of the Industrial Commission, appealed from the order of the district court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Minnesota Commissioners of the Industrial Commission, sought review of a decision of the Hubbard County District Court (Minnesota), which invalidated application of a Commission minimum wage order for women and minor workers in the public housekeeping industry to a business operated by appellee partners.


OVERVIEW: Under Minn. Stat. § 177.08, the Commission initiated proceedings by the appointment of an advisory board to recommend an increase in minimum wages. On review, the court reversed the district court's order vacating the Commission's minimum wage order. The court found that the decision of the Industrial Commission was amply supported by the evidence and that it engaged in a reasonable exercise of judgment. The court held that the Commissioner did not abuse their discretion in leaving such employees under the same minimum wage order governing workers whose duties were connected with the principal purpose of such retail and drug businesses.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's order.

 

629 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


In re Warner's Trust


No. 38,267.


Supreme Court of Minnesota


263 Minn. 449; 117 N.W.2d 224; 1962 Minn. LEXIS 805



September 7, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Harold L. Warner, objector, from a decree of the Hennepin County District Court, Leslie L. Anderson, Judge, allowing certain accounts upon the petition of H. David Warner, trustee of a trust created by Katherine B. Warner by instrument dated December 7, 1929. Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the objector to the allowance of certain accounts made by respondent trustee, sought review of the decision by the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which allowed certain accounts upon the trustee's petition. The trustee was the trustee of a trust created by the settlor.


OVERVIEW: At issue was whether the trial court correctly held that the trustee could deduct from gross receipts a reasonable amount annually as depreciation of the property of the trust in determining net income. The settlor created an inter vivos trust in which her husband and a holding company were trustees. They were later divorced, and the children sought to remove the husband as trustee. The trustee son was appointed successor trustee, and he took a depreciation deduction of the cost value of property, both for income tax purposes and trust purposes, in determining net income available for distribution. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision in favor of the trustee. The court adopted the rule that, where depreciable buildings were acquired with trust funds after creation of the trust, the trustee could deduct from the gross receipts as an expense item an amount equal to the reasonable estimated depreciation of the cost value of the property. The settlor intended the corpus of the trust to remain intact for income beneficiaries and the ultimate remaindermen. If the buildings in question were depreciable, the only way to accomplish that intent was to permit the deduction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision allowing the accounts upon the trustee's petition.

 

630 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ritholz


No. 38,405


Supreme Court of Minnesota


263 Minn. 36; 115 N.W.2d 743; 1962 Minn. LEXIS 749



June 8, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Winona County District Court to enjoin Benjamin D. Ritholz, M. I. Ritholz, S. J. Ritholz, Fannie Ritholz, Sylvia Ritholz, Sophie Ritholz, Jacob Bendo, Anna Bendo, and King Optical Company, a partnership, from solicitation by "price advertisements" in connection with their business of selling and dispensing eyeglasses. After findings for plaintiff, Leo F. Murphy, Judge, defendants appealed from an order denying their motion for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions to enter judgment for defendants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant opticians appealed a judgment from the Winona County District Court (Minnesota), which found for plaintiff State and enjoined the opticians from "price advertising" in connection with their business of selling and dispensing eyeglasses.


OVERVIEW: The opticians were in the business of selling and dispensing eyeglasses. They hired an optometrist to refract their customers eyes. They utilized price advertising in connection with the business. In reversing the judgment the court held that Minn. Stat. § 148.57, subd. 3, which prohibited an optometrist from price advertising, did not apply to opticians. The court noted that Minn. Stat. § 148.56 effectively exempted the price advertising prohibition from sales upon prescription from persons legally authorized by the laws of Minnesota to examine eyes and prescribe glasses therefor. This was precisely what the opticians were doing. The court moreover noted that by its terms Minn. Stat. § 148.57, subd. 3, applied only to optometrists. The court further observed that this practice was prohibited merely because it was deemed unprofessional when engaged in by optometrists. The court also held that it was not for it to say whether this practice by opticians should be condemned.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that enjoined the opticians from price advertising.

 

631 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. La Rose v. Tahash


No. 38,402


Supreme Court of Minnesota


262 Minn. 552; 115 N.W.2d 687; 1962 Minn. LEXIS 741



May 25, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Miles La Rose from an order of the Washington County District Court, Carl W. Gustafson, Judge, denying his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator inmate appealed an order of the Washington County District Court (Minnesota), which denied his petition seeking a writ of habeas corpus. The inmate contended that he was unlawfully imprisoned in the state prison under an invalid judgment of conviction.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was serving a sentence of up to 10 years in prison for violating Minn. Stat. § 168.49. The trial court increased defendant's sentence based upon his prior felony convictions pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 610.29. The inmate filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus, and the district court denied the petition. On appeal, the inmate asserted that the statute under which he was convicted was invalid because the state legislature had not redistricted the state as a basis for legislative representation as required by Minn. Const. art. IV, §§ 2, 23, and 24. The court held that a mere change in relative population and the consequent inequality of representation did not render a law enacted by the legislature void and did not make it necessary to set aside criminal convictions under such laws. The court affirmed the judgment denying the writ of habeas corpus. The court noted that the inmate could have received a life sentence based upon his three prior felony convictions pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 610.29. The court held that there was nothing in the record to establish that either the proceedings, the judgment of conviction, or the sentence imposed were invalid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's denial of the petition for writ of habeas corpus.
