State v. McCorvey


No. 38,379


Supreme Court of Minnesota


262 Minn. 361; 114 N.W.2d 703; 1962 Minn. LEXIS 719



April 19, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Defendant was convicted in the municipal court of Minneapolis, Hennepin County, Lindsay G. Arthur, Judge, on a charge of vagrancy, and she appealed from an order denying her motion for a new trial and from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and new trial granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of vagrancy, a violation of Minn. Stat. § 614.57 in the municipal court of Minneapolis, Hennepin County (Minnesota) and sought review of the trial court's denial of her motion for a new trial. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in permitting certain testimony of the arresting officers and that § 614.57 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The trial court permitted three police officers to testify at defendant's vagrancy trial that they had discussed defendant's reputation and character with numerous people in the community and that it was commonly understood that defendant was a prostitute. Defendant argued that she never put her character in issue and objected repeatedly to the testimony. The court reversed the conviction and held that it was error to admit the officers' testimony. The court also held that the vagrancy statute, Minn. Stat. § 614.57 was not unconstitutional and that the court must presume that the statute was constitutional. The court further held that the statute was not invalid for lack of definiteness and certainty or for failure to state an offense, because a person of common intelligence could determine its meaning with reasonable certainty.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and ordered a new trial.

 

633 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. Rolfe


Nos. 38,350, 38,351, 38,361


Supreme Court of Minnesota


262 Minn. 284; 114 N.W.2d 671; 1962 Minn. LEXIS 709



April 6, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action brought by Robert Williams in the Cass County District Court for a declaratory judgment declaring unconstitutional L. 1957, c. 730, establishing the Board of Education of the Unorganized Territory of Cass County, and to enjoin Gertrude Rolfe, superintendent of schools of said county, from proceeding with the consolidation of said unorganized territory with other school districts. The school boards of the unorganized territory and of Independent School District No. 115 were permitted to intervene. Plaintiff appealed (No. 38,350) from an order, John T. Galarneault, Judge, declaring the statute unconstitutional but refusing to invalidate acts already performed thereunder and certifying the questions presented to be important and doubtful. This appeal was consolidated with an appeal (No. 38,351) by Russell Lego, Robert Williams, and Art Combs from another order by said judge denying their motion for summary judgment in appeals they had taken from certain orders of said county superintendent. In these appeals in the district court, Bernadine Kirt and others had been permitted to intervene, and they joined the Board of Education of the Unorganized Territory with the above-named [***2] defendant in an appeal (No. 38,361) from the same orders, which was also consolidated with the others for hearing.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff individuals and defendant superintendent of schools sought review of a judgment by the Cass County District Court (Minnesota), which declared 1957 Minn. Laws 730, establishing the Board of Education of the Unorganized Territory of Cass County, unconstitutional, but refused to invalidate acts already performed thereunder by the superintendent.


OVERVIEW: The superintendent sought to consolidate a part of the unorganized county with existing school districts. The individuals sought a restraining order to prevent the superintendent from issuing that order. The order was initially granted by the trial court, which the court reversed. The individuals then filed a supplemental complaint seeking to have 1957 Minn. Laws 730 declared unconstitutional. The trial court held that 1957 Minn. Laws 730 was unconstitutional but that acts performed by the Board under 1957 Minn. Laws 730 prior to its determination of unconstitutionality were valid. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's decision. The court held the fact that the Act applied to only one county was not enough to invalidate it if there were other reasonable grounds for placing that county in a class by itself. The court found that the act was necessary for the county because the population was not dense enough to warrant the formation of a school district. The court recognized that unique problems were involved in the management of schools in unorganized territory in counties having large areas and that the classification caused by the act was therefore justified.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

 

634 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Plunkett v. First Nat'l Bank


No. 38,235


Supreme Court of Minnesota


262 Minn. 231; 115 N.W.2d 235; 1962 Minn. LEXIS 703



March 30, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari upon the relation of First National Bank of Austin to review two orders of the Department of Commerce, one granting an application by Warren F. Plunkett, A. S. Lund, Albert M. Skinner, B. A. Miller, and Minnesota Trust Company of Albert Lea to change the name and place of business of said company; and one denying relator's petition for a rehearing.



DISPOSITION: Writ quashed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent trust company moved to quash a writ of certiorari granted to review two orders of the Department of Commerce (Minnesota), which granted the trust company's application to move and change its name and which denied relator bank's petition for a rehearing.


OVERVIEW: In anticipation of a relocation, the trust company applied to move its place of business and to change its name. After the Department's order authorized the move and the name change, the bank moved for a rehearing. When the Department denied the rehearing, the bank sought the writ of certiorari, and the trust company moved to quash the writ. Quashing the writ. the court noted that the proceedings were barred by a statute of limitations under Minn. Stat. § 606.01, governing reviews by certiorari. The courts no longer had jurisdiction to determine the validity of the orders. The orders were consented to by the Commissioner of Banks. The trust company could change its name and move its place of business as a trust company. There was no statutory provision for judicial review for the orders. There were no statutory provisions for rehearings in matters determined by the Department or the Commissioner. Any judicial review had to be sought under § 606.01. The writ was issued long after the expiration of 60 days after the bank had received notice of the orders.


OUTCOME: The court granted the trust company's motion to quash the writ of certiorari.

 

635 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Brooks v. International Brotherhood of Boilermakers


No. 38,372


Supreme Court of Minnesota


262 Minn. 253; 114 N.W.2d 647; 1962 Minn. LEXIS 705



March 30, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Hennepin County District Court wherein plaintiff sought an injunction requiring the International Brotherhood of Boilermakers, Iron Ship Builders, Blacksmiths, Forgers & Helpers, AFL-CIO, its officers, Local No. 647, and its officers to reinstate him to membership and also damages for his alleged wrongful expulsion. The International Brotherhood appeared specially to have the action dismissed or service of the summons quashed, which motion was denied, D. E. LaBelle, Judge, and said defendant appealed from the order.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action brought by plaintiff union member against defendants, a local union, its parent union, and their officers, seeking reinstatement into membership and damages for his wrongful expulsion, the parent union appealed from an order of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which denied its motion to dismiss the action or in lieu thereof to quash service of the summons upon the parent union.


OVERVIEW: The member filed suit against defendants, alleging that he was wrongfully expelled from the local union, which was located in Minnesota, by a vote of its membership. The parent union, which was based in Kansas, sought to quash the substituted service of process upon it pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 540.152, contending that it performed no acts in Minnesota resulting in any damage or giving rise to any cause of action. The trial court, finding that the parent union had almost complete control over the activities of the local union, denied the motion to quash. On appeal, the court held that the parent union was subject to substituted service of process because: (1) the parent union had a very important control over the local union and its activities within the state; (2) the members of the local union were also members of the parent union, and, thus, the local union's expulsion of the member was on behalf of the parent union; (3) § 540.152 as so construed was constitutional because the parent union had a great number of contacts with the state; and (4) jurisdiction could be constitutionally based upon the actions of the members of the local union as agents for the parent union.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying the parent union's motion to quash.

 

636 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Grobe v. Oak Center Creamery Co.


No. 38,245


Supreme Court of Minnesota


262 Minn. 60; 113 N.W.2d 458; 1962 Minn. LEXIS 681



February 9, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari upon the relation of Elwood B. Grobe and Arlene M. Grobe to review an order of the Wabasha County District Court, Leo F. Murphy, Judge, which granted a petition of Oak Center Creamery Company to take an easement across their land in an eminent domain proceeding.



DISPOSITION: Writ discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relators landowners sought review by way of certiorari of the order of the Wabasha County District Court (Minnesota) that granted respondent creamery company's petition to take an easement across their land in an eminent domain proceeding. The landowners argued that Minn. Stat. § 308.39 was unconstitutional on its face in that it authorized the taking of private property for private use.


OVERVIEW: The creamery company, pursuant to § 308.39, sought an easement across the landowner's property for the construction and operation of a sewer drain for disposal of waste from the company. The landowners argued that the statute was unconstitutional on its face and the court did not need the settled case or certificate of the trial court as to the accuracy and completeness of the record to decide the issue. The court declined to decide on the constitutionality of the statute and held that it could not find that the statute was inherently unconstitutional. The court held that every statute must be presumed valid and that judicial restraint demanded a deference to the will of the legislature which required that the court assume it intended the power granted by the statute should be exercised for a public purpose within the framework of the constitution. Further, the court held that if the statute was valid as applied to one set of facts and invalid in another, it could not make that determination without the factual background of the case which was lacking since the settled case or certificate as to the completeness of the record was not supplied.


OUTCOME: The court declined to determine the issue of the constitutionality of the statute.

 

637 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Christopherson v. Tahash


No. 38,336


Supreme Court of Minnesota


261 Minn. 233; 111 N.W.2d 404; 1961 Minn. LEXIS 632



October 27, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Jerry Adlof Christopherson from an order of the Washington County District Court, Leonard Keyes, Judge, denying his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed an order of the District Court of Washington County (Minnesota), which denied his petition for a writ of habeas corpus after a conviction for third degree burglary. Petitioner contended that his arraignment under Minn. Stat. § 610.31 on an information which charged him with prior felonies constituted double jeopardy because the trial court failed to impose an increased sentence upon his conviction.


OVERVIEW: On February 5, 1958 petitioner was convicted for third degree burglary. On June 23, 1958 petitioner was arraigned under Minn. Stat. § 610.31 on an information which charged him with having been convicted of felonies prior to his burglary conviction. Petitioner subsequently filed a writ of habeas corpus which was denied by the trial court. Petitioner appealed and contended that the § 610.31 proceedings constituted double jeopardy because the prior convictions had been made to the trial court at the time of the original sentence and no increased sentence was then imposed. The court affirmed and held that the statute required that a separate information had to be filed and a hearing held before an increased sentence could be imposed. The court also rejected petitioner's argument that he was denied assistance of counsel at the arraignment. The court held that there was no constitutional requirement that petitioner be represented by counsel on arraignment where he pleaded not guilty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

638 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Lambach v. Northwestern Refining Co.


Nos. 38,116, 38,117


Supreme Court of Minnesota


261 Minn. 115; 111 N.W.2d 345; 1961 Minn. LEXIS 622



October 6, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two actions in the Ramsey County District Court arising out of a collision involving a truck maintained by Northwestern Refining Company, Inc., and driven by Vernon Scheid; an automobile owned and operated by Richard S. Lambach; and an automobile driven by Gerald E. Fitzgerald. One action was brought by Gloria A. Lambach as trustee for the heirs of Richard Lambach, who died as a result of the accident, against Northwestern Refining Company and Scheid. The other action was brought by Fitzgerald for his personal injuries and property damage against Gloria A. Lambach, administratrix of the estate of Richard Lambach; Scheid; and Northwestern Refining Company. The cases were tried together before James C. Otis, Judge, and a jury, which found that defendant Scheid was guilty of negligence which was a proximate cause of the accident; that Lambach was not guilty of negligence which was a proximate cause of the accident; that plaintiffs were entitled to damages of $ 25,000 and $ 30,000 respectively. Defendants Scheid and Northwestern Refining Company appealed from an order in each case denying their alternative motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict or for a new trial.



DISPOSITION:  [***2] Reversed and new trial granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, an owner and a driver, appealed a judgment of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which denied their alternative motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict or for a new trial. Plaintiffs, an administratrix and a claimant, recovered for personal injuries resulting from a car wreck.


OVERVIEW: The administrator's decedent, the claimant, the driver, and another vehicle were involved in a car crash. The driver and the owner were found liable in actions by the administrator and the claimant. The claimant also sued the administrator, who prevailed in the claimant's action against the decedent's estate. On review, the court reversed and remanded for a new trial. The court ruled that the two theories of the administrator and the claimant could not be reconciled. The administrator claimed that the driver's truck forced the decedent across the yellow line into the path of the claimant's car. The claimant claimed that the driver's truck climbed the rear of the decedent's car, causing it to spin across the yellow lines. The driver and the owner claimed that the decedent pulled across the yellow line to pass the truck, and that the collision forced the decedent's car into the truck. The court concluded that the administrator's theory was not proven by a preponderance of the evidence. The court determined that the fact that the claimant and the decedent hit head on in the claimant's lane was prima facie evidence of the decedent's negligence.


OUTCOME: The court ruled in favor of the owner and driver, reversed the judgment, and remanded the case for a new trial.

 

639 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Oman


No. 38,383


Supreme Court of Minnesota


261 Minn. 10; 110 N.W.2d 514; 1961 Minn. LEXIS 610



September 1, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Defendant was charged in the Waseca County District Court with violation of the statute prohibiting the sale and possession of indecent literature and he demurred to the information. The court, John F. Cahill, Judge, overruled the demurrer and certified questions of law arising to be important or doubtful.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in the Waseca County District Court (Minnesota) with unlawfully selling and having in his possession with intent to sell obscene or indecent magazines, pamphlets, or story papers containing pictures and photographs in violation of Minn. Stat. § 617.24 (later repealed by 1961 Minn. Laws 664). The trial judge overruled defendant's demurrer to the information and certified questions of law arising to be important or doubtful.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the terms "obscene" and "indecent" in the information were so vague and indefinite that they failed to comply with the requirements for terminology in criminal informations. On appeal, the court construed the statutory language such that the definition of the crime was instinct with the idea of scienter. A reading of § 617.24 as a whole clearly indicated that only those who were in some manner aware of the character of the material they attempted to distribute should be punished. It was not innocent but calculated purveyance of filth that was exorcised. Further, no statute should be declared unconstitutional if by any reasonable construction it could be given a meaning in harmony with the fundamental law. The court also held that the words "obscene or indecent" as used in § 617.24 were not unconstitutionally indefinite in violation of the federal and state constitutions. The new statute, 1961 Minn. Laws 664, although not retroactive, was indicative of the legislature's intent in enacting § 617.24. The court rejected defendant's argument that § 617.24 was ambiguous. Section 617.24 could be construed as not imposing strict criminal liability upon an accused.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

640 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State by Lord v. Pearson


No. 38,072


Supreme Court of Minnesota


260 Minn. 477; 110 N.W.2d 206; 1961 Minn. LEXIS 598



July 28, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Condemnation proceeding in the Hennepin County District Court brought by the state, by Miles Lord, its attorney general. Coffman Realty Company, one of the respondents, and the petitioner appealed from an award of $ 32,500 made by the commissioners. The case was tried before John A. Weeks, Judge, and a jury, which returned a verdict of $ 13,000. Said respondent appealed from an order denying its motion for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a condemnation proceeding, defendant landowner sought review of a judgment from the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which awarded the owner less than he had sought for his property. The owner contended that the trial court erred in permitting cross-examination one of the commissioners and in denying his motion for a new trial because the evidence was insufficient to support the verdict.


OVERVIEW: At issue was the difference in the market value of the land before and after the taking. The jury awarded less than the commissioners had recommended. The court noted that no objection was made as to the qualifications of the witnesses on either side. All appeared to have had a sufficiently wide experience in real estate transactions and estimating real estate values. The court noted that a commissioner in condemnation proceedings might be called by either party to testify as to the amount of the commissioner's award. The commissioner called by the owner to testify was subjected to a complete cross-examination, as were the other value witnesses. Testimony about land values was mere opinion, and the jury was not bound by the amounts set by the witnesses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

641 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Slezak v. Ousdigian


No. 38,052


Supreme Court of Minnesota


260 Minn. 303; 110 N.W.2d 1; 1961 Minn. LEXIS 577



June 16, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Ramsey County District Court brought by June Slezak, Mark C. Erspamer, Paul Ravenscraft, Lawrence H. Furcht, and George Ruoms, all members of the Public Employees Retirement Association, for an accounting and repayment of funds allegedly wrongfully withdrawn from said association by defendant as its secretary. The court, Albin S. Pearson, Judge, granted defendant's motion for summary judgment, and plaintiffs Erspamer, Ravenscraft, and Furcht appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, representatives of a group of members of the Minnesota Public Employees Retirement Association, challenged an order of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) granting summary judgment to defendant, in official capacity as a secretary of the Association, in the representatives' action for an accounting and repayment of funds allegedly wrongfully withdraw from the Association by the secretary.


OVERVIEW: From an examination of the authorities and the record, the court concluded that the representatives were without legal capacity to maintain their suit and that the summary judgment was properly ordered. The court observed that the attorney general could not bind the state by his appearance in the action so as to give the court jurisdiction of the Association or the board representing that agency in the absence of a statute. The representatives had no private contractual or vested right in the Association's pension granted by the government except as payments became due under law. As the pension plan arrangement was statutory, and the members had no vested contractual rights, the appeal presented no case of an unconstitutional impairment of contract rights. Thus, this was not a representative suit. The public employees retirement board's action taken on behalf of the secretary gave rise to the presumption that the secretary acted in good faith in the performance of his duty pursuant to the regulations adopted by the board in so far as the fraud charge was concerned. Lack of subject matter jurisdiction was a question of law suitable for summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court granting summary judgment to the secretary in the representatives' action for an accounting and repayment of funds to the Association.

 

642 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Fairmont Foods Co. v. Duluth


No. 38,204


Supreme Court of Minnesota


260 Minn. 323; 110 N.W.2d 155; 1961 Minn. LEXIS 579



June 16, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied 260 Minn. 323 at 329.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action in the St. Louis County District Court for a declaratory judgment that a milk licensing ordinance of the city of Duluth is invalid and for an injunction restraining said city, its mayor, city clerk, and director of public health from enforcing said ordinance. After findings for defendants, E. J. Kenny, Judge, plaintiff appealed from an order denying its motion for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff dairy sought a judgment declaring that defendant city's ordinance regulating the sale of milk was unconstitutional and an injunction to restrain the city and defendants, the mayor, the city clerk, the and director of public health from enforcing the ordinance. The St. Louis County District Court (Minnesota) dismissed the dairy's action as well as its motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted a modified a model milk ordinance that was developed by the United States Public Health Service. Instead of a bacterial count of 200,000 per liter as permitted by the model ordinance, the city required a bacterial level of 170,000 per liter. The city's ordinance imposed the obligation of procuring a license on those selling milk and set the cost of a license based on the seller's distance from city hall. The city required no fewer than two inspections of each seller's dairy per year. The trial court found against the dairy, and the court reversed. Scientific testimony established that the difference in bacterial counts between the two ordinances was scientifically insignificant. In addition, there was no claim that milk inspected under the model ordinance in other cities was unwholesome. The court found that the more city's rigid requirement bacterial count requirement exceeded its police power because it went beyond the reasonable demands of the occasion. There was no public health benefit to the city's more rigid ordinance controlling production and pasteurization of milk. The ordinance adversely affected the dairy's due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed.

 

643 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Lott v. Davidson


Nos. 38,065, 38,066, 38,067, 38,071


Supreme Court of Minnesota


261 Minn. 130; 109 N.W.2d 336; 1961 Minn. LEXIS 623



May 19, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Four actions in the Hennepin County District Court arising out of the collision of an automobile owned by Eugene Alton and driven by Michael Alton with a taxicab owned by George R. Davidson, d.b.a. Red and White Airway Taxi Company, and driven by Gary L. Raymond, who died as a result of the accident. Two of the actions were for personal injuries, one by Patricia Lott, a passenger in the taxicab, was brought against the Altons and Davidson; one on behalf of a passenger in the Alton automobile, Marie G. Spath, a minor, was brought by Allen N. Spath, her father and natural guardian, against the Altons, who filed a third-party complaint against Davidson. An action by Betty Raymond, trustee for the heirs of Gary L. Raymond, for death by wrongful act and one by George R. Davidson for property damage were brought against the Altons. The cases were consolidated for trial before Dana Nicholson, Judge, and the jury found in a special verdict that the negligence of Raymond did not cause the injuries to his passenger and that there was no contributory negligence or assumption of risk on the part of Marie Spath. The Altons appealed in each case from a judgment entered against them and [***2] from an order denying their motion to set aside the special verdict or in the alternative for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged the decision of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which in an action for negligence following an automobile accident entered judgment against defendants and denied their motion to set aside the special verdict or in the alternative for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The four cases involved in the appeal arose out of a collision at an intersection. A car owned by defendant and driven by his son collided with a taxicab, who was going north. The taxi cab driver was killed in the accident. The taxicab passenger was injured, as was the passenger in defendant's car. The trial court, inter alia, entered judgment against defendants and denied their motion to set aside the special verdict or in the alternative for a new trial. On appeal, defendants claimed that the finding of the jury that the taxicab driver exercised due care and that his conduct was not a contributing cause of the accident was contrary to the evidence. The court affirmed, holding, inter alia, that it was for the jury to decide disputed claims and questions of fact in the light of the evidence introduced under instructions of the court as to the law. Where the verdict had the approval of the trial court and it was not manifestly and palpably contrary to the evidence viewed as a whole, it would not be disturbed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against defendants and the denial of their motion to set aside the special verdict or in the alternative for a new trial in an action for negligence.

 

644 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. McGregor v. Rigg


No. 38,166


Supreme Court of Minnesota


260 Minn. 141; 109 N.W.2d 310; 1961 Minn. LEXIS 553



May 5, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Donald G. McGregor from an order of the Washington County District Court, Leonard Keyes, Judge, denying his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner appealed an order of the Washington County District Court (Minnesota), which denied the prisoner's petition for a writ of habeas corpus that had been directed to respondent warden on the grounds that the prisoner was unlawfully imprisoned.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was convicted of attempt to obtain a narcotic drug by fraud in violation of Minn. Stat. § 618.18. The prisoner challenged his imprisonment by a writ of habeas corpus and claimed that § 618.18 was contrary to the provisions of Minn. Const. art. 1, § 7, and U.S. Const. art. 4, § 27, and U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1, in that its title "Restrictions on obtaining drugs" was ambiguous and misleading and failed to explain the subject matter of the section, that the statute embraced more than one subject and defined more than one crime, and that the prisoner was denied a speedy trial. The trial court determined that the petition for the writ of habeas corpus was without merit and denied it. The prisoner appealed, and the court affirmed. The court held that the title of the statute chapter was well within the requirements of Minn. Stat. § 618.18 against obtaining narcotics by fraud, deceit, misrepresentation, or subterfuge, or by the use of a false name or the giving of a false address.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the prisoner's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

 

645 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Nelson v. Minneapolis, S. P. & S. S. M. R. Co.


Nos. 37,796, 38,049


Supreme Court of Minnesota


260 Minn. 61; 108 N.W.2d 720; 1961 Minn. LEXIS 541



April 14, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Crow Wing County District Court for personal injuries allegedly sustained by plaintiff when the automobile which he was driving collided with a train operated by defendant railroad. Plaintiff also sought consequential damages for injuries to his wife, who was a passenger in the automobile. The case was tried before John T. Galarneault, Judge, and a jury, which returned a verdict for plaintiff. Plaintiff appealed from an order granting defendant's motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict. Although the order did not deny defendant's alternative motion for a new trial, defendant also appealed from the order.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff driver appealed an order of the Crow Wing County District Court (Minnesota), which granted a judgment notwithstanding the verdict (JNOV) to defendant railroad in the driver's action against the railroad arising from the personal injuries the driver sustained in his collision with a train.


OVERVIEW: The driver collided with the railroad's train. The driver commenced an action to recover for his personal injuries. The jury awarded a verdict to the driver, but the trial court granted the railroad a JNOV. The driver appealed, arguing that (1) that he was deprived of his constitutional right to a trial by jury by virtue of the court's order granting JNOV; (2) contributory negligence was improperly asserted as a defense; and (3) the railroad failed to warn the driver regarding a defective or extrahazardous crossing. The court held that the trial court's grant of a JNOV to the railroad did not deprive the driver of his right to a jury trial. While the railroad crossing was under repair, the driver admitted that the condition of the crossing did not contribute to the collision. The collision was caused by the driver's failure to observe an approaching train, which was plainly visible if he had looked. While a view of the approaching train was somewhat obstructed by the cut through which the track ran, it was obvious from the driver's own testimony that, if he had looked, he would have seen the train. Accordingly, contributory negligence was an appropriate defense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of a JNOV to the railroad.

647 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Dahlberg Co. v. Western Hearing Aid Center, Ltd.


Nos. 38,030, 38,031, 38,032


Supreme Court of Minnesota


259 Minn. 330; 107 N.W.2d 381; 1961 Minn. LEXIS 673



January 27, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Six actions in the Hennepin County District Court, one against Western Hearing Aid Center, Ltd., upon a promissory note; one against Dahlberg Western Company, Inc., upon an open account; and four against Oregon Hearing Center, Inc., on promissory notes. Each defendant appealed from an order, Harold N. Rogers, Judge, denying its motion in each case to set aside service of process upon it.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, several foreign corporations that sold and distributed hearing aids, sought review of the order of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), denying their motions to set aside service of process in six actions brought by plaintiff, a corporation and manufacturer of hearing aids, on promissory notes or on open accounts.


OVERVIEW: The summons and complaint in each action were served by leaving a duplicate copy with the Secretary of State of Minnesota as agent for process pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 303.13, subd. 1(3). Defendants argued that they did not have sufficient contacts with Minnesota to render them amenable to the jurisdiction thereof, and that the application of Minn. Stat. § 303.13, subd. 1(3), would be unconstitutional as applied to them. The court affirmed the judgment. It reasoned that defendants were interrelated in that they possessed common officers, directors, and stockholders, who were in turn related to an individual who was an officer, director, and general manager of all defendants. It further reasoned that defendants had enjoyed the benefits of the laws of Minnesota and had had access to its courts to enforce any rights in regard to the transactions involved; that the actions grew directly out of the relationships of the parties created in Minnesota; and that considering the factors bearing on traditional notions of fair play and substantial justice, it was clear that defendants' burden of defending in Minnesota was no greater than would be plaintiff's burden of suing in Oregon.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

648 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State by Clark v. Applebaums Food Markets, Inc.


No. 38,164


Supreme Court of Minnesota


259 Minn. 209; 106 N.W.2d 896; 1960 Minn. LEXIS 676



December 23, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two actions in the Ramsey County District Court to enjoin defendant from practices allegedly constituting unfair competition under Minnesota statutes. Defendant appealed from that part of an order, Arthur A. Stewart, Judge, granting plaintiff's motion for a temporary injunction.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant food market corporation appealed from an order of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which granted a temporary injunction against the corporation in connection with plaintiff State's suit alleging that the corporation violated Minn. Stat. § 325.04 by selling items below cost.


OVERVIEW: The State filed suit seeking a temporary injunction against the corporation for alleged violations of Minn. Stat. § 325.04. After the injunction was issued, the corporation appealed, arguing insufficient evidence existed to warrant the injunction. The State contended that injunctive relief should be available under the statute on a simple showing of threatened injury to a competitor without requiring proof of the purpose or effect of the allegedly illegal sales. The court rejected the argument, holding that the statute prohibited only below-cost sales with the purpose or effect of harming competition. Thus, the court held that the State was required to meet its prima facie burden on the element before issuance of an injunction. Examining the evidence, the court held that the burden had not been met and vacated the injunction. The court also refused to hear amicus curiae arguments as to the constitutionality of the statute, because the litigants had not raised the argument.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

649 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Gram v. Shoreview


No. 38,229


Supreme Court of Minnesota


259 Minn. 145; 106 N.W.2d 553; 1960 Minn. LEXIS 664; 89 A.L.R.2d 325



December 2, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Ramsey County District Court by Frederick S. Gram and other taxpayers of the village of Shoreview for a judgment declaring that actions of said village of Shoreview in connection with the installation of a sanitary sewer system were null and enjoining said village from acting under such proceedings. The court, Clayton Parks, Judge, made an order providing that if plaintiffs failed to file a surety bond in the amount of $ 60,000 the action would be dismissed with prejudice. Plaintiffs appealed from judgment of dismissal entered after their failure to file said bond.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners sought review of a judgment of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which dismissed the owners' action seeking a declaratory judgment against defendants, a village and related parties, preventing the village from the installation of a new sanitary sewer system. The trial court dismissed the action based on the fact that the owners failed to file a required surety bond.


OVERVIEW: The village entered into an agreement with another village regarding the connection of sanitary sewers, with shared costs for the building of the lines. The property owners objected to the project, but a village council voted to proceed. The owners sought a declaratory judgment holding that proceedings taken by the village, under Minn. Stat. § 429, for the establishment of the new sanitary sewers were invalid. The owners also sought injunctive relief. The trial court dismissed the claim based on the owners' failure to furnish a surety bond. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that Minn. Stat. § 562.02, which set forth the bond conditions, did not violate either the U.S. Constitution or the Minnesota Constitution. The court found that statutes requiring security, as a prerequisite to an appeal, existed in Minnesota since the origin of its state governments and that, where other challenges had taken place, it was universally held that such statutes were not unconstitutional. The court compared the statute to Minn. Stat. § 585.04, which required bond as a prerequisite to the issuance of a temporary injunction, and found that the provisions of § 562.02 were less onerous.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

650 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Berndt v. Iten


No. 37,992


Supreme Court of Minnesota


259 Minn. 77; 106 N.W.2d 366; 1960 Minn. LEXIS 652



November 4, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Mandamus proceeding in the Hennepin County District Court upon the relation of Oscar Berndt and Roman Schommer to compel members of the village council of Osseo, the mayor of said village, the clerk of said village, and the village itself to issue a permit for the operation of a trailer park on premises owned by relators. After findings that the alternative writ of mandamus be discharged, William D. Gunn, Judge, relators appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relators, property owners, appealed a judgment from the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) that discharged the property owners' petition for a writ of mandamus to compel respondents, a mayor and village clerk, to issue a permit for the operation of a trailer park.


OVERVIEW: A village ordinance prohibited residential uses on the property owners' property. The ordinance was passed after the property owners submitted a request for a license to operate a trailer park. The property owners claimed that they bought the land in reliance on assurances from village officials that there would be objection to operating a trailer park at the location. The court on appeal affirmed the discharge of the petition for a writ of mandamus. The court held that the prohibition against residential use was reasonable, constitutional, and an appropriate exercise of legislative discretion. The court rejected a claim that the property owners had acquired a vested interest in a prior ordinance that zoned the area for manufacturing but did not prohibit residential use. The property owners did not complete the purchase of more than half of the parcel until after the ordinance prohibiting residences was passed. No building permits had been applied for and no construction had commenced. In addition, the court held that the village's denial of the application for the trailer park permit was not arbitrary, capricious, or unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The judgment discharging the petition for a writ of mandamus was affirmed.

St. Paul v. Morris


No. 37,909


Supreme Court of Minnesota


258 Minn. 467; 104 N.W.2d 902; 1960 Minn. LEXIS 631



July 22, 1960 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied, 365 U.S. 815, 81 S. Ct. 696,    L. ed. (2d)   .


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal by defendant from a judgment of guilty of disorderly conduct entered in the municipal court of St. Paul, Ramsey County, Leonard J. Keyes, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Municipal Court of St. Paul, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which convicted defendant of disorderly conduct for defendant's use of abusive language towards police officers while the officers were arresting defendant's relative.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in the trial court of disorderly conduct for shouting offensive language at police officers while the officer were arresting defendant's relative. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. Defendant argued that the use of abusive language toward a police officer was not disorderly conduct. The court explained that laws that addressed disorderly conduct also encompassed acts which corrupted the public morals or outraged the sense of public decency. The court held that the local ordinance that defendant was convicted for violating was not unconstitutionally vague or indefinite because the ordinance was modeled on Minn. Stat. § 615.17, which had been held valid. The court concluded that no racial issues were presented in the appeal, so no arguments concerning defendant's race were considered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which convicted defendant of disorderly conduct for shouting abusive language at police officers.

State ex rel. La Jesse v. Meisinger


No. 38,104


Supreme Court of Minnesota


258 Minn. 297; 103 N.W.2d 864; 1960 Minn. LEXIS 611



June 17, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Quo warranto upon the relation of Levi J. La Jesse to test the right of E. C. Meisinger to exercise jurisdiction as municipal judge for the city of West St. Paul.



DISPOSITION: Let writ of ouster issue.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court considered a quo warranto proceeding filed by the State to test the right of respondent judge to act as a special judge in the Municipal Court of West. St. Paul pursuant to designation under Minn. Stat. § 488.06(5).


OVERVIEW: The State filed a quo warranto proceeding to test the right of the judge to act as a special judge pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 488.96(5). The court issued the writ of ouster because it found that a special judgment could not be chosen by the mayor or president of the municipal council. The court stated that the fundamental law of Minnesota was that the selection of judgment had to be submitted to the electors and that appointment was to be made by the governor. Minn. Stat. § 488.06(5) was inconsistent with Minn. Const. art. 6, the court found, and it was therefore void. The court further found that because the judge was designated a special judge under an unconstitutional provision, he had no claim to the title or office.


OUTCOME: The court granted a writ of ouster in a proceeding by the State to test the right of the judge to act as a special judge in the Municipal Court of West. St. Paul pursuant to statutory designation.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:

654 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dehler


No. 37,897


Supreme Court of Minnesota


257 Minn. 549; 102 N.W.2d 696; 1960 Minn. LEXIS 561; 89 A.L.R.2d 496



April 8, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Defendant moved the Morrison County District Court to set aside certain indictments for murder in the first degree and said court, E. J. Ruegemer, Judge, certified certain questions to this court as important and doubtful.



DISPOSITION: Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The judge of the Morrison County District Court (Minnesota) certain questions to the court. Defendant had moved to set aside indictments charging him with murders. The judge questioned whether his court had jurisdiction and whether defendant could be prosecuted because of double jeopardy and speedy trial issues. He had been convicted of the murder of his mother and the conviction was reversed because of defective juvenile proceedings.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, age 16 years at the time of the crime, killed his mother, father, brother, and sister. He was tried as an adult for the murder of his mother and received life imprisonment as a sentence. The indictments against him for the other murders were dismissed. Seventeen years later, his writ of habeas corpus was granted and his conviction was void because of the failure to use proper juvenile proceedings in transferring his case to adult district court. The state then re-indicted him for the murders and the judge certified certain questions to the court. One question was whether defendant could be retried for the murder of his mother on the original indictment. The court held that the district court had jurisdiction to try him at the original trial because he was now over the age of 18 years of age and no longer had the status of a juvenile, and the previous proceeding against him did not constitute former jeopardy because the court which tried him lacked jurisdiction. The court held that his failure to demand a speedy trial constituted a waiver of that right.


OUTCOME: The district court had jurisdiction to try defendant for the killing of his mother on the original indictment.

Remington Arms Co. v. G. E. M. of St. Louis, Inc.


No. 37,969


Supreme Court of Minnesota


257 Minn. 562; 102 N.W.2d 528; 1960 Minn. LEXIS 562



April 8, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Hennepin County District Court wherein plaintiff, Remington Arms Company, Inc., sought to enjoin defendants, G.E.M. of St. Louis, Inc., and Playtime Sporting Goods, Inc., from selling certain products in violation of fair trade agreements. During the trial, Miles Lord, attorney general, was allowed to intervence. After findings for plaintiff, Dana Nicholson, Judge, defendants appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which enjoined them from selling or offering for sale certain trademark commodities of the plaintiff at prices below established fair trade minimum prices pursuant to the Fair Trade Act, Minn. Stat. Ann. §§ 325.08- 325.14.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff manufactured and distributed, under the registered trademark "Remington," sporting firearms and loaded ammunition. Plaintiff contracted with two Minnesota retailers stipulating the minimum retail price of its products. Plaintiff did not contract with defendants with respect to the sale of its commodities or the minimum resale prices. Plaintiff argued that the prices stipulated by its contracts were binding on defendants, regardless of whether defendants were parties to the contracts by virtue of the nonsigner provision of the Fair Trade Act, Minn. Stat. Ann. § 325.12 (1937). The court found in favor of plaintiff and restrained defendants. On appeal, the court held that the nonsigner provision of the Fair Trade Act was an unlawful delegation of legislative power. Accordingly, the judgment was reversed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed because the nonsigner provision of the Fair Trade Act was an unlawful delegation of legislative power.

Naftalin v. King

257 Minn. 498; 102 N.W.2d 301; 1960 Minn. LEXIS 557

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state auditor sought review of a judgment from the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), granting plaintiff commissioner of administration's motion for judgment on the pleadings in the commissioner's declaratory judgment action seeking an order to compel the state auditor to issue and sell certain certificates of indebtedness, pursuant to Ex. Sess. L. 1959, c. 90.

The district court ordered the auditor to sell certificates pursuant to the legislative act. The court found that the issuance of the certificates created a debt within the meaning of Minn. Const. art. IX, § 5, and, to the extent that the amount exceeded $ 250,000, it was a violation of the constitution. Exercising its discretion to invoke the doctrine of stare decisis, the court affirmed so that confusion would not result from the curtailment of that part of the building program provided for in Ex. Sess. L. 1959, c. 90.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

657 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. Rolfe


No. 37,964


Supreme Court of Minnesota


257 Minn. 237; 101 N.W.2d 923; 1960 Minn. LEXIS 683



March 18, 1960 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 257 Minn. 237 at 242.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of January 22, 1960, Reported at 257 Minn. 237.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff petitioned for reargument seeking clarification of a previous opinion. He was concerned with respect to his ability to review the constitutionality of 1957 Minn. Laws ch. 730.


OVERVIEW: Review of the issue constituted a direct attack on the legal existence of the Board of Education of the Unorganized Territory of Cass County. With clarification, the court denied the petition. The court held that the question could not be reviewed on an appeal under Minn. Stat. Ann. § 122.051, subd. 1, because the scope of review under that section was limited to the matters that were enumerated therein. Also, according to the court, to raise the constitutional issue on that appeal would have constituted a collateral attack upon the corporate existence, which was not permissible. However, the court held that plaintiff could have a review pursuant to Minn. Stat. Ann. §§ 555.01, 555.11 of the Uniform Declaratory Judgments Act, or Minn. Stat. Ann. § 556.01, which provided for an action to prevent the usurpation of office. Also, the court held that a writ of quo warranto could be available to him pursuant to Minn. Stat. Ann. § 480.04, which granted the supreme court the power to issue such writs. Finally, the court held that the power was not restricted by Minn. R. Civ. P. 81.01(2), which abolished the writ of quo warranto, because the rules applied only to the district court.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition.

 

658 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. Rolfe


No. 37,964


Supreme Court of Minnesota


257 Minn. 237; 101 N.W.2d 923; 1960 Minn. LEXIS 524



January 22, 1960 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied 257 Minn. 237 at 242.


PRIOR HISTORY: Proceeding in the Cass County District Court to enjoin Gertrude Rolfe, superintendent of schools for said county, from proceeding with the consolidation of certain lands of the Unorganized Territory of Cass County with Independent School Districts Nos. 119 and 116, in which action the Board of Education for the Unorganized Territory and Independent School District No. 115 intervened. Defendant and intervenors appealed from an order, John T. Galarneault, Judge, granting plaintiff's motion for a temporary injunction.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a county superintendent of schools, and intervenors, boards of education, challenged an order of the Cass County District Court (Minnesota) that granted a motion for a temporary injunction filed by plaintiff, a taxpayer and resident of an unorganized territory, enjoining the superintendent from proceeding with the consolidation of certain lands of the unorganized territory with certain school districts.


OVERVIEW: Plats for the disputed consolidation had been adopted and approved by the boards of education of the unorganized territory and of each of the affected school districts before the superintendent was served with a temporary restraining order enjoining her from issuing the consolidation order. The district court refused to grant a declaratory judgment, but it issued the temporary injunction under Minn. Stat. Ann. § 585.02. The court reversed its order. An injunction was not to issue where there was an adequate remedy at law. The taxpayer had such a remedy in Minn. Stat. Ann. § 122.051, subd. 1, providing for a direct appeal from a consolidation order in which the merits of such an order could be tested. The remedy of appeal was not inadequate even if the taxpayer was correct that the consolidation proceeding depended upon an unconstitutional statute because operation of the order was suspended by such an appeal and an automatic stay followed. Therefore, no substantial and irreparable injury resulted from denial of the injunction. Injunction was not appropriate before the issuance of the order when there was a right of appeal and taking the appeal precluded substantial injury.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order.

 

659 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Beck v. Spindler


No. 37,736


Supreme Court of Minnesota


256 Minn. 543; 99 N.W.2d 670; 1959 Minn. LEXIS 677



November 20, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the St. Louis County District Court by James M. Beck and Barbara Belancic for damages allegedly sustained in connection with the purchase of a trailer house manufactured by defendant Ventoura Corporation and sold to plaintiffs by defendant Herbert Spindler, sole trader d.b.a. Herb Spindler Company. The case was tried before J. K. Underhill, Judge, and a jury, which returned a verdict that plaintiffs were entitled to rescission and damages of $ 4,617. Defendant Ventoura Corporation appealed from an order denying its alternative motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict or for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff purchasers filed an action for breach of an implied warranty of fitness and for rescission of a sales contract against defendants, a house trailer dealer and a house trailer manufacturer. The St. Louis County District Court (Minnesota) entered judgment for the purchasers against the dealer and the manufacturer, whose alternative motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict or for a new trial was denied. The manufacturer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The purchasers bought a house trailer, which was defective. After defendants failed to repair the defect, the purchasers sued defendants for breach of an implied warranty of fitness and also sought rescission of the sales contract. The jury returned a verdict for the purchasers against defendants, and the manufacturer appealed. In affirming the court held that: (1) jurisdiction over the manufacturer was proper because the business conducted by the manufacturer was of such a nature that it was amenable to suit in Minnesota, and service upon it under Minn. Stat. Ann. § 303.13 satisfied due process; (2) whether or not a purchaser should be able to recover from a manufacturer on an implied warranty claim in the absence of privity of contract, these purchasers could recover from the manufacturer because it was no stranger to the sales contract, an express agreement under its warranty policy between the manufacturer and the purchasers was an integral part of the sales contract, and the manufacturer was a seller within the meaning of the Minnesota Sales Act; and (3) the reasonable time within which the purchasers could rescind did not run while defendants attempted to repair the defect.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for the purchasers against the manufacturer.

 

660 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Northern States Power Co. v. St. Paul


Nos. 37,713, 37,722


Supreme Court of Minnesota


256 Minn. 489; 99 N.W.2d 207; 1959 Minn. LEXIS 671



November 6, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Ramsey County District Court wherein plaintiff sought to enjoin the city of St. Paul, its mayor, and its council members from enforcing certain gas rates specified by ordinance and to have such rates declared unreasonable and confiscatory and new rates established. Dan Gephart, a consumer, was permitted to intervene. After findings, Albin S. Pearson, Judge, that an interlocutory injunction should issue, defendants appealed from said order.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city, mayor, and councilmen, appealed the judgment of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which granted plaintiff power company's petition for an interlocutory injunction restraining defendants from enforcing existing gas rates during the pendency of the action for injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: To offset an increased cost to it, the company petitioned the city for an increase in the rates it might charge its consumers over and above the rates established by an ordinance. The company's petition was denied by defendants. The trial court granted an interlocutory injunction restraining defendants from enforcing existing rates or from interfering with the collection of rates proposed by the company in its petition until the city established reasonable rates. The company was also permitted to raise these rates if further increases in cost of gas to it occurred in the future. The court held that: (1) denial of an application for increased rates, where existing conditions required it, had the same effect as fixing unreasonably low rates; (2) the injunction did not purport to establish a rate but simply preserved the status quo of the parties until the case was finally determined on its merits or until the ratemaking body proceeded to fix a rate that was compensatory; and (3) when a city failed or refused to perform its delegated function, a court of equity may protect the property of a utility from confiscation by enjoining the city from enforcing existing rates.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Asch v. Housing & Redevelopment Authority


No. 37,741


Supreme Court of Minnesota


256 Minn. 146; 97 N.W.2d 656; 1959 Minn. LEXIS 630



June 26, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Ramsey County District Court by certain taxpayers of the city of St. Paul to have declared invalid the Municipal Housing and Redevelopment Act and certain proceedings thereunder by defendant Housing and Redevelopment Authority of City of St. Paul resulting in a sale of certain real estate to defendant Sears, Roebuck & Company. Miles Lord, attorney general, was allowed to intervene. After findings for defendants, Arthur A. Stewart, Judge, plaintiffs appealed from an order denying their motion for a new trial and from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers appealed from an order of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) denying their motion for amended findings or a new trial and from the judgment entered by the district court in favor of defendant Housing and Redevelopment Authority of City of St. Paul. The taxpayers challenged the Municipal Housing and Redevelopment Act and certain proceedings thereunder.


OVERVIEW: The Authority approved a redevelopment plan of two areas pursuant to Minn. Stat. Ann. § 462.415 of the Act. The Authority acquired the property in the areas in eminent domain proceedings and accepted bids to dispose of the land. Pursuant to Minn. Stat. Ann. § 462.541, the Authority established a fair use value of one of the tracts, which was the amount bid by defendant company. The sale to the company was approved. Ann. § 462.525, subd. 6 because the amendment did not substantially alter or effect the general land uses established in the previous plan.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's order denying the taxpayers' appeal and denying their motion for amended findings or a new trial.

 

662 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Housing & Redevelopment Authority v. Greenman


No. 37,620


Supreme Court of Minnesota


255 Minn. 396; 96 N.W.2d 673; 1959 Minn. LEXIS 611



May 29, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Condemnation proceeding in the Ramsey County District Court. After findings for petitioner, Albin S. Pearson, Judge, respondent Allan E. Greenman appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner landowner appealed a judgment of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) entered in favor of respondent housing and redevelopment authority in a condemnation action.


OVERVIEW: The landowner asserted the that the taking of his land, which was in a blighted area, was not for a public purpose because the housing and redevelopment authority was going to sale the land to private person. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment allowing the condemnation. The court held that the taking did not violate Minn. Const. art. 1, § 13 even though the land was to be sold to private persons. The taking of the land was for the purpose of eliminating the blighted area, which was a public purpose. Once the blighted area is cleared, the public purpose is accomplished. The subsequent sale to private persons is merely incidental to the public purpose and is not prohibited. The court held that the landowner's due process rights were not violated by any alleged lack of notice because the landowner had a full hearing on the issue of the reasonableness and the purpose for which the property was taken. The court also held that the trial court properly determined that the correct date for determining damages was the date of taking, which was the date the housing and redevelopment authority deposited the money for the taking with the clerk of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court entered in favor of the housing and redevelopment authority.

Brooklyn Center v. Rippen


No. 37,612


Supreme Court of Minnesota


255 Minn. 334; 96 N.W.2d 585; 1959 Minn. LEXIS 604



May 15, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal in the Hennepin County District Court from a conviction for violation of an ordinance of the village of Brooklyn Center which required defendant to have a license for a boat which he owned. After findings, William C. Larson, Judge, affirming the judgment entered in the justice court of said village, defendant appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant boat owner sought review of a decision from the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which affirmed the judgment of the lower court that convicted the boat owner for a violation of Village of Brooklyn Center, Minn., Village Ordinances ch. 33 that was promulgated by respondent village and required the boat owner to have a license for his boat in order to operate it on a local lake.


OVERVIEW: The boat owner was convicted in the lower court of operating his boat on an area lake without a license, as required by Village of Brooklyn Center, Minn., Village Ordinances ch. 33. The trial court sustained that decision. On appeal, the boat owner contended that the village had no power to license boats. The court reversed the boat owner's conviction because the village had no inherent powers and Minn. Stat. § 412.221, subd. 32 was not an express grant of authority to license the boat owners watercraft because the lake was not wholly within the village's boundaries. The court noted that the licensure of boats presented a statewide problem that was not peculiarly subject to local regulation and that an overly expansive reading of § 412.221, subd. 32 would lead to an absurd result in a state with over 10, 000 lakes.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the boat owner's conviction for the violation of the village ordinance.

 

664 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Foster v. Minneapolis


No. 37,609


Supreme Court of Minnesota


255 Minn. 249; 97 N.W.2d 273; 1959 Minn. LEXIS 593



May 1, 1959 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied 255 Minn. 249 at 254.


PRIOR HISTORY: Mandamus in the Hennepin County District Court to compel Donald Erickson, building inspector of the city of Minneapolis, to issue a building permit for a proposed office building to relators, Melville Foster and Mary B. Foster. The court, William C. Larson, Judge, found that the petition should be dismissed and the alternative writ quashed, and relators appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator property owners challenged a decision from the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which, pursuant to Minn. Stat. Ann. § 462.18, denied the owners' petition for writ of mandamus seeking to compel respondent city building inspector to issue a building permit for a proposed office building to the owners.


OVERVIEW: The owners sought to erect an office building on their property. The premises was originally zoned for commercial property; however, a zoning ordinance was amended to include a consent clause, whereby two-thirds of adjoining landowners could reclassify the area. Based on a reclassification to residential, the building inspector denied the owners' application. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment. The court found that the owners were denied a permit to erect a commercial building on premises which at the time of their purchase were zoned commercial because two-thirds of the adjacent property owners had instituted proceedings to empower the city council to rezone the owners' property from commercial to residential. The court held that a purchaser of real property was entitled to place some reliance on zoning ordinances which had classified the property being purchased. The court held that the consent clause of § 462.18, as a prerequisite to the exercise of the city council's legislative authority to amend the comprehensive zoning ordinance, constituted an unlawful delegation of power to impose restrictions on real property and rendered the provision of the statute invalid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case with directions that an order be issued directing the building inspector to issue the owners a permit for construction of a commercial structure on the premises.

 

665 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Bierlein v. Gagnon


No. 37,559


Supreme Court of Minnesota


255 Minn. 143; 96 N.W.2d 573; 1959 Minn. LEXIS 579



April 3, 1959 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied 255 Minn. 143 at 151.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action in the Carver County District Court to foreclose a mechanics lien brought by Ray J. Bierlein and Frank Lipinski, copartners d.b.a. Chaska Construction Company. After findings for plaintiffs, Harold E. Flynn, Judge, defendants Theodore J. Gagnon and Juanita N. Gagnon appealed from an order denying their motion for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed if plaintiffs consent to reduction of attorneys' fees.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant landowners appealed from a judgment of the Carver County District Court (Minnesota), which found for plaintiff builders and denied the landowners' motion for amended findings of fact, conclusions of law, and order for judgment or, in the alternative, for a new trial in the builders' action to foreclose a mechanics lien.


OVERVIEW: The builders filed an action to foreclose on a mechanics lien after the landowners failed to pay the alleged balance owed on work done by the builders in constructing a house for the landowners. The court affirmed the judgment, except for the issue of attorneys' fees. The court held that the evidence sustained the trial court's finding that the parties never entered into a contract regarding the cost of constructing the house. The evidence sustained the trial court's finding as to the reasonable value of material and labor contributed by plaintiffs. The builders did not violate Minn. Stat. Ann. § 514.74 by "padding" the account. There was no ground for estoppel based on the landowners' claim that the builders proceeded with the work knowing that the landowners insisted throughout that the cost could not exceed $ 28,000. Because the attorneys' fees allowance was determined on an erroneous basis, a new trial on that issue was required. In order to obviate the necessity of such new trial, the court allowed the builders 10 days to consent to a reduction in the attorneys' fees allowed.


OUTCOME: The court granted a new trial on the issue of attorneys' fees unless the builders consented to reduction of attorneys' fees. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

 

666 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Lieser v. St. Martin


No. 37,640


Supreme Court of Minnesota


255 Minn. 153; 96 N.W.2d 1; 1959 Minn. LEXIS 580



April 3, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal in the Stearns County District Court by Arcella Lieser and Thecla Spanier to review a determination of the town boards of the towns of St. Martin and Zion denying their petition to establish a road on the boundary line between said towns. The case was tried before E. J. Ruegemer, Judge, and a jury, which found that said town boards had acted arbitrarily, oppressively, or fraudulently and against the best interests of the public. The town of St. Martin appealed from an order denying its alternative motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict or for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and judgment ordered affirming the town boards.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant town board challenged a judgment from the Stearns County District Court (Minnesota), which held that the board acted arbitrarily, oppressively, or fraudulently and against the best interest of the public in denying respondent citizens' petition to establish a road on the boundary line between the towns. The trial court denied the board's motions for a judgment notwithstanding the verdict or for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The citizens filed petitions with the board and with the board of another town, which was also a party in the trial court, seeking the establishment of a road on the boundary line of the two towns. The boards of each town held a joint meeting and took separate votes on the issue. In the calculation of the combined vote, the majority of the board members did not vote for the road. On appeal, the board challenged the sufficiency of the evidence supporting the trial court's finding that the members of the boards acted arbitrarily, oppressively, or fraudulently and against the best interests of the public in denying the petition. The court found that there was insufficient evidence to support the trial court's decision. The board showed that it along with the other board it had considered the cost of the road, the close proximity of other roads, and maintenance costs that would have been incurred by the towns. The court held that these were all valid factors and that the trial court should have directed a verdict in favor of the boards or entered a judgment notwithstanding the verdict of the jury.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which had been in favor of the citizens, and ordered a judgment in favor of the board and the board of the other town.

State ex rel. Brown v. Johnson


No. 37,625


Supreme Court of Minnesota


255 Minn. 134; 96 N.W.2d 9; 1959 Minn. LEXIS 577; 43 L.R.R.M. 2765; 36 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P65,310



March 26, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari in the Freeborn County District Court upon the relation of Joseph G. Brown and Hugh Brown, copartners d.b.a. Brownie's Bake Shop, to review an order of Charles W. Johnson, State Labor Conciliator, determining the sole bargaining agent of relators' employees to be Hotel, Hospital, Restaurant, and Tavern Employees Union, Local 21, AFL-CIO. Relators appealed from an order, A. C. Richardson, Judge, affirming the order of the labor conciliator and discharging the writ.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer challenged an order of the Freeborn County District Court (Minnesota), which held in the action for judicial review of respondent State Labor Conciliator's administrative order that he validly decided that the union was the sole bargaining agent of the production and delivery employees and that confirmed respondent union's certification as the bargaining representative. Also, the employer's writ of certiorari was discharged.


OVERVIEW: The employer alleged that designating the production and delivery employees as a separate bargaining unit was improper, that not holding an election invalidated the certification, and that Minn. Stat. Ann. § 179.16, subd. 2 unconstitutionally granted overly broad powers to the conciliator. The court affirmed the district court's judgment, concluding that the record reasonably supported the certification. The court reasoned that the production and delivery employees were a craft with the meaning of § 179.16, subd. 2 because the nature of their work and their pay scale distinguished them from the other employees. The court also held that certifying a union without holding an election was a reasonable exercise of the conciliator's power under § 179.16, subd. 2 and that § 179.16, subd. 2 did not unconstitutionally delegate legislative power to the conciliator because he was clearly required to decide representation questions in a way that insured that the employees would have received the full benefit of their right to self-organization and to collective bargaining and because the right to judicial review fully protected interested parties from arbitrary and capricious action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that confirmed the conciliator's certification of the union as the production and delivery employee's sole bargaining representative and that discharged the employer's writ of certiorari.
