Roeck v. Halvorson


Nos. 37,569, 37,570


Supreme Court of Minnesota


254 Minn. 394; 95 N.W.2d 172; 1959 Minn. LEXIS 561



February 27, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two actions in the Wilkin County District Court arising out of a collision between an automobile driven by Olaf I. Halvorson and a tractor driven by Henry T. Roeck, one for wrongful death by Emil Roeck as trustee for the heirs and next of kin of Henry T. Roeck whose death resulted from the accident; and one by Olaf I. Halvorson for personal injuries and property damage against Emil A. Roeck as administrator of decedent's estate. The cases were tried together before C. A. Rolloff, Judge, and a jury, which returned a verdict for defendant in the wrongful death action and for plaintiff in the other action for $ 1,600. Emil Roeck appealed from an order denying his motion for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the administrator of a deceased tractor driver's estate, challenged an order of the Wilkin County District Court (Minnesota), which returned a verdict for respondent automobile driver in the administrator's wrongful death action following a collision of an automobile and a tractor. The trial court entered a verdict for the automobile driver in his action against the administrator for personal injuries and property damage.


OVERVIEW: Two cases arose out of a collision which occurred when a tractor hauling a hayrack, owned and driven by the deceased, turned in front of a 1955 Lincoln automobile, owned and operated by the automobile driver, as he attempted to pass the truck on the left. Both the deceased and the automobile driver were injured and the deceased died as a result of the injuries. The tractor and automobile were damaged. The administrator of the deceased's estate initiated a wrongful death action, and the automobile driver filed an action for personal injuries and property damage. The actions were consolidated, and the trial court entered judgment for the automobile driver in both actions. The administrator appealed, and the court affirmed. The court held that the act of passing the tractor did not present a potential hazard or an actual hazard until the tractor driver had signaled to turn left, which the deceased had not done in this case. Therefore the circumstances did not justify an inference of negligence of the automobile driver based on excessive speed considering the actual and potential hazards.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the automobile driver in both actions arising out of the collision of an automobile and tractor.

 

669 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. Donovan


No. 37,698


Supreme Court of Minnesota


253 Minn. 493; 92 N.W.2d 915; 1958 Minn. LEXIS 695



November 14, 1958 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application in this court by order to show cause by W. Earl Williams and H. E. Swenson for an order directing respondent as secretary of state to refrain from placing the name of August J. Duren on the ballot for November 4, 1958, as candidate for the office of representative in Congress for the Ninth Congressional District.



DISPOSITION: Respondent ordered to omit name from ballot.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Minn. Stat. Ann. § 205.78, petitioner voters sued respondent Minnesota Secretary of State seeking an order compelling the Secretary to remove an independent candidate's name from the ballot for the next election. The voters alleged that the nominating certificate was invalid because it did not comply with Minn. Stat. Ann. §§ 202.19 to 202.22.


OVERVIEW: An independent candidate presented a nominating certificate to the Secretary seeking to have his name included as a nominee for Congress on the next election. The voters sued the Secretary to prevent the candidate's name from being added. The court entered judgment for the voters and held as follows: Under Minn. Stat. Ann. §§ 202.19 to 202.22, the words "voters" and "electors" were interchangeable. The voters' affidavits alleged that certain signers of the certificate had voted in the primary election and other signatures were forged. Under Minn. Stat. Ann. 202.21, those who voted at the primary were ineligible to sign the certificate. After the forged signatures and the primary voters' signatures were removed, the number of valid signatures were less than the number required by Minn. Stat. Ann. § 202.19. Although the candidate was served with notice of the voters' suit, he failed to intervene. Thus, the voters' affidavits had to be accepted as true, and the voters met their burden under Minn. Stat. Ann. § 205.78 of proving that the candidate's certificate did not meet the mandatory requirements of Minn. Stat. Ann. §§ 202.19 to 202.22.


OUTCOME: The court granted the voter's petition and ordered the Secretary to remove the candidate's name from the ballot.

Minneapolis Gas Co. v. Zimmerman


No. 37,568


Supreme Court of Minnesota


253 Minn. 164; 91 N.W.2d 642; 1958 Minn. LEXIS 664



July 11, 1958 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application in the Hennepin County District Court for a declaratory judgment declaring Ex. Sess. L. 1957, c. 4, to be valid and for a writ of mandamus commanding the commissioner of highways to proceed thereunder. After findings granting plaintiff summary judgment, Rolf Fosseen, Judge, defendant appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant commissioner of highways sought review of a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which granted petitioner gas company's motion for summary judgment in its action seeking a declaratory judgment that the Reimbursement Act, 1957 Minn. Ex. Sess. Laws 4, was valid and a peremptory writ of mandamus compelling the commissioner to act thereunder.


OVERVIEW: The gas company sought to compel the commissioner to ascertain, as required by the Act, the cost of relocating the gas company's utility facilities, to certify the cost thereof to the Bureau of Public Roads, and to pay the same out of state highway funds. The trial court granted the gas company's motion for summary judgment and the commissioner appealed. On appeal, the court held that the legislature properly authorized the use of highway funds for the nonbetterment location of utility services as a proper cost of highway construction, reconstruction, improvement, and maintenance. The commissioner argued that the Act, in authorizing payment of relocation costs from the highway fund, conferred upon the gas company a gratuity of public moneys in violation of Minn. Const. art. 9, §§ 1 and 10. However, the court held that the legislature was not prohibited from fixing the conditions of performance and making provisions for the future recognition of claims for damages founded on equity and justice. Accordingly, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's award of summary judgment to the gas company was affirmed.

No. 37,262


Supreme Court of Minnesota


253 Minn. 62; 91 N.W.2d 154; 1958 Minn. LEXIS 652



June 27, 1958 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal in the Hennepin County District Court by Al McGinnis from a decision of the Police Civil Service Commission of the Village of Golden Valley discharging him from the position of chief of police of said village. The case was tried before Irving R. Brand, Judge, and a jury, which returned a special verdict upon which the court reversed the commission. The village appealed from an order denying its alternative motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict or for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant civil service commission appealed from the order of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) that denied its post-trial motions after reversing, vacating, and setting aside its order that suspended plaintiff former employee from his position as chief of police.


OVERVIEW: The former employee filed an action against the civil service commission, challenging his discharge from his position as chief of police. The former employee served the civil service commission with a notice of appeal under the Veterans' Preference Law, Minn. Stat. Ann. § 197.46, and a subsequent notice of appeal under the Police Civil Service Commissions Act, Minn. Stat. Ann. § 419.12. The district court reversed, vacated, and set aside the civil service commission's order based upon the jury's finding that the former employee did not commit inefficiency or misconduct. The district court denied the civil service commission's post-judgment motions. The court reversed and remanded, holding that § 197.46 was not applicable to the positions of chief deputy or head of a department. Because the district court made no findings of fact in connection with its order that the former employee was not a chief deputy or head of a department, the case was remanded for such findings. It was stated that if the former employee was a department head or chief deputy, the case was to be redecided under § 419.12.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the district court's order that denied the civil service commission's post-trial motions and reversed, vacated, and set aside its order that suspended the former employee from his position as chief of police.

State v. Simonsen


No. 37,373


Supreme Court of Minnesota


252 Minn. 315; 89 N.W.2d 910; 1958 Minn. LEXIS 615



May 2, 1958 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Defendant was convicted in the municipal court of Minneapolis, Hennepin County, Tom Bergin, Judge, of driving an automobile while under the influence of intoxicating liquor, and he appealed from an order denying his motion for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and defendant discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Municipal Court of Minneapolis (Minnesota), which convicted defendant of driving an automobile while under the influence of intoxicating liquor and denied his motion for a new trial. Defendant claimed that he suffered from insulin shock.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for driving under the influence after he was involved in an accident. Defendant claimed that he had consumed less than one drink and that he had suffered insulin shock, which mimicked an intoxicated state. Defendant was convicted and appealed. The court reversed and discharged defendant. The court held that the evidence that defendant's conviction was based on was wholly insufficient to sustain a conviction. The court found that the evidence of defendant's diabetic condition was undisputed and that it was prejudicial error to admit defendant's refusal to take a drunkometer test. The evidence indicated that defendant was unable to perceive the opportunity to clear himself by taking the drunkometer test offered to him and had no recollection of it being offered. The opinion testimony of as to defendant's drunken condition by another driver lacked any foundation. The court stated that the witness had no opportunity to observe defendant walking alone, did not hear defendant say anything, did not observe defendant's face, and had not detected an odor of alcohol on defendant's breath.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the conviction and discharged defendant.

Visina v. Freeman


No. 37,510


Supreme Court of Minnesota


252 Minn. 177; 89 N.W.2d 635; 1958 Minn. LEXIS 600



April 11, 1958 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the St. Louis County District Court wherein plaintiff sought to have declared invalid certain laws authorizing a tax levy and bond issues to raise funds for the Port Authority of Duluth. Orville L. Freeman, as governor of the state; Stafford King, as state auditor; St. Louis County; the members of its board of commissioners; the city of Duluth; the members of its city council; and the Port Authority of Duluth were named as defendants. The court, Mark Nolan, Judge, granted defendants' motion for summary judgment, and plaintiff appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer challenged a judgment of the St. Louis County District Court (Minnesota), which granted defendants, a city, a Minnesota governor, a state auditor, a county, the city's port authority, and other municipal entities, summary judgment in the taxpayer's action for a declaration that 1957 Minn. Laws 648, 831, and 849, which authorized a tax levy and bond issues to raise funds for the city's port authority, were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The city's port authority was organized in 1930 under 1929 Minn. Laws 61 and was reorganized under 1955 Minn. Laws 685, § 2 to provide for the appointment of members of the port authority board by the board of county commissioners of the county and by the governor. In anticipation of the opening of the Great Lakes-St. Lawrence waterway, the Minnesota Legislature adopted 1957 Minn. Laws 648, 831, and 849, relating to the financing of the reclamation of land and the construction of terminal port facilities by the city's port authority. Title 1957 Minn. Laws 849 related to state aid, 1957 Minn. Laws 831 related to county aid, and 1957 Minn. Laws 849 related to city aid. The court held that the purposes for which the port authority was established involved the establishment of an agency of the State of Minnesota for the administration of a purely governmental function and that, therefore, the laws authorizing public taxation for the improvement of the port facilities were for a public purpose under Minn. Const. art. 4, § 33. The court further held that 1957 Minn. Laws 648, 831, and 849 did not violate Minn. Const. art. 9, §§ 1, 5, or 10 or Minn. Const. art. 10, § 2 .


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State by Clark v. Wolkoff


No. 37,025


Supreme Court of Minnesota


250 Minn. 504; 85 N.W.2d 401; 1957 Minn. LEXIS 654



October 4, 1957 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Proceeding in the Ramsey County District Court to enjoin defendants from offering for sale and selling certain commodities at less than the cost thereof. After finding for defendants, Arthur A. Stewart, Judge, plaintiff and Minnesota Council of Retail Trade Associations, intervenor, appealed from an order denying their motions for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed refusal of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) to issue an injunction against defendants' sale of commodities at below-cost prices, allegedly in violation of Minn. Stat. § 325.04.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, owners of several retail grocery stores, offered certain commodities for sale to the public at less than cost. Plaintiff, the state through its business development commissioner, sought to enjoin defendants from making such sales on the premise that such below-cost sales violated Minn. Stat. § 325.04, the state's antitrust statute. The trial court declined to issue an injunction, and plaintiff appealed. The state supreme court affirmed denial of injunction, reasoning that mere offering of commodity for less than cost was alone insufficient to violate § 325.04; offering must be undertaken with an anticompetitive objective. As evidence was inadequate to refute defendants' contention that below-cost sales of certain commodities were undertaken in good faith, the trial court properly declined to issue injunction.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; the trial court properly declined to issue injunction, as evidence was insufficient to establish that defendants' below-cost sales were undertaken with requisite intent to injure or destroy competition.

Yaeger v. Delano Granite Works


Nos. 37,109, 37,067, 37,085


Supreme Court of Minnesota


250 Minn. 303; 84 N.W.2d 363; 1957 Minn. LEXIS 632



July 26, 1957 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to review three decisions of the Industrial Commission, one awarding compensation to Cyrilla Yaeger, widow of Bernard F. Yaeger, deceased employee, against Delano Granite Works, employer, and American Mutual Liability Insurance Company, its insurer; one awarding compensation to Doryce Mathison, widow of Harry S. Mathison, deceased employee, against John A. Kuether, d.b.a. Mille Lacs Transport Company, employer, and Great American Indemnity Company, its insurer; and one awarding compensation to Janice and Gary Fleischauer, dependent children of Roy Fleischauer, deceased employee, against Minnesota Valley Canning Company, employer, and Employers Mutual Liability Insurance Company, its insurer.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimants, in separate cases involving the same issue, sought review of orders from the Minnesota Industrial Commission denying their claims against respondent, the special compensation fund, related to the deaths of their husbands.


OVERVIEW: The issue was whether additional payments of compensation were to be made under the law which was in effect at the time that the employees died, Minn. Stat. Ann. § 176.13 (1945), as amended by 1949 Minn. Laws c. 705, § 1(c), or under a subsequently enacted statute, Minn. Stat. Ann. § 176.12, subd. 20 (1949), as amended by 1951 Minn. Laws, c. 457, § 6. Under the former statute the special compensation fund would pay, under the latter statute the employer and insurer would pay. The court reversed and held that 1951 Minn. Laws, c. 457, § 6 was unconstitutional as it purported to apply to employees who died before the effective date of the statute. Since the workmen's compensation act was contractual in nature, any statute which purported to alter a substantial term of the contract, which was in effect at the time the controlling event occurred (the death of the employee in these cases) impaired the obligation of such contract and was unconstitutional. The rights of the claimants, therefore, to benefits of the special compensation fund were not destroyed by the enactment of 1951 Laws, c. 457, § 6 because the circumstances of the cases all came within the purview of the amended act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the orders from the State Industrial Commission.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city and airport commission sought review of judgments from the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which granted respondent taxpayers' motion for summary judgment in each of two actions to enjoin appellants from issuing any bonds or from taking any other action toward a proposed improvement and development of an airport, or in the alternative to require the commission to hold a public hearing immediately on the proposed plan.

Wichelman v. Messner

Supreme Court of Minnesota

June 18, 1957

Flynn, Judge, establishing that title to the premises was in plaintiff and John and Victor Glaeser, defendants Fred Messner and the school district appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of a judgment from the Sibley County District Court (Minnesota) rendered in favor of plaintiffs in an action to determine adverse claims to certain real estate and to obtain possession thereof.


OVERVIEW: Defendant school district obtained property from a farmer with the express purpose that the property be used for construction of a school house. The school house was built, but after several years of service, was discontinued, and the property was sold to defendant purchasers. In the meantime, plaintiffs approached the heirs of the prior owners and induced them to sell their interest in the property to plaintiffs. Thereafter, plaintiffs instituted an action against defendants contending that the cessation of the original purpose of the property and its ultimate sale resulted in a reversion of the property to the heirs of the prior owners, thus their purchased interest superceded that of defendants. The trial court agreed and returned a judgment in favor of plaintiffs, and defendants appealed the decision. The court held, using the applicable rules of statutory construction, that Minn. Stat. § 541.023 could not have been construed to protect old interests in property properly sold. Therefore, the judgment in favor of plaintiffs was improper as against public policy.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed.

State v. Northwestern States Portland Cement Co.


No. 36,826


Supreme Court of Minnesota


250 Minn. 32; 84 N.W.2d 373; 1957 Minn. LEXIS 611



June 14, 1957 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certified to United States Supreme Court September 18, 1957.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action in the Hennepin County District Court for the recovery of income taxes allegedly owed by plaintiff for the fiscal years 1933 through 1948. After findings for plaintiff, Paul S. Carroll, Judge, defendant appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which found in favor of respondent, the State of Minnesota, in the State's action to collect income taxes.


OVERVIEW: The State sought to collect income taxes upon a portion of the taxpayer's total net income that was allocable to State. The tax under Minn. Stat. Ann. § 290.03 related to income derived solely from the interstate business of the taxpayer, a foreign corporation, conducted in the State. The taxpayer contended that it did not have sufficient contacts with the State to make it subject to jurisdiction, that § 290.03 was in conflict with the Due Process Clauses of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Minn. Const. art. I, § 7, and the Commerce Clause. On appeal, the court held that the taxpayer was subject to jurisdiction of the trial court because the taxpayer maintained an office in the State, employed persons in the State, and solicited orders in the State. As to the due process claim, the court found that the imposition of a net-income tax under § 290.03 upon that portion of the taxpayer's net income that was allocated to Minnesota under the three-factor formula of § 290.19 was not unconstitutional as violating due process. Further, the tax imposed was not in contravention of the Commerce Clause since it did not impose a burden upon, or discriminate against, interstate commerce.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

679 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Knutson v. Jackson


No. 36,928


Supreme Court of Minnesota


249 Minn. 246; 82 N.W.2d 234; 1957 Minn. LEXIS 566



March 15, 1957 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Lloyd Laverne Knutson from an order of the Sherburne County District Court, Leonard Keyes, Judge, discharging a writ of habeas corpus and from the judgment entered pursuant thereto.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner juvenile inmate sought review of an order from the Sherburne County District Court (Minnesota), which discharged the inmate's writ of habeas corpus and remanded the inmate to the custody of respondent superintendent of the state reformatory.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to petition, the juvenile court ordered the inmate's prosecution. The inmate was proceeded against in district court in the same manner as anyone. He pled guilty to murder in the second degree. The inmate contended that the district court was without jurisdiction to proceed against him because proceedings held by the juvenile court were defective and that court was therefore without jurisdiction. The court reversed the judgment, finding that the intent of the legislature was clearly to require proceedings under the Juvenile Court Act prior to a proceeding in district court. Further, the court found that there was no conflict with Minn. Const. art. 6, § 5 in requiring a proper proceeding under Minn. Stat. Ann. ch. 260 prior to the district court's exercise of criminal jurisdiction. Additionally, the court found that the inmate's mother was not given notice of the juvenile proceedings as required under Minn. Stat. Ann. § 260.08 and that a waiver of notice signed thereafter was not based on a full knowledge of the facts. Thus, the court concluded that it was inconsistent with principles of due process to hold that requirements of notice had been met.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order.

 

680 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Connor v. Chanhassen


No. 36,953


Supreme Court of Minnesota


249 Minn. 205; 81 N.W.2d 789; 1957 Minn. LEXIS 562



March 8, 1957 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Carver County District Court by Dwight E. Connor and Gladys Z. Connor for a declaratory judgment determining the validity of a zoning ordinance of defendant township. The court, Harold E. Flynn, Judge, found the ordinance unconstitutional, and defendant appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Township of Chanhassen sought review of the judgment of the Carver County District Court (Minnesota), which held that the township's zoning ordinance was unconstitutional. The judgment complained of was rendered in plaintiff business owners' action alleging that after he lost his property through eminent domain, the ordinance subjected him to a possible fine for continuing a lawnmower business not authorized under the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The township enacted a zoning ordinance that limited land use to residential, farming, and other agricultural pursuits and did not permit industrial uses in the owner's area. The owners' lawnmower business was allowed as a nonconforming use, but the initial business site was later taken by the state through condemnation. The owners, wishing to continue the business, sought a rezoning of the area but the township denied the request, indicating however, that they could rebuild and operate the shop elsewhere on their property. The owners did so and were not interfered with in their business. The owners filed the instant action alleging that the ordinance subjected them to potential fines for conducting a nonauthorized use. The trial court held that the ordinance was unconstitutional and the township appealed. The court found that the ordinance was constitutional as an exercise of the township's police powers, but held that inasmuch as the ordinance would deny the owners the right to continue their business, it constituted an unreasonable police regulation restricting the right of use of the owners' property for business purposes contrary to the provisions of U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment as to the constitutionality of the zoning ordinance. The court modified the judgment so as to provide judgment for the owners in accordance with its opinion that where condemnation resulted in the taking of land on which the owners conducted a nonconforming use under local ordinance, the taking did not give effect to the prohibition in the ordinance so as to deprive the owners of the right to continue their use.

 

681 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


In re Common Sch. Dist.


No. 36,903


Supreme Court of Minnesota


249 Minn. 17; 80 N.W.2d 849; 1957 Minn. LEXIS 540



February 8, 1957 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal in the Pipestone County District Court by Bennett Melby from an order of the county board of said county merging Common School District No. 8 with Independent Consolidated School District No. 1. After findings affirming the order, Charles A. Flinn, Judge, appellant appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, protestants contesting a school district merger, challenged the order of the Pipestone County District Court (Minnesota) that affirmed the merger order of appellee county board of commissioners, arguing that the county board lacked jurisdiction to act where signers of the merger petition withdrew their signatures and that the remaining district had no right to refuse to accept children from the merged district without a merger.


OVERVIEW: A petition was filled with the county board of commissioners requesting the merger of two school districts, and the board scheduled a hearing on the petition. Thereafter, six of the signers filed written withdrawals of their signatures. Despite this, a hearing was held, and the board granted the petition and ordered the merger of the school district. The protestants sought judicial review and challenged the district court's judgment affirming the merger order. In affirming, the court concluded that the right of the signers to withdraw their names from the petition ceased to exist the moment the board exercised any action in reliance upon the jurisdiction conferred by the petition. Further, the alleged ultimatum of the enlarged school district that it would not accept non-resident students in the absence of a merger could not have affected the jurisdiction of the board in its decision to merge and was both immaterial and ineffective to invalidate the board's action.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed.

 

682 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Dairyland Power Cooperative v. Brennan


No. 36,978


Supreme Court of Minnesota


248 Minn. 556; 82 N.W.2d 56; 1957 Minn. LEXIS 536



February 1, 1957 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari upon the relation of William Brennan and others to review an order of the Olmsted County District Court, Arnold Hatfield, Judge, granting the petition of Dairyland Power Cooperative in an eminent domain proceeding for the taking of a right-of-way easement over certain lands of said relators.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator landowners challenged an order from the Olmsted County District Court (Minnesota), which entered a judgment in favor of respondent electric power cooperative in an action to condemn an easement over the landowners' property to install electric power lines.


OVERVIEW: The cooperative was authorized under Minnesota laws to engage in supplying heat, light, and power. The cooperative was a federation of member cooperatives, commercial public utilities, and municipalities. It was organized to serve as a corporate vehicle in furnishing wholesale electric energy to its membership. Under Minn. Stat. Ann. § 308.05, the cooperative was given the power to exercise eminent domain. The landowners argued that the proposed taking of their land was unnecessary and that it was not for a public use as required by U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Minn. Const. art. 1, § 13. The landowners also alleged that 1955 Minn. Laws 757, amending Minn. Stat. Ann. § 308.05, was unconstitutional as applied to the cooperative. Upon review, the court concluded that the taking was for a public use because the cooperative acted as a public utility. The court determined that 1955 Minn. Laws 757 was not unconstitutional as applied to the cooperative as the cooperative was a public service corporation. The court found that the cooperative was not required to show absolute necessity for the taking, only that the proposed taking was reasonably necessary to the intended purpose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Genzel v. Halvorson


No. 36,856


Supreme Court of Minnesota


248 Minn. 527; 80 N.W.2d 854; 1957 Minn. LEXIS 532



January 25, 1957 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Koochiching County District Court for personal injuries suffered by plaintiff in a collision between an auto driven by defendant, Harvey Halvorson, and one driven by third-party defendant, John Roemer, in which plaintiff was a passenger. The case was tried before Arnold C. Forbes, Judge, and a jury, which returned a verdict for plaintiff for $ 3,000. After the court denied plaintiff's motion for a new trial if the defendants consented to an entry of judgment for $ 9,830.92, which they did, plaintiff appealed from said order.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injury victim sought review of the decision of the Koochiching County District Court (Minnesota), which denied his motion for a new trial if defendant driver and third-party defendant driver consented to an entry of judgment after the trial court used additur to increase the judgment in the injury victim's action against defendant to recover for personal injuries sustained in a car accident.


OVERVIEW: The injury victim was a passenger in a car driven by third-party defendant. Third-party defendant's car collided with the car driven by defendant. The injury victim filed an action claiming $ 56,000 for personal injuries. The jury returned a verdict for the injury victim in the sum of $ 3,000, after which he moved in the alternative for a new trial on the issue of damages and, in the event of denial, for a new trial on all of the issues. The trial court denied the motion on the condition that each of the drivers consented to an entry of judgment in the sum of $ 9,830.92 against them jointly. The injury victim appealed the order of the trial court on the ground that the use of additur constituted an infringement upon his constitutional guarantee of a jury trial. The court affirmed the trial court and held that the practice of using additur was in the interest of the sound administration of justice and was within the trial court's constitutional power in raising the amount of damages with the consent of the drivers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

684 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Sellin v. Duluth


No. 36,811


Supreme Court of Minnesota


248 Minn. 333; 80 N.W.2d 67; 1956 Minn. LEXIS 645



December 14, 1956 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the St. Louis County District Court wherein plaintiff alleged that she had been improperly laid off by defendant city and sought reinstatement and back pay. After findings for plaintiff, Mark Nolan, Judge, defendant appealed from an order denying its motion for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in accordance with opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city sought review of an order from the St. Louis County District Court (Minnesota), which denied its motion for a new trial after judgment was rendered in favor of plaintiff employee in her action for reinstatement and back pay.


OVERVIEW: Due to a shortage of funds, the city decided to reduce the number of employees. Plaintiff, an elevator operator, protested her layoff to the civil service board. A hearing was held before the civil service commission and her layoff was upheld. Plaintiff brought an action against the city in district court demanding reinstatement and back pay. The district court held a trial de novo without regard to the proceedings before the board. On appeal of judgment in favor of plaintiff, the court reversed. The court held that the removal of a municipal employee was an administrative function although performed in a judicial manner. Pursuant to Minn. Const. art. III, § 1, the trial court's review of the board's decision was limited to questions affecting the board's jurisdiction, the regularity of its proceedings, and as to the merits, whether the order was arbitrary, oppressive, unreasonable, fraudulent, under an erroneous theory of law, or without evidence to support it. The trial court could not find facts but was limited to reviewing the board's findings of facts. This had to be done by way of a writ of certiorari from the board's decision.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

 

685 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Anoka County Airport Protest Committee v. Minneapolis-St. Paul Metropolitan Airports Com.


No. 36,926


Supreme Court of Minnesota


248 Minn. 134; 78 N.W.2d 722; 1956 Minn. LEXIS 625



September 11, 1956 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari upon the relation of the Anoka County Airport Protest Committee in the District Court for Ramsey County to review an order of the Minneapolis-St. Paul Metropolitan Airports Commission extending the Anoka County Airport. After the case was remanded for further hearings, the commission again ordered expansion of said airport, and relator appealed from an order, James C. Otis, Judge, quashing the writ and dismissing the proceedings.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a county airport protest committee, sought review of an order of the District Court of Ramsey County (Minnesota), which quashed a writ of certiorari issued to review an order of respondent, the Minneapolis-St. Paul Metropolitan Airports Commission, extending the Anoka County Airport.


OVERVIEW: The committee argued that the laws creating the commission, 1943 Minn. Laws 500 and L. 1951 Minn. Laws 72, violated the federal and state constitutions, that the commission's acts were similarly unconstitutional, that the commission did not comply with Minn. Stat. Ann. § 360.124 in determining whether the airport should be used by jet aircraft, and that the commissions' findings were not supported by the evidence. The court disagreed. The fact that no resident of Anoka County could serve on the board of governors was not unconstitutional. Providing a unified, integrated, centralized system of air traffic control was a proper exercise of the state's police power, and residents of Anoka County were represented in the legislature. The evidence supported the commission's determinations of factual matters required to be considered under § 360.124. Moreover, it was not the court's function to substitute its judgment for the commission's judgment. The evidence also showed substantial compliance with the Doolittle report, which, in any event, was not mandatory directive. The committee's objections appeared to be based more on an apprehension than on the proposed use.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

In re Menzel's Will


Nos. 36,862, 36,863


Supreme Court of Minnesota


247 Minn. 559; 77 N.W.2d 833; 1956 Minn. LEXIS 605



June 29, 1956 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two appeals to this court by James D. Bain as guardian ad litem for the remaindermen under a trust created under the will of Caroline M. Menzel, deceased, one from an order of the Hennepin County District Court, Levi M. Hall, Judge, authorizing the Northwestern National Bank of Minneapolis as trustee to join in the execution of an agreement amending a long-term lease of certain land partially owned by the trust; and one from a judgment of said court affirming an order of the probate court of said county authorizing said bank as guardian of Emma Menzel Levering, incompetent, part owner of said land and a beneficiary of the trust, to join in the execution of the same agreement.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, appellant guardian ad litem sought review of the judgment of a Minnesota district court which authorized respondent trustee under the will of the decedent to execute and deliver an agreement amending a long-term ground lease. He also appealed from the judgment of the district court affirming a probate court order authorizing the guardian of an incompetent to join in the execution and delivery of that same lease.


OVERVIEW: Under the trust set up in the last will and testament of the decedent, the trustee held an undivided 4/10 of the land to which the lease pertained and the lessor's interest in the lease. In addition, the trustee, as guardian of an incompetent, held an undivided 3/10 of the land and the lessor's interest in the lease. The court held that the petitions of the trustee constituted application for authority to execute and deliver the proposed amended lease, a request for instructions in the administration of the trust, and for construction of the trust instrument in the light of the uses and trusts statutes. After examining the express and implied powers conferred by the will, the court concluded that the approval of the proposed lease was not in contravention of the trust. There was nothing in the instrument which could indicate that the settlor had a sentimental reason for wanting the property to vest in the contingent remaindermen at the termination of the trust free from the incumbrance of a lease continuing into the future. There was no support for the contention that the proposed extension would deprive the contingent remaindermen of property without just compensation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court.

State ex rel. Associated Master Barbers & Beauticians v. Eischen


No. 36,784


Supreme Court of Minnesota


246 Minn. 559; 76 N.W.2d 385; 1956 Minn. LEXIS 541



March 16, 1956 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Quo warranto in this court upon the relation of Associated Master Barbers & Beauticians of Minnesota and Garrett Brink, A. J. Raganen, Jack Smith, C. H. Theesfield, and Carl F. Schulz, individually and as officers thereof, to test the validity of the appointments of Joseph Eischen and Peter Odegard as members of the Board of Barber Examiners.



DISPOSITION: Respondents' motion to quash the writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent board members filed a motion to quash a writ of quo warranto by relators, an association and officers, seeking the removal of the board members from their offices as members of the board of barber examiners.


OVERVIEW: The association and the officers sought, by writ of quo warranto, removal of the board members from their offices as members of the board of examiners. Specifically, the association and the officers asserted that the board members were unqualified to serve as members of the board because they were not practical barbers who had followed the occupation for at least five years prior to appointment as required under Minn. The board members filed a motion to quash the writ on the ground that § 154.22 was unconstitutional as it placed an unreasonable restriction upon the governor's power of appointment under Minn. Const. art. V, § 4. The court held that the right of the legislature to prescribe qualifications as the basis for appointment to public office was not inconsistent with the executive power of appointment to office. Accordingly, the requirement of § 154.22 was not unconstitutional as an unreasonable restriction upon the governor's power of appointment. The motion to quash was denied.


OUTCOME: The board members' motion to quash was denied.

State v. Duluth, M. & I. R. R. Co.


No. 36,621


Supreme Court of Minnesota


246 Minn. 383; 75 N.W.2d 398; 1956 Minn. LEXIS 521



February 24, 1956 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certified to United States Supreme Court May 22, 1956.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal by Duluth, Missabe & Iron Range Railway Company from a judgment of the District Court for St. Louis County, Gustavus Loevinger, judge of the second judicial district acting for the judges of the eleventh judicial district, affirming an order of the Railroad and Warehouse Commission requiring said company to reestablish certain passenger train service and directing the time schedule for said service. Order of Railway Conductors, Brotherhood of Locomotive Firemen and Enginemen, Brotherhood of Locomotive Engineers, Brotherhood of Railroad Trainmen, and Range Municipalities & Civic Association were permitted to intervene in the district court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant railroad company sought review of a judgment from the District Court for St Louis County (Minnesota), which affirmed an order of the Railroad and Warehouse Commission that required the company to reestablish certain passenger train service and directed the time schedule for the service. Intervenor unions were also involved in the district court.


OVERVIEW: The company was a common carrier of passengers and freight and had scaled back its passenger service as the demand for it decreased. Although the Commission initially approved the company's application to discontinue certain passenger service, on its own initiative it later issued an order to show cause why the service should not be reestablished and issued its decision reinstating the service. The company appealed the decision pursuant to Minn. Stat. Ann. § 216.25. Under the standard of review established in § 216.25, the court held that the evidence sustained the findings of the Commission and the district court and the Commission did not go beyond its authority in ordering reestablishment of the passenger service. The court did acknowledge that the record of the Commission hearing revealed that one of the commissioners had behaved very hostile to the company. However, the court noted that it did not have the power to grant a new hearing, nor was their any way in which the court could disqualify a commissioner for bias. The court noted that the company had received due process and was allowed to submit its evidence. The court therefore held that the Commission's order was lawful.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment enforcing the Commission's order.

State ex rel. Foster v. Naftalin


No. 36,749


Supreme Court of Minnesota


246 Minn. 181; 74 N.W.2d 249; 1956 Minn. LEXIS 504



January 20, 1956 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Proceeding in quo warranto in the District Court for Ramsey County to test the rights of the following respondents to hold office pursuant to L. 1955, c. 857: Arthur Naftalin as Secretary of the State Executive Council; Arthur Hansen as Secretary of the State Investment Council; and Morris Hursh as Secretary of the State Board of Pardons. The court, James C. Otis, Judge, granted relators motion for summary judgment, and respondents appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent state officials appealed from a summary judgment of the District Court for Ramsey County (Minnesota), which, in a quo warranto proceeding by relator citizens, determined that the state officials did not have a right to hold office pursuant to 1955 Minn. Laws ch. 857 because the law was invalid.


OVERVIEW: The legislature initiated a bill to reorganize its government. The bill passed the house and went to the senate. In the senate two amendments were passed, the first of which directed the commissioner of administration to formulate a system of uniform records and the second of which gave such duty to the auditor. After conference, the bill with the second amendment was passed; however, due to an error, the bill with the first amendment was signed by the governor. The trial court ruled that this variance rendered the law void. On appeal, the state officials contended that the variance was not material or that the erroneous provision should be severed from the law. The court affirmed the judgment. The court concluded that the erroneous provision was material because it was amended by the senate. The court determined that subsequent valid legislation defining the duties of the auditor could not be used to clarify the erroneous provision if the law was not validly enacted in the first place. Most importantly, the court affirmed its prior position that portions of invalidly enacted legislation could not be severed from those portions that were otherwise validly enacted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in the quo warranto proceeding by the citizens that the state officials did not have a right to hold office under invalidly enacted legislation.

In re Consolidation of School Dist.


Nos. 36,562, 36,673, 36,689


Supreme Court of Minnesota


246 Minn. 96; 74 N.W.2d 410; 1956 Minn. LEXIS 495



January 6, 1956 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals in the District Court for Freeborn County from an order of consolidation made by the county superintendent of schools of said county creating Independent Consolidated School District No. 44. After a jury verdict that the consolidation was arbitrary, the court made findings, A. C. Richardson, Judge, setting aside the order of consolidation, and the consolidated school district appealed from the order for judgment, from an order denying its motion for a new trial, and from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a consolidated school district, challenged an order and judgment of the District Court for Freeborn County (Minnesota), which, on appeal by respondents, the school board officers of affected districts, a corporation, and several individual district residents, set aside a proceeding for the consolidation of a number of school districts in Freeborn County. It also appealed an order denying its motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: A proposed school consolidation plat was approved by an election, and respondents challenged the order of consolidation. The district court submitted to the jury the question of whether the consolidation was arbitrary, oppressive, or in unreasonable disregard of the best interests of the territory affected. The jury answered in the affirmative, and the district court entered judgment setting aside the consolidation. On appeal, the court affirmed the district court's judgment and order denying a new trial. The court held that pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 122.21, read together with Minn. Stat. § 122.32, the district court had jurisdiction to determine whether the consolidation was for the best interests of the territory affected, but its inquiry was limited to the question of whether the proceedings were arbitrary, resulting in unnecessary injustice to those who complained. The evidence was sufficient to sustain the district court's findings because it was unfair for one of the school districts to lose 75 percent of its assessed valuation and only two school children.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Minnesota Baptist Convention v. Piillsbury Academy


No. 36,617


Supreme Court of Minnesota


246 Minn. 46; 74 N.W.2d 286; 1955 Minn. LEXIS 691



December 23, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the District Court for Hennepin County for a declaratory judgment that plaintiff, Minnesota Baptist Convention, has authority to elect trustees for defendant Pillsbury Academy. Alleged trustees of the academy were joined as defendants, and later persons plaintiff claimed to have named as trustees were made additional defendants. After findings for plaintiff, the academy and certain individual defendants appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, academy and others, sought review of a decision of the District Court for Hennepin County (Minnesota), which found for plaintiff, religious convention, in the convention's action for declaratory judgment that it had authority to elect trustees for the academy.


OVERVIEW: The religious convention filed an action for declaratory judgment that it had authority to elect trustees for the academy. The trial court entered judgment for the convention. On appeal, the court affirmed. The amendment which tried to take from the religious convention the right to fill all vacancies in the board of trustees was a nullity and the convention continued to have the sole rights to elect the trustees. The academy's argument that the privilege granted to the convention to elect trustees for the academy was a grant to an outsider and hence could not be a membership right within the meaning of the Minnesota Nonprofit Corporation Act, Miss. Stat. Ann. § 317, failed. Under the liberal policy to be afforded in the operational activities of nonprofit corporations, it was not necessary that the entity meet every recognized requirement of qualification of a member or shareholder. Section 317.02, subd. 11 merely required that the entity was to have some or any of the rights usually possessed and exercised by such a class. The purported amendment was ineffective and void because of failure of the trustees to submit the resolution to the convention for its approval as required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which found for the religious convention in the convention's action for declaratory judgment that it had authority to elect trustees for the academy.

Western Auto Supply Co. v. Commissioner of Taxation


No. 36,340


Supreme Court of Minnesota


245 Minn. 346; 71 N.W.2d 797; 1955 Minn. LEXIS 654



August 5, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari upon the relation of Western Auto Supply Company to review a decision of the board of tax appeals affirming an order of the commissioner of taxation assessing additional income franchise tax against relator for the year ending December 31, 1947.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner corporate taxpayer appealed by certiorari from a decision of the state board of tax appeals (Minnesota), which affirmed an order by respondent, the Commissioner of Taxation for the State of Minnesota, to assess additional income franchise taxes against the taxpayer using a three-factor formula as provided in Minn. Stat. Ann. § 290.19, subd. 1(2)(b) (1945).


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer, which was engaged in the retail and wholesale merchandising of automotive parts and accessories and other merchandise on a nationwide basis, filed its income and franchise tax return based on a separate accounting system that it had previously used. The Commissioner claimed that there was a deficiency in the taxes, disallowed the taxpayer's accounting methods, and assessed a deficiency for the tax year based on the three-factor formula in § 290.19, subd. 1(2)(b). On de novo review, the state board affirmed the Commissioner's decision. In affirming the judgment, the court held that the record as a whole justified its belief that the formula adopted by the Commissioner and approved by the state board did give weight to the different factors responsible for the taxpayer's earning of the income; therefore, the multiple formula applied did properly and fairly reflect the taxpayer's income from its entire business among the various states in which it was conducted. Thus, the court concluded that the state board's affirmance of the Commissioner's decision to use the three-factor formula was supported by the evidence, and therefore had to be affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the state board's decision, which affirmed the Commissioner's decision to assess additional income franchise tax against the taxpayer based on the three-factor formula.

 

693 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Starkweather v. Blair


No. 36,538


Supreme Court of Minnesota


245 Minn. 371; 71 N.W.2d 869; 1955 Minn. LEXIS 655



August 5, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the district court for Ramsey county wherein E. R. Starkweather sought a declaratory judgment establishing the invalidity of a statutory provision that no part of an appropriation should be used to pay the salary of an assistant director of the division of game and fish, which office plaintiff previously held. After findings for plaintiff, Robert V. Rensch, Judge, defendants, Frank D. Blair as director of the division of game and fish, Chester S. Wilson as commissioner of conservation, and Robert D. Stover as director of civil service appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state executives challenged a judgment of the District Court for Ramsey County (Minnesota) that declared a rider to an appropriations bill invalid, and that ordered plaintiff civil servant reinstated to his former assistant director position. The trial court held that the rider violated prohibitions against bills of attainder and ex post facto laws, improperly impaired an obligation of contract, and violated the servant's rights.


OVERVIEW: The legislature refused to appropriate funds under Minn. Stat. Ann. § 97.49, subd. 1, to pay the civil servant's assistant director salary. Therefore, he was laid off. The court reversed the judgment that found the rider violated prohibitions against bills of attainder and ex post facto laws. The rider violated neither because it did not prohibit the servant from occupying other civil services positions, it did not specifically identify him, and there was no indication that the legislature passed the rider to punish the civil servant. The rider did not impair an obligation of contract because the legislature by creating the assistant director position possessed the power to abolish it and to fail to fund the position. Furthermore, in Minnesota a civil servant did not have a vested right in a particular position. For the same reason the legislature by enacting the rider did not unconstitutionally remove a state officer in the executive branch without finding malfeasance or nonfeasance. Finally, the court reversed the trial court's conclusion that the rider deprived the civil servant of equal protection because there were no facts in the record to sustain that conclusion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that ordered the civil servant's reinstatement.

St. Paul v. Dalsin


No. 36,593


Supreme Court of Minnesota


245 Minn. 325; 71 N.W.2d 855; 1955 Minn. LEXIS 652



July 22, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Defendant was convicted in the municipal court of St. Paul, Ramsey county, Edward D. Mulally, Judge, of a violation of the building code and appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Municipal Court of St. Paul (Minnesota) of violating Building Code of City of St. Paul § 111-1, which required non-resident roofers to hold a license in warm air heating, ventilation, and general sheet metal work.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a roofer with a firm whose principal place of business was in Minneapolis. He was installing copper flashing associated with the roof installation on a building in St. Paul. The building inspector determined that defendant was doing sheet metal work in violation of Building Code of City of St. Paul § 111-1 which required a license for such work. In order to obtain a certificate as a master tradesman, and qualify for such work, defendant's firm was required to maintain a place of business in St. Paul. The court held that the ordinance was invalid because installation of metal flashings was incidental to roofing work, and the requirement that a roofer also obtain a license in warm air heating, ventilation, and sheet metal work was unreasonable and oppressive. In reversing the conviction the court held that the classification of non-resident contractors, in requiring them to obtain a place of business in St. Paul, was a violation of the equal protection clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the conviction.

 

695 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Beck v. Groe


Nos. 36,476, 36,477


Supreme Court of Minnesota


245 Minn. 28; 70 N.W.2d 886; 1955 Minn. LEXIS 620; 52 A.L.R.2d 875



May 27, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two actions in the district court for Mower county, one for wrongful death by Roy W. Beck as trustee in re the death of Ardell L. Beck, who died in a collision of the car in which she was riding with one owned by defendant Pearl Groe and driven by defendant Gerald D. Groe and one owned and driven by defendant Harry Levi; and the other action by Roy W. Beck for personal injuries and property damage against the same defendants arising out of the same collision. In both actions The Prom, Inc., was named a defendant by reason of allegedly having sold intoxicants to defendant Gerald D. Groe who was a minor. The cases were tried before A. C. Richardson, Judge, and a jury, which returned a verdict for $ 10,000 in the wrongful death action and for $ 8,250 in the other action against defendants Gerald D. Groe, Pearl Groe, and The Prom, Inc. The Prom, Inc., appealed from an order in each case denying its alternative motion for judgment or a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and judgment ordered for defendant The Prom, Inc.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant bar owner appealed from orders of the District Court for Mower County (Minnesota), which denied the bar owner's motions for judgments notwithstanding verdicts that held the bar owner liable to plaintiff husband for his wife's wrongful death and the husband's injuries that were incurred in a car collision. The bar owner was found liable for having sold intoxicants to the minor driver who caused the collision.


OVERVIEW: The husband obtained judgments against the bar owner pursuant to the wrongful death act, Minn. Stat. § 573.02, and the civil damage act, Minn. Stat. § 340.95, based upon the bar owner having sold 3.2 beer to the minor who caused the car collision that killed the husband's wife. However, the court directed on appeal that judgments should be entered in favor of the bar owner. The court explained that because the wrongful death act and civil damage act provided statutory rights unknown at common law, they were to be strictly construed. The court noted that the civil damage act provided a right of recovery only against alcohol providers who illegally sold intoxicating liquors. The court determined that under the Minnesota liquor laws, 3.2 beer did not come with the definition of an "intoxicating liquor." Thus, the court held that even though the bar owner violated Minn. Stat. § 340.03 by selling 3.2 beer to the minor, the action did not constitute an illegal sale of intoxicating liquor under the civil damage act. Also, the husband could not assert claims under civil damage act for his deceased wife because the statute required the action to be brought by the injured party.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the orders of the trial court with instructions that the trial court enter judgments below, notwithstanding the verdicts, in favor of the bar owner.

 

696 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Iowa Electric Light & Power Co. v. Fairmont


No. 36,282


Supreme Court of Minnesota


243 Minn. 176; 67 N.W.2d 41; 1954 Minn. LEXIS 700



November 19, 1954 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the district court for Martin county to enjoin defendant city from condemning the gas distribution system operated by plaintiff Iowa Electric Light and Power Company in said city, which property was being held by plaintiff The First National Bank of Chicago as trustee under a mortgage indenture to secure a bond issue. After findings for defendant, Chris Carlson, Judge, plaintiffs appealed from an order denying their motion for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff gas company brought an action to enjoin defendant city from condemning the gas distribution system operated by the gas company. The District Court of Martin County (Minnesota) ruled that Minn. Stat. Ann. ch. 454 granted the city the right to condemn the gas company's system. The gas company filed a motion for a new trial, which was denied. The gas company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The gas company argued that Minn. Stat. Ann. ch. 117, which provided for the taking of private property for public use, was inapplicable to the condemnation of personal property and that it was unconstitutional and ineffective. On review, the court noted that Minn. Stat. Ann. § 454.01 provided that the city could exercise the power of eminent domain in pursuance of Minn. Stat. Ann. ch. 117 to take any and all property necessary to establish a gas utility system. The court held that even under strict construction, ch. 117 did not exclude condemnation of mixed real and personal property operated as a unit, such as the gas company's utility system. There was no indication that the legislature intended ch. 117 to be limited in it its application to the condemnation of real estate only. The court further held that the statutory provision for determining compensation was adequate and that the district court had inherent power to consider the compensation to be awarded the gas company for improvements, betterments, and extensions made during the pendency of the condemnation action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court in favor of the city in the gas company's action to enjoin the city from condemning the gas company's gas distribution system.

 

697 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Reynolds


No. 36,372


Supreme Court of Minnesota


243 Minn. 196; 66 N.W.2d 886; 1954 Minn. LEXIS 703



November 19, 1954 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal to the district court for Washington county from a conviction in the municipal court of Stillwater, Washington county, on a complaint for disorderly conduct based on L. 1953, c. 661.



DISPOSITION: Defendant moved for a dismissal of the action on the grounds that the statute is unconstitutional, and the court, Carl W. Gustafson, Judge, denied the motion and certified the question to this court as important and doubtful. L. 1953, c. 661, held constitutional.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Washington County (Minnesota) certified to the court the question of whether Minn. Stat. Ann. § 615.17, the statute upon which defendant's conviction on a count of disorderly conduct was based, was void and unconstitutional because of vagueness and indefiniteness.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that Minn. Stat. Ann. § 615.17 was unconstitutional because it was not limited to public places and that there were no limitations upon the words "brawling" and "fighting." He claimed that those terms, due to the vagueness and the indefiniteness of the statute, included many innocent acts which it could not have been the intention of the legislature to make a crime. The court rejected defendant's arguments. The court held that the question of whether or not the offense had in fact been committed depended upon the circumstances of the situation and the evidentiary proof tested by the rules of procedure applicable at the trial. The difficulty in construing the statute had no bearing on the question of its validity because, whatever construction of the statute was adopted, a definite standard was established. Common usage and legal tradition had given to the terms "brawling" and "fighting" used in the statute a clear and definite meaning.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

698 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Koalska v. Swenson


No. 36,455


Supreme Court of Minnesota


243 Minn. 46; 66 N.W.2d 337; 1954 Minn. LEXIS 683



October 1, 1954 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied, 348 U.S. 908, 75 S. Ct. 308, 99 L. ed.    .


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal by Robert J. Koalska from an order of the district court for Washington county, Rollin G. Johnson, Judge, denying his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.



DISPOSITION: Upon motion of respondents, Edwin T. Swenson, warden of Minnesota state prison, and Jarle Leirfallom, commissioner of public welfare, to dismiss the appeal, order of the trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator inmate appealed from an order of the District Court for Washington County (Minnesota), which denied his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of grand larceny and sentenced to prison to from two to 10 years. After his conviction, the state board of parole published a set of revised rules governing parole and discharge. Pursuant to the new rules, the inmate was denied parole. Also, pursuant to the new rules, the inmate had been placed in segregation as a disciplinary measure. The inmate claimed that the application of the revised rules to him constituted an ex post facto law in violation of his constitutional rights. The court affirmed the trial court's order. The court noted that, nowhere in the inmate's petition did he claim that the sentencing court lacked either personal or subject matter jurisdiction or that the sentence was not imposed by a court of competent jurisdiction. The court found that the application of the new rules to the prisoner did not violate his constitutional rights under Minn. Const. art. 1, § 11, or U.S. Const. art. I, § 10. Furthermore, the inmate could not use the habeas corpus remedy to obtain relief from alleged ill treatment at the prison, where he was being lawfully held under a valid judgment, sentence, and commitment; and the inmate's sentence was not improper.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

 

699 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Richter v. Swenson


No. 36,456


Supreme Court of Minnesota


243 Minn. 42; 66 N.W.2d 17; 1954 Minn. LEXIS 682



September 17, 1954 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied, 348 U.S. 893, 75 S. Ct. 225, 99 L. ed.    .


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal by Lester L. Richter from an order of the district court for Washington county, Rollin G. Johnson, Judge, denying his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.



DISPOSITION: Upon motion of respondents, Edwin Swenson, warden of Minnesota state prison, and Jarle Leirfallom, commissioner of public welfare, to dismiss the appeal, order of the trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator inmate appealed from the order of the District Court for Washington County (Minnesota), which denied his petition for a writ of habeas corpus. Respondents, the warden and the Commissioner of Public Welfare, moved to dismiss the appeal.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was incarcerated on a forgery conviction. After the inmate actively participated in a riot, the warden placed him in segregated confinement. However, the Commissioner never enacted a mechanism for using segregated confinement as a means for discipline. The inmate filed a petition for habeas corpus seeking immediate release, contending that the use of segregated confinement was an ex post facto measure in violation of Minn. Const. art. 1, § 11 and U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 because it inflicted a more burdensome and aggravated punishment than was in existence at the time of his original sentencing or at the time of his participation in the riot. On review of the petition, which the warden and the Commissioner moved to dismiss, the court noted that, once the inmate had been committed or detained by virtue of a final judgment from a competent tribunal, under Minn. Stat. Ann. § 589.01, habeas corpus proceedings were not available to the inmate as a means of seeking release. Habeas corpus proceedings were to be used against unlawful imprisonment. The court found that the inmate was lawfully imprisoned and affirmed the denial of the petition.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

 

700 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State by Burnquist v. Miller Home Dev., Inc.


No. 36,130


Supreme Court of Minnesota


243 Minn. 1; 65 N.W.2d 900; 1954 Minn. LEXIS 676; 50 A.L.R.2d 1377



August 6, 1954 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Proceeding in the district court for Mower county by the state, by its attorney general, for the condemnation of lands in said county for highway purposes. Petitioner entered into a stipulation with respondents owning parcel 12 reducing the size of said parcel and abandoning the taking of the right of access of said respondents. The commissioners awarded $ 42,260 as to parcel 12, and on appeal by both the petitioner and respondents R. J. Naslund and others, the jury returned a verdict for $ 39,559. Respondents R. J. Naslund and others appealed from an order, Martin A. Nelson, Judge, which denied their motion for allowance of expert witness fees and attorneys' fees and also for attorneys' fees and costs incident to the abandonment of the taking of the right of access and also granted petitioner's motion for taxation of expert witness fees and allowed its taxation of costs.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed except as to appellants' costs with respect to the right of access.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners challenged an order by the District Court for Mower County (Minnesota), which taxed costs and disbursements against them in a condemnation proceeding brought by respondent State of Minnesota.


OVERVIEW: The State petitioned the trial court to condemn certain parcels of land in Mower County for trunk highway purposes. After the appeal of the commissioners' award to the landowners, the jury assessed the damages due and the trial court ordered the landowners to pay costs and disbursements and witness fees. The trial court denied the landowner's motion requesting reimbursement for costs, expenses, and fees of counsel incurred in defending the taking of the right of access. The landowners appealed this decision. Affirming the portion of the motion which granted the State their costs, fees, and expenses, the court held that under Minn. Stat. Ann. § 117.20(2) the State was entitled to reimbursement as the prevailing party in the condemnation proceeding. In modifying the trial court's judgment, the court held that the landowners were also entitled to reimbursement for their actions in defending their right of access. The court found no merit in the State's contention that the landowners by entering into a stipulation regarding the land released their rights under Minn. Stat. Ann. § 117.16. The court held that right of access was an independent property right.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order as modified. The court found that the landowners were entitled to recover these reasonable costs and expenses including fees of counsel relating to their rights of access.

 

701 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Veblen v. Swenson


No. 36,441


Supreme Court of Minnesota


243 Minn. 578; 65 N.W.2d 619; 1954 Minn. LEXIS 724



August 6, 1954 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition in this court by Kenneth Melvin Veblen for a writ of habeas corpus and appeal from an order of the district court for Washington county, Rollin G. Johnson, Judge, denying his petition for such a writ.



DISPOSITION: On motion of respondent as warden of the state prison, appeal and petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner appealed from an order of the District Court for Washington County (Minnesota), which denied his petition for a writ of habeas corpus. He also applied for an original writ of habeas corpus. Respondent State moved to dismiss the appeal and the petition.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner pleaded guilty to second-degree forgery. A subsequent information charged him with four prior convictions. The prisoner admitted to three of the four prior convictions and the trial court sentenced him in accordance with the habitual criminal act, Minn. Stat. § 610.29. The prisoner contended that the trial court deviated from Minn. Stat. § 610.31 in not cautioning him of his right to trial by jury with respect to the truth of the information charging him with the prior felony convictions. The court did not consider whether there was any merit to the contention because, even if it was assumed that the prisoner had a constitutional right to be informed of his right to a jury trial prior to arraignment, the failure of the trial court so to inform him would not have been a violation of the due process clause where the prisoner was represented by competent counsel. Since it was a basic principle that habeas corpus was available to correct jurisdictional defects only and that it was not a substitute for appeal, the prisoner failed to present a case entitling him to habeas corpus relief.


OUTCOME: The court granted the State's motion to dismiss the appeal and the petition.

Western States Utilities Co. v. Waseca


No. 36,341


Supreme Court of Minnesota


242 Minn. 302; 65 N.W.2d 255; 1954 Minn. LEXIS 646



May 28, 1954 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the district court for Waseca county for a declaratory judgment declaring a provision of an ordinance of the city of Waseca invalid and directing said city and its council to consider plaintiff's application for an increase in the rates to be charged for natural gas in said city. After findings for plaintiff, C. A. Rolloff, judge of the twelfth judicial district acting for the judge of the fifth judicial district, defendants appealed from an order denying their motion for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a declaratory judgment action seeking to declare invalid an ordinance of defendant City of Waseca, regarding rates to be charged for natural gas, the city and defendants, members of its council, appealed the order of the District Court for Waseca County (Minnesota), which, having entered judgment for plaintiff utilities company, denied defendants' motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The utilities company presented a petition to the city council, requesting an increase in rates and alleging that the rates in effect made it impossible for the utilities company to realize a fair and reasonable return. The petition was denied, and the utilities company initiated a declaratory judgment action to declare invalid the city's ordinance that regulated franchises and the rates to be charged for utilities. The trial court found the ordinance to be invalid and denied defendants' motion for a new trial or for amended findings. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court found that the city had no power or authority to contract for maximum rate schedules because of the enactment of 1919 Minn. Laws ch. 469. The city could not urge that the utilities company was estopped to challenge the validity of the ordinance because the city's authority, power, and duty in regard to rate regulation was delegated by the state and limited by the terms of such delegation. The title of 1919 Minn. Laws ch. 469 contained only one subject, which was the delegation of rate-fixing powers, and other provisions contained in the act were ancillary or incidental to that one subject.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.
