Fairview Hospital Ass'n v. Public Bldg. Service, etc. Employees Union


No. 36,125


Supreme Court of Minnesota


241 Minn. 523; 64 N.W.2d 16; 1954 Minn. LEXIS 606; 25 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P68,285



April 2, 1954 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Nine actions in the district court for Hennepin county, consolidated for trial and heard together on appeal, by Fairview Hospital Association, Asbury Methodist Hospital, Lutheran Deaconess Home, Nicollet Hospitals, Inc., The Northwestern Hospital of Minneapolis, St. Barnabas Hospital, St. Mary's Hospital, The Swedish Hospital, and The Trustees of the Westminster Church to restrain defendant union and its officers from encouraging or participating in a strike of employees in charitable hospitals operated by plaintiffs. The court, Rolf Fosseen, Judge, granted plaintiffs' motion for a temporary injunction, and defendants appealed from the order.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant union sought review of an order from the District Court for Hennepin County (Minnesota), which granted plaintiff employers' individual motions for temporary injunction to prevent the union from causing, promoting, or participating in a strike of the union members who worked at charitable hospitals operated by the employers.


OVERVIEW: Prior to the termination of the parties' individual collective bargaining agreements the union served notices on the employers of its intention to reopen their contracts for modifications and proposed renewal agreements. The parties were unable to reach an agreement and the union filed a strike notice. The union contended that the anti-strike provisions of Minn. Stat. §§ 179.35 to 179.39 were unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the operation of a charitable hospital was a business in which the public had a direct and vital interest. The arbitration provided for in §§ 179.35 to 179.39 was not the result of such an arbitrary, capricious, and unreasonable action on the part of the legislature, or was so inadequate, unreasonable, and lacking in substance as an alternative to the right to strike that the entire act was invalid as violative of due process. The legislature in enacting §§ 179.35 to 179.39 did not arbitrarily and unreasonably discriminate against certain individuals in favor of others. Minn. Stat. § 179.38 was not invalid because of its failure to provide adequate standards for guidance of the arbitrators to be selected.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

704 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. International Harvester Co.


No. 36,143


Supreme Court of Minnesota


241 Minn. 367; 63 N.W.2d 547; 1954 Minn. LEXIS 585; 25 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P68,206



March 5, 1954 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal Dismissed, 348 U.S. 853, 75 S. Ct. 78, 99 L. ed.    .


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal by defendant from a judgment of the municipal court of St. Paul, Ramsey county, James C. Otis, Judge, convicting it of interfering with the election privileges of an employee in violation of M.S.A. 206.21 and 210.11.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a company, sought review of the judgment of the Municipal Court of St. Paul, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which convicted it of interfering with the election privileges of an employee in violation of Minn. Stat. Ann. §§ 206.21 and 210.11 for deducting from the employee's pay two hours of wages when the employee absented himself from work for the purpose of voting in a public election.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's contract with its employees' union provided that employees were to be allowed time off to vote without pay. Defendant contended that the pay-while-you-vote statutes, Minn. Stat. Ann. §§ 206.21 and 210.11, in conjunction with Minn. Stat. Ann. § 610.19, which provided for the punishment of misdemeanors by imprisonment or a fine, were unconstitutional. The court held that the statutes neither interfered with defendant's freedom of contract nor violated due process under either U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 or Minn. Const. art. I, §§ 2, 7, 8, 11, and 13. The statutes were not so unreasonable and unequal in their application to employers of the class to which defendant belonged so as to constitute an unlawful exercise of the police power and a violation of federal or state due process or equal protection provisions. The imposition of a fine pursuant to Minn. Stat. Ann. § 610.19 did not result in the indirect imposition of imprisonment for a debt in violation of Minn. Const. art. I, § 12 because defendant rather was being prosecuted for a breach of a statutory duty as provided under Minn. Stat. Ann. § 210.11.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

705 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Kiges v. St. Paul


No. 35,765


Supreme Court of Minnesota


240 Minn. 522; 62 N.W.2d 363; 1953 Minn. LEXIS 727



December 31, 1953 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the district court for Ramsey county against the city of St. Paul and the mayor, council members, architect, chief of police, and official newspaper of said city to have a building permit held by plaintiff declared valid and to enjoin the enforcement of an ordinance rezoning certain property including the premises of plaintiff. The court, Albin S. Pearson, Judge, found for defendants and ordered a temporary injunction dissolved, and plaintiff appealed from an order denying his motion for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff lot owner sought review of a judgment by the District Court for Ramsey County (Minnesota), which ruled in favor of defendants, a city, a mayor, council members, an architect, and a chief of police, in the owner's action to have a building permit declared valid and to enjoin the enforcement of a ordinance rezoning the owner's property.


OVERVIEW: The owner received a permit to construct a retail cleaning establishment on his lot. After the owner began construction, a petition for rezoning the owner's land was presented to defendants. The owner's permit was then suspended pending the city council's decision on the petition. Two more petitions for rezoning were later filed, following which the city council was advised that further suspension of the owner's permit would be illegal. After the third petition for rezoning was adopted, the owner filed an action to have his building permit declared valid and to enjoin the enforcement of the rezoning ordinance. From an adverse decision, the owner appealed. On appeal, the court held that the expenditures and obligations incurred by the owner from construction during the pendency of the rezoning permit were insufficient to create a right to erect a building in violation of the ordinance. The court stated that the owner had not acquired a vested right of which he could not be deprived. The court found that a letter written to defendants from a city attorney regarding the lack of authority to suspend the owner's construction did not estop defendants from permitting the rezoning.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

706 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Arens v. Rogers


No. 36,056


Supreme Court of Minnesota


240 Minn. 386; 61 N.W.2d 508; 1953 Minn. LEXIS 711



December 4, 1953 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal Dismissed, 347 U.S. 949, 74 S. Ct. 680, 98 L. ed. 1096.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action in the district court for Hennepin county in which plaintiffs, who formerly were licensed to sell intoxicating liquor in defendant village, seek judgment declaring that the statute under which said village operates a municipal liquor store is unconstitutional and requiring that defendant village be enjoined from such operation, that the money lost or illegally spent in such operation be recovered, and that the purchase of plaintiffs' stock be a prerequisite to such operation. The court, Harold N. Rogers, Judge, granted defendant's motion for a summary judgment, and plaintiffs appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, taxpayers on behalf of themselves and all taxpayers, appealed a summary judgment decision in favor of defendant city by the District Court for Hennepin County (Minnesota) in an action to challenge the city's authority to operate a municipal liquor store and the refusal to pay liquor store owners for their equipment as required by Minn. Stat. 340.11, subd. 16.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers claimed that the city could not have operated liquor stores where they operated at a loss and that the owners had not been paid for their equipment as required by § 340.11, subd. 16. The court held that the stores were valid and that the owners were not entitled to be paid because § 340.11, subd. 16 was unconstitutional. The taxpayers had standing to challenge the stores' existence because of a real interest to prevent the city's loss of money in the stores. Minn. Stat. Ann. §§ 340.07, subd. 5, 340.11, subd. 10 were not unconstitutional as special legislation where they only applied to cities of less than 10,000 people because of the justification of insufficient police resources for the private stores and larger cities would have had too many stores. The refusal to renew the owners' licenses was not unconstitutional under the Fourteenth Amendment or Minn. Const. art. I, § 7, despite the legislature's motives, because the owners had no property rights to operate the stores. Without those property rights, the owners had no right to be paid because that would have been the expenditure of public funds for private purposes in violation of Minn. Const. art. IX, § 1.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision in favor of the city.

Kaljuste v. Hennepin County Sanatorium Com.


No. 36,084


Supreme Court of Minnesota


240 Minn. 407; 61 N.W.2d 757; 1953 Minn. LEXIS 712



December 4, 1953 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari upon the relation of Aetna Casualty & Surety Company to review a decision of the industrial commission awarding compensation to Margit Kaljuste, employee, against Hennepin County Sanatorium Commission, employer, and relator, its insurer.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petition for certiorari brought to the Supreme Court of Minnesota to review a decision of the industrial commission awarding, against respondent and its insurer, compensation benefits to petitioner.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner contracted tuberculosis while employed by respondent. A referee awarded compensation benefits to petitioner under Minn. Stat. Ann. § 251.041- 251.045 against respondent and its insurer. The insurer argued that the workmen's compensation policy that it issued did not cover the benefits established under § 251.041 because it was unconstitutional and did not amend or supplement state workmen's compensation law nor was a part of it. The Supreme Court held § 251.041, as amended, was supplemental to, and to that extent a part of, state workmen's compensation law, and therefore the standard workmen's compensation insurance policy issued by the insurer covered the benefits established under § 251.041 as amended. In addition, the court held that § 251.041 was not unconstitutional special or class legislation.


OUTCOME: Affirmed award of workmen's compensation to petitioner because Minn. Stat. Ann. § 251.041- 251.045 was supplemental to, and part of, state workmen's compensation law, and therefore policy covered benefits payable under § 251.041; statute was not unconstitutional special or class legislation.

State ex rel. South St. Paul v. Hetherington


No. 36,051


Supreme Court of Minnesota


240 Minn. 298; 61 N.W.2d 737; 1953 Minn. LEXIS 699



November 13, 1953 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Granted 240 Minn. 298 at 305.


PRIOR HISTORY: Mandamus in the district court for Dakota county upon the relation of South St. Paul, Elmer Culbertson, West St. Paul, and John V. Sperl to enjoin the members of the board of county commissioners of said county from putting into effect a resolution purporting to redistrict the county. The court, B. M. Heinzen, judge of the ninth judicial district acting for the judges of the first judicial district, affirmed the action of the county board and plaintiffs appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Remanded for vacation of judgment and taking of additional evidence.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff cities appealed from a judgment by the District Court for Dakota County (Minnesota), which dismissed an order to show cause in the nature of an alternative writ of mandamus and sustained the action of defendant Board of County Commissioners of Dakota County redistricting a county under Minn. Stat. Ann. § 375.02.


OVERVIEW: The county board proposed to redistrict Dakota county pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 375.02, which required a redistricting whenever one county commissioner district was found to contain 30 percent or more of the population of the county. The cities sought to enjoin the county board adopting a resolution affecting the redistricting, claiming that one of the districts, as redistricted, was not composed of contiguous territory as required by § 375.02. The trial court affirmed the action of the county board, finding that plaintiffs failed to rebut the presumption that the county commissioners acted within the limits of their statutory powers in redistricting the county. Without a showing that the gross disparity in the population of the county commissioner districts was avoidable, the county board exercised proper discretion in compliance with the provisions of § 375.02. On appeal, the court determined that the stipulated facts sustained the trial court's findings. However, the court remanded that case to the trial court to vacate the judgment and to take additional evidence as a basis for an additional finding of whether the gross inequalities in population were unavoidable.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the action for a vacation of the judgment and the taking of additional evidence.

Thomas v. Ramberg


No. 36,005


Supreme Court of Minnesota


240 Minn. 1; 60 N.W.2d 18; 1953 Minn. LEXIS 667; 24 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P67,755



July 10, 1953 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by plaintiff, a retail merchant, from an order of the district court for Hennepin county, Levi M. Hall, Judge, denying his motion to enjoin defendants as commissioners of the industrial commission from taking further action in the matter of fixing minimum rates of pay for women and minors in retail merchandising business and vacating a restraining order contained in an order to show cause.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff retail merchant appealed an order of the district court for Hennepin county (Minnesota), which denied his motion to enjoin defendants, commissioners of the industrial commission, from taking further action in setting the minimum rates of pay for women and minors in retail merchandising business, and which vacated an earlier restraining order contained in an order to show cause.


OVERVIEW: The industrial commission appointed an advisory board with regard to the revision of its minimum wage order pertaining to women and children. The advisory board consisted of three employer representatives, three employee representatives, and three public representatives, all of whom were women. A former commission employee was appointed as one of public representatives. The commission received majority and minority reports, and announced that public hearings would be held on the issue of wages for women and minors. The retail merchant obtained a temporary restraining order to enjoin any action by the commission except to hold public meetings, claiming that the commission exceeded its jurisdiction. The trial court denied his motion for a permanent injunction and vacated the restraining order. On appeal, the court held that the merchant was not entitled to an injunction absent a final agency order, or the exhaustion of his administrative remedies, or the proof of irreparable harm. There was no final order and the merchant had not proven irreparable harm insofar as there was no determination from the commission with regard to the increase, if any, in women's and minors' wages.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

State ex rel. King v. Ruegemer


No. 36,014


Supreme Court of Minnesota


238 Minn. 440; 57 N.W.2d 153; 1953 Minn. LEXIS 576



February 20, 1953 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to review an order of the district court for Todd county, E. J. Ruegemer, Judge, quashing an indictment against George Lehner for the crime of misappropriating money received as a public officer. Said George Lehner moved to discharge the writ.



DISPOSITION: Writ discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved to quash a writ of certiorari that had issued for review of an order quashing the indictment that charged him with misappropriation under Minn. Stat. § 620.01.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a deputy county treasurer, was charged with the crime of misappropriating county funds under Minn. Stat. § 620.01. Defendant moved to quash the indictment, arguing that Minn. The State petitioned for a writ of certiorari to review the order of the trial court. In granting the motion and quashing the writ, the court concluded that Minn. Stat. § 632.10 was convincing evidence of a legislative policy that denied the State the right of review in criminal matters in the absence of defendant's consent. Further, the policy of the court in denying to the State the right to appeal or review in a criminal matter was so long standing that any change in this policy should be done by the legislature and not by the courts.


OUTCOME: The writ of certiorari was quashed.

 

711 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Clarke Plumbing & Heating, Inc.


No. 35,802


Supreme Court of Minnesota


238 Minn. 192; 56 N.W.2d 667; 1952 Minn. LEXIS 769



December 26, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by defendant from a judgment of the municipal court of Minneapolis, Hennepin county, Tom Bergin, Judge, convicting it of violation of an ordinance requiring that a permit be obtained to install a hot water heating system.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant plumbing company sought review of the decision of the Municipal Court of Minneapolis, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which convicted the plumbing company of violating an ordinance requiring a permit to install a hot water heating system. The plumbing company argued that it was unreasonable and unconstitutional to require preparation of the plans by a Registered Professional Engineer because the ordinance detailed the plans' requirements.


OVERVIEW: The plumbing company did not question the city's authority to pass an ordinance that required a permit or plans to install a hot water heating system. The plumbing company did contend that it was unreasonable and unconstitutional to require that a Registered Professional Engineer prepare the plans for the installation of the hot water heating system. The city's ordinance included detailed, complete mechanical requirements and specifications for installation and construction of hot water heating systems. The plumbing company contended that nothing more could be accomplished by requiring the plans to be prepared by a Registered Professional Engineer. The court affirmed the plumbing company's conviction, finding that the city's ordinance was constitutional. Minn. Stat. Ann. § 326.02 required that a professional engineer prepare any plans for structures wherein the public welfare or the safeguarding of life, health, or property was involved. The court concluded that the city's ordinance, which followed the requirements of the state statute, was not unconstitutional for requiring such professional plans for larger heating installations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the municipal court's judgment convicting the plumbing company of violating an ordinance requiring a permit to install a hot water heating system.

 

712 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Duluth


No. 35,794


Supreme Court of Minnesota


238 Minn. 128; 56 N.W.2d 416; 1952 Minn. LEXIS 760



December 5, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two actions by the state in the district court for St. Louis county to collect the costs of the examination of certain financial affairs and records for defendant city. After findings for the state, Victor H. Johnson, Judge, defendant appealed from an order denying its motion for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the State of Minnesota, initiated two actions against defendant, the City of Duluth, in an effort to collect the costs of the examination of certain financial affairs and records of the City, in accordance with 1947 Minn. Laws ch. 634, § 24. The District Court of St. Louis County (Minnesota) entered judgment in favor of the State. The City appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State performed an examination of the financial records of the City. In accordance with 1947 Minn. Laws ch. 634, § 24, the State sought to collect its costs. The City claimed that the State was not entitled to collect any costs in excess of the $ 10 per day permitted for such examinations by Minn. Stat. § 215.21. The trial court entered judgment in favor of the State. In affirming the trial court's judgment, the court held that 1947 Minn. Laws ch. 634, § 24, became as permanent a law as Minn. Stat. § 215.21 upon its enactment. The court further held that 1947 Minn. Laws ch. 634, § 24, was clearly inconsistent with Minn. Stat. § 215.21, inasmuch as it provided for reimbursement of larger fees. Therefore, the court concluded that § 215.21 was repealed by implication. Lastly, the court rejected the City's contention that 1947 Minn. Laws ch. 634, § 24, was unconstitutional. The court so held based on its finding an implied repeal of an act was an effect or result, as opposed to a separate subject; thus, the court found no violation of Minn. Const. art. 4, § 27.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

713 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Bricelyn School Dist. v. Board of County Comm'rs


Nos. 35,630, 35,633


Supreme Court of Minnesota


238 Minn. 63; 55 N.W.2d 602; 1952 Minn. LEXIS 750



November 14, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On reargument opinions in Bricelyn School Dist. v. Board of Co. Commrs. 238 Minn. 53, 55 N.W. (2d) 597, and Frost Independent School Dist. v. Board of Co. Commrs. 238 Minn. 62, 55 N.W. (2d) 602, adhered to.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent county board filed a petition for rehearing after a decision in favor of petitioners, the school district and the county, over the reorganization of school districts. The board argued that 1947 Minn. Laws 421, as amended by 1949 Minn. Laws 666, violated Minn. Const. art. IV, § 27, and that it was entitled to question the constitutionality of such laws.


OVERVIEW: The county board filed a petition for a rehearing after the court found for the school district and the county in district reorganization. The county board contended that it was entitled to question the constitutionality of 1947 Minn. Laws 421, as amended by 1949 Minn. Laws 666 as contrary to Minn. Const. art. IV, § 27. The court granted the rehearing and found that the county board were not entitled to question the constitutionality of the statute because they had no personal or property interest which was being infringed. The only interest of the county board affected by the constitutionality of the reorganization provisions of the statute was its interest in the proper exercise of its official functions. The court held that the public interest in the validity of the two reorganized districts alone did not warrant making an exception to the rule that public officials could not question the constitutionality of a statute, which infringed no personal or property interest of such officials. The court held that its original decision was correct.


OUTCOME: The court ruled that its original decisions were correct.

 

714 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


In re Repair of Cty. Ditch


No. 35,617


Supreme Court of Minnesota


237 Minn. 358; 55 N.W.2d 308; 1952 Minn. LEXIS 731



August 1, 1952 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Granted 237 Minn. 358 at 367.


PRIOR HISTORY: Proceeding in the district court for Faribault county for the repair of county ditch No. 1 of said county, wherein William F. Seidlitz appealed from an order, Chris Carlson, Judge, denying his alternative motion for judgment or a new trial after the return of a verdict assessing benefits of $ 408 against his land.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions to enter judgment for appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner challenged an order of the Faribault County District Court (Minnesota), which denied the landowner's alternative motion for judgment or a new trial after the return of a verdict assessing benefits of $ 408 against his land in an action under Minn. Stat. Ann. § 106.471 for the repair of a county ditch.


OVERVIEW: The landowner was the joint owner of the subject property with his wife. In the repair proceeding the landowner was assessed for benefits to his land. An appeal was taken to the district court, as provided by Minn. Stat. Ann. §§ 106.471, subd. 7(d), and 106.631. The jury in the district court found the land benefited to the extent of $ 408, and the trial court denied the landowner's motion for judgment or a new trial. The landowner appealed, and the court reversed. The court held that the landowner's property was not benefited by the original drainage system, that it did not fall within the purview of the repair proceedings for assessment, and that the legislature intended that benefit of a possible future outlet for a lateral should be left to appropriate proceedings for which it had specifically provided. The court found that the water from the landowner's property flowed in the same direction prior to the construction of county ditch No. 1 and in no greater quantity nor any more freely after the construction than before.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order against the landowner and remanded the case to the district court with instructions to enter judgment for the landowner.

State ex rel. Grozbach v. Common School Dist.


No. 35,798


Supreme Court of Minnesota


237 Minn. 150; 54 N.W.2d 130; 1952 Minn. LEXIS 708



June 17, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Quo warranto in this court upon the relation of Arnold Grozbach to test the validity of the organization of Consolidated School District No. 18, Goodhue county.



DISPOSITION: Writ discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator initiated a proceeding in the nature of quo warranto to test the constitutional validity of the organization of respondent, county school district, and specifically, whether the acts providing for reorganization of school districts were unconstitutional in that they were in violation of Minn. Const. art. 4, § 27.


OVERVIEW: The following questions were raised in the proceedings: were the acts providing for reorganization of school districts unconstitutional in that they were in violation of Minn. Const. art. 4, § 27? Were the acts invalid in that they constituted an unlawful delegation of judicial and legislative power and set up procedures lacking in due process of law? Was the reorganization election invalid? Was the purported assumption of part of the bonded indebtedness of one of the former districts without the authority of the statute and thus invalid? The court discharged the writ and held that the reorganization of school district was proper and according to valid law, and that the questions of assumption of bonded indebtedness were not before the court. The court held that, at least insofar as the acts of 1947 and 1949 provided for a survey, which would ordinarily include a recommendation, they were constitutional. The court held that the acts of 1947 and 1949 were invalid insofar as they related to the reorganization itself, as distinct from a survey.


OUTCOME: The court discharged the relator's proceeding in the nature of quo warranto.

 

716 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Culver v. Nelson


No. 35,595


Supreme Court of Minnesota


237 Minn. 65; 54 N.W.2d 7; 1952 Minn. LEXIS 700



May 29, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the district court for Ramsey county for a declaratory judgment construing the state pharmacy law insofar as it relates to the sale of vitamin products by retail food store dealers. The case was heard before Albin S. Pearson, Judge, who made findings holding that the sale of said products is subject to the state pharmacy law, that they are not authorized to be sold at retail except by licensed pharmacists, and that said law is constitutional as so construed. From the judgment entered, plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff grocer sought review of an order from the District Court for Ramsey County (Minnesota), which entered judgment in favor of defendant state board of pharmacy members (members) in the grocer's suit seeking a declaratory judgment determining the proper construction of Minn. Stat. Ann. § 151 as it related to the sale of vitamin products by retail food store dealers.


OVERVIEW: The grocer brought suit against the members seeking a declaratory judgment determining the proper construction of Minn. Stat. Ann. § 151, which prohibited the grocer from selling retail tablets, capsules, or liquids containing vitamins in their original packages as prepared by the manufacturer or distributor without giving any directions as to their use except such as were given on or in the package in which they were offered for sale. The district court entered judgment in favor of the members. On appeal, the court affirmed. Despite the grocer's argument to the contrary, the court held that the vitamin products involved in the case were drugs within the meaning prescribed by § 151. The court reasoned that the mere fact that they were harmless household remedies did not except the sale of the products from the operation of § 151 unless they were also sold exclusively for non-medicinal purposes. The court further held that § 151 was not so foreign to the protection of public health that it violated the Minn. Const. art. I, § 7 or Minn. Const. art. IV, § 33.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order entering judgment in favor of the members in the grocer's action seeking a declaratory judgment determining the proper construction of a state statute prohibiting the retail sell of tablets, capsules, or liquids containing vitamins.

 

717 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Duluth v. Northland Greyhound Lines


No. 35,735


Supreme Court of Minnesota


236 Minn. 260; 52 N.W.2d 774; 1952 Minn. LEXIS 651



March 28, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the district court for St. Louis county for an injunction to restrain defendant from operating its buses on plaintiff's streets until certain license fees claimed to be due under a city ordinance have been paid, and for the collection of such fees. After findings for defendant, Victor H. Johnson, Judge, plaintiff appealed from the judgment.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the City of Duluth, Minnesota, appealed a judgment of the District Court for St. Louis County (Minnesota), which, after trial without a jury upon stipulated facts, denied the City's request for an injunction to restrain defendant bus company from operating its buses on the City's streets until certain license fees claimed to be due under Duluth, Minn., Ordinance No. 636, §§ 3, 9 had been paid.


OVERVIEW: The bus company argued that, in a series of acts, of which 1949 Minn. Laws 694, § 3, subd. 9 was the current act, the City and other cities similarly situated were deprived of the power to exact a tax or license fee or bond from interurban bus lines. On appeal, the court rejected the City's argument that 1949 act dealt with the taxation of motor vehicles and that the license required by the ordinance was not germane to taxation; the act dealt generally with the regulation of motor vehicles and not with taxation alone. Thus, the title of the act did not violate Minn. Const. art. IV, § 27. The City did not challenge the 1923 predecessor to the 1949 act, which had reenacted the 1923 act without any change in language. Further, the 1949 act dealt with the same subject as the City's ordinance. The 1949 act was germane to the subject expressed in its title. Nor did the 1949 act constitute class legislation in violation of Minn. Const. art. I, § 2, art. IV, § 33, and U.S. Const. amend. XIV; there was a demonstrable reason for the classification in the act. There was no merit to the City's argument that its right to exact the license fee was reserved to it under 1925 Minn. Laws 185, § 18.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

718 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Suess


Nos. 35,575, 35,576


Supreme Court of Minnesota


236 Minn. 174; 52 N.W.2d 409; 1952 Minn. LEXIS 641



March 14, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Defendants were charged by separate informations filed by the county attorney of Morrison county with the offense of spotlighting game in violation of M.S.A. 100.29, subd. 10. Their demurrers to the informations were overruled, W. F. Rogosheske, Judge, and the court certified the questions involved as important and doubtful.



DISPOSITION: As to both informations, first question certified answered in the negative; as to first information, second question certified answered in the affirmative.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court had before it two questions certified per Minn. Stat. Ann. § 632.10. The questions had been certified by the District Court, Morrison County (Minnesota). The questions asked were Minn. Stat. Ann. § 100.29, subd. 10 so general, vague, indefinite, or uncertain that it denied due process of law; and did the information against one of two defendants under Minn. Stat. Ann. § 610.12, or otherwise, state a public offense?


OVERVIEW: Both defendants were charged by separate instruments with a violation of Minn. Stat. Ann. § 100.29, subd. 10, which made it criminal to shine an artificial light in certain areas for spotting, locating, or taking any wild animal, except raccoons when treed with the help of dogs, while having in possession or under control any firearm or other implement by which big game could be killed, except where the firearm was unloaded and properly encased or broken down. The court ruled that § 100.29, subd. 10 was not void for vagueness. The court wrote, inter alia, that § 100.29, subd. 10 was clearly focused at stopping the shining of big-game animals, which in Minnesota practically meant deer. The court also ruled that the term firearm as used in § 100.29, subd. 10 and a phrase "or other implement whereby big game could be killed" were not illegally vague. The phrase according to the court obviously referred to lethal instruments such as bows and arrows that could kill big-game animals. Regarding the information at issue, the court ruled that it sufficiently informed respective defendant about the crime with which he was charged.


OUTCOME: Regarding the criminal information against each defendant, the court wrote that the first question certified was answered in the negative, and, as to the first information, the second question certified was answered in the affirmative.

State ex rel. Paff v. Kelley


No. 35,518


Supreme Court of Minnesota


235 Minn. 350; 50 N.W.2d 703; 1952 Minn. LEXIS 587



January 4, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Mandamus in the district court for Koochiching county upon the relation of Elmo Paff and others as residents and taxpayers of the city of International Falls to enjoin Archie Kelley and others as mayor, city clerk, and the members of the city council (respondents) from issuing more than five "on sale" liquor licenses in said city, the contention of relators being that L. 1937, c. 387 (M.S.A. 340.11, subd. 9), permitting the governing body of certain cities of the fourth class in certain counties of the state to determine the number of "on sale" licenses which may be issued, is unconstitutional as special legislation. Chester Sumner and others as the holders of "on sale" liquor licenses issued by the city pursuant to said statute intervened. On motion of relators for judgment on the pleadings, the court, Arnold C. Forbes, Judge, granted the motion and made findings directing the issuance of a peremptory writ. From the order so made, respondents and interveners appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, a city mayor, city clerk, and city council members, as well as intervenors, the holders of on sale liquor licenses issued by the city pursuant to Minn. Stat. Ann. § 340.11, subd. 9, sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Koochiching County (Minnesota), which granted a motion for mandamus sought by relators, city residents and taxpayers, prohibiting the city from issuing more than five on sale liquor licenses.


OVERVIEW: The city residents and taxpayers sought a writ of mandamus to prohibit the mayor, city clerk, and city council members from issuing more than five on sale liquor licenses upon the contention that Minn. Stat. Ann. § 340.11, subd. 9, which permitted the governing body of certain cities of the fourth class in certain counties of Minnesota to determine the number of on sale licenses which could be issued, was unconstitutional as special legislation. The holders of on sale liquor licenses issued by the city pursuant to said statute intervened. The trial court granted the motion and prohibited the city from issuing more than five on sale liquor licenses as authorized by Minn. Stat. Ann. § 340.11, subd. 4, and Minn. Stat. Ann. § 340.11, subd. 7. The trial court's judgment was affirmed on appeal. The court found that the provisions of Minn. Stat. Ann. § 340.11, subd. 9, under which the licenses involved were issued, were unconstitutional. The court found that the classification attempted in the statute was not germane or relevant to the law.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Fox v. Swartz


No. 35,497


Supreme Court of Minnesota


235 Minn. 337; 51 N.W.2d 80; 1952 Minn. LEXIS 586; 30 A.L.R.2d 739



January 4, 1952 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by George C. Stetson as assignee of a judgment in favor of plaintiff against defendant Joseph Swartz from an order of the district court for Hennepin county, Theodore B. Knudson, Judge, granting the motion of defendant Joseph Swartz to vacate a levy of execution and denying the motion of the assignee for an order directing the sheriff to sell at execution sale under the levy heretofore made said defendant's interest in and to a 15-year insurance endowment policy to satisfy said judgment.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The assignee of plaintiff's judgment appealed from an order of the district court for Hennepin County (Minnesota), granting defendant motion to vacate a levy of execution, and denying the assignee's motion for an order directing the sheriff to sell defendant's interest in an insurance endowment policy on the ground that policy constituted life insurance and was, therefore, exempt from execution under Minn. Stat. Ann. §§ 61.14 and 61.15.


OVERVIEW: The assignee of plaintiff's judgment appealed from order granting defendant's motion to vacate levy of execution, and denying the assignee's motion for an order directing sheriff to sell defendant's interest in an insurance endowment policy that he had purchased six weeks after entry of judgment. The policy had a 15-year maturity date, but if the insured died prior to maturity, it was payable to the insured's wife or son. The trial court had held that policy was exempt under Minn. Stat. Ann. §§ 61.14 and 61.15, which exempted from execution the proceeds of life insurance policies. The assignee argued on appeal that the policy was not life insurance, but rather was an investment or savings contract, and furthermore, argued that if the policy came within scope of Minn. Stat. Ann. §§ 61.14 and 61.15, such an exemption would violate the Minnesota Constitution. The court affirmed the trial court judgment, holding that endowment insurance was life insurance for purposes of Minn. Stat. Ann. §§ 61.14 and 61.15; and that an unreasonable exemption in violation of Minn. Const. art. 1, § 12, did not arise with respect to insurance policy proceeds that were not due and payable to the insured.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court decision, rejecting assignee's arguments that the policy was not life insurance, but rather was an investment or savings contract, and that if the policy came within the scope of the statutory exemption, such an exemption would violate the Minnesota Constitution.

State ex rel. Railroad & Warehouse Com. v. Mees


No. 35,494


Supreme Court of Minnesota


235 Minn. 42; 49 N.W.2d 386; 1951 Minn. LEXIS 744; 27 A.L.R.2d 1197



October 5, 1951 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Proceeding in the district court for Hennepin county upon the petition of the railroad and warehouse commission in the matter of an investigation by the commission into the affairs of the Twin City Rapid Transit Company and its subsidiaries for an order to show cause requiring R. C. Mees, as resident partner and manager of the brokerage firm of Paine, Webber, Jackson & Curtis, to comply with a subpoena duces tecum to produce the books, records, and documents of said firm relating to the names of persons, firms, or corporations who had bought or sold stock or other securities of the transit company and its subsidiaries. William T. Towey, a stockholder of the transit company, intervened, asking that the petition of the commission be dismissed and the subpoena quashed. From an order, Frank E. Reed, Judge, denying the motion of intervener to dismiss the petition, granting the motion of the commission that the complaint in intervention be dismissed, and directing Mees to comply with the command of the subpoena, intervener appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervenor stockholder appealed an order of the District Court for Hennepin County (Minnesota), which denied the stockholder's motion seeking dismissal of the petition brought by petitioner Railroad and Warehouse Commission and granted the Commission's motion, dismissed the complaint in intervention, and ordered the partner to comply with the subpoena.


OVERVIEW: The Commission on its own motion and without issuing a complaint, passed a resolution authorizing an investigation into the control and management of the transit company. The Commission directed a subpoena duces tecum to the resident partner of a brokerage firm. The subpoena ordered the partner to produce all books, records, and documents of the brokerage firm relating to the names of persons, firms, and corporations who bought or sold transit company stock. The partner refused to obey the subpoena. The trial court issued an order to show cause, and the stockholder served on the Commission a complaint in intervention requesting that the petition be dismissed and the subpoena quashed. The court held that: (1) the provision permitting the commission to conduct investigations on its own motion in Minn. Stat. § 216.21, was intended to give the Commission an informal means of aiding the performance of functions not quasi-judicial in nature; and (2) so long as an investigation was for a lawfully authorized purpose and the information sought relevant and material to the investigation, due process was not offended by requiring any person possessed of that information to testify.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

Thomas v. Housing & Redevelopment Authority


No. 35,444


Supreme Court of Minnesota


234 Minn. 221; 48 N.W.2d 175; 1951 Minn. LEXIS 698



May 25, 1951 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Taxpayers' action in the district court for St. Louis county to restrain defendants from proceeding with a low-rent housing development program in the city of Duluth. After findings for defendants, Mark Nolan, Judge, plaintiffs appealed from the judgment.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of a decision of the District Court for St. Louis County (Minnesota) that entered judgment in favor of appellee housing authority in the owners' action to enjoin the authority from proceeding with a program of action intended to culminate in the establishment of a low-rent housing development in conformity with federal and state law.


OVERVIEW: In funding the construction of the housing project, the authority entered into an agreement pursuant to state law that contemplated the taking of land through eminent domain. The agreement also provided for the demolition or compulsory repair of slum areas. The property owners contended that the taking of private land for the use of housing projects did not constitute a public purpose and that providing public housing for low income families was an unconstitutional class legislation. The court found no constitutional violations and affirmed. The court held that: (1) public housing and slum clearance were public uses for which the power of eminent domain might be exercised; (2) the ability to pay and extent of protection or benefit were proper considerations to justify a classification because it was reasonably related to a governmental interest; and (3) the act contemplating the building of low income housing and the redevelopment of slum areas did not embrace more than one subject because the two matters were logically related.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the authority.

 

723 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Hassler v. Engberg


No. 35,328


Supreme Court of Minnesota


233 Minn. 487; 48 N.W.2d 343; 1951 Minn. LEXIS 665



April 6, 1951 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the district court for Ramsey county for a declaratory judgment that Ex. Sess. L. 1933-1934, c. 53, as amended (M.S.A. 69.54), is invalid, that an order of the state commissioner of insurance made pursuant to said act directing the collection of a surcharge of two percent of premiums on fire insurance policies for the benefit of fire department relief associations is null and void, and for certain other relief. After findings for plaintiff, Robert V. Rensch, Judge, defendant Armand W. Harris, as state commissioner of insurance, and interveners appealed from an order denying their motion for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions to amend findings and conclusions in conformity with opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insured instituted an action for a declaratory judgment that Minn. Stat. § 69.54 was invalid and that an order directing the collection of a surcharge on fire insurance policies for the benefit of fire department relief associations was null and void. Appellant commissioner of insurance challenged the decision of the District Court for Ramsey County (Minnesota), which entered a judgment in favor of the insured.


OVERVIEW: The insured argued that he was not required to pay the surcharge as a condition to maintaining his policy in force. The court held that the trial court was correct in concluding that a justiciable controversy did exist, and therefore the action was proper for adjudication. However, the court held that the constitutionality of the tax could be sustained either as a tax on the privilege of the insurance company of writing insurance or as a tax upon the privilege of the property owner insuring his property against the risk of fire. The court concluded that Minn. Stat. § 69.54 was not unconstitutional merely because it imposed a tax upon fire insurance premiums in certain cities of the first class and did not apply to all parts of the state. Therefore, the court reversed the decision of the trial court because § 69.54 was not violative of the uniformity requirements of Minn. Const. art. 9, § 1, or of the due process and equal protection clauses of U.S. Const. Amend. XIV, and it did not unconstitutionally delegate to the trustees of firemen's relief associations in cities of the first class legislative power in contravention of the constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court declaring that a statute authorizing the collection of a surcharge on fire insurance policies for the benefit of fire department relief associations was invalid and that any order directing the collection of the surcharge was null and void.

 

724 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Northern Pump Co. v. So-Called Village of Fridley


No. 35,061


Supreme Court of Minnesota


233 Minn. 442; 47 N.W.2d 204; 1951 Minn. LEXIS 658



March 30, 1951 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original proceeding in supreme court in the nature of quo warranto upon the relation of Northern Pump Company and Northern Ordnance, Inc., to test the validity of the incorporation of the so-called village of Fridley in Anoka county. The matter was referred to the Honorable Kenneth G. Brill, one of the judges of the second judicial district, as referee, to hear and report the evidence and make findings.



DISPOSITION: Writ of ouster ordered as to 48.5 acres inadvertently included in petition; as to remainder of territory sought to be incorporated, writ discharged as to village and its officers.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relators, two business corporations, brought a proceeding in the nature of quo warranto against respondents, a village and it officers, challenging the legality of the incorporation of certain territory as the village by the legal voters of the territory pursuant to 1885 Minn. Laws ch. 145. A referee, appointed to make findings of fact and conclusions of law, determined that a writ of ouster should issue.


OVERVIEW: By inadvertence and mistake, certain acreage already incorporated in a city was included in the territory sought to be incorporated as the village. The referee concluded that a writ of ouster should issue because the mistaken inclusion of the acreage vitiated the incorporation proceeding. On review, the court held that, by including the acreage that was already incorporated in the city, the incorporators had exceeded their delegated legislative authority pursuant to 1885 Minn. Laws ch. 145. Because the area was not included in the proposed village territory by an unreasonable attempt to incorporate unsuitable but otherwise eligible land, the inclusion of the area was void ab initio. The court held that the whole proceeding was not vitiated but that a writ of ouster was to issue as to the area illegally included. The remaining portion of the territory in the village was, as a whole, suburban in character with houses and places of business somewhat scattered. It was not unreasonable for the voters to determine that this area and the undeveloped areas which adjoined the platted areas in the village were suitable for incorporation.


OUTCOME: The court issued a writ of ouster as to the inadvertently included acreage and discharged the writ with respect to the remainder of the village territory.

 

725 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Petition of Dreosch


No. 35,204


Supreme Court of Minnesota


233 Minn. 274; 47 N.W.2d 106; 1951 Minn. LEXIS 640



February 23, 1951 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Northern Natural Gas Company from an order of the district court for Blue Earth county, Chris Carlson, judge of the seventeenth judicial district acting for the judge of the sixth judicial district, granting the motion of the county of Blue Earth to dismiss an appeal to the district court by said company from an order of the county board approving an award of no damages to appellant in connection with the establishment of county ditch No. 78 in said county.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant natural gas company challenged an order from the District Court for Blue Earth County (Minnesota), which granted the motion of appellee county to dismiss the company's appeal from an order of the board of county commissioners approving an award of no damages to the company in connection with the establishment of a drainage ditch.


OVERVIEW: The company owned, operated, and maintained a natural gas pipeline system. When the county proposed a new drainage ditch that crossed the company's main pipeline in three points and made it necessary for the company to alter or reconstruct the pipeline, the company sought compensation. The board approved a viewer's report awarding no damages to the company, and the company appealed. The district court dismissed the company's appeal finding that it was the company's uncompensated duty to reconstruct its pipeline to accommodate itself to the ditch. The court reversed the district court's order. In view of caselaw precedent, there was no question that the county in establishing the ditch was exercising its delegated power of eminent domain. Although the company did not own the fee title to the real estate involved, it did own an easement in the land, and an easement was property that when taken for public use entitled the owner to compensation. Clearly, there was a taking or damaging of the company's property for a public use. Thus, compensation was required.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order, which dismissed the company's appeal from the board's order approving an award of no damages to the company in connection with the establishment of a drainage ditch.

 

726 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Gustafson v. Holm


No. 35,430


Supreme Court of Minnesota


232 Minn. 118; 44 N.W.2d 443; 1950 Minn. LEXIS 735



October 5, 1950 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application to this court by order to show cause upon the application of Chester G. W. Gustafson requiring respondent as secretary of state to place petitioner's name upon the ballot at the November 7, 1950, general election as a candidate for the office of associate justice of the supreme court.



DISPOSITION: Order to show cause discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner candidate applied for an order to show cause directing respondent, the Minnesota Secretary of State, to place the candidate's name upon the ballot at the general election as a candidate for the office of associate justice of the supreme court.


OVERVIEW: The candidate, the incumbent, and another stood for election to associate justice of the supreme court. Two other supreme court associate justice offices were also in contention at this election. One other incumbent was opposed by another candidate, and one other incumbent was unopposed. In the primary election the candidate tallied the least number of votes out of the six candidates for the three offices, and as a result his name was omitted from the general election ballot. In denying the relief the candidate sought, the court held that Minn. Stat. § 205.82, which for the first time governed an election, was not unconstitutional. The court held that the system of offices recognized by § 205.82 was not prohibited by Minn. Const. art. VI, §§ 2 or 3. Thus the court rejected the candidate's contention that all the candidates ran against each other, in which case the candidate would still have been entitled to a spot on the ballot. The court also held that Minn. Stat. § 205.82 did not offend the constitution by requiring the word "incumbent" to be placed alongside the incumbent's name on the ballot.


OUTCOME: The court discharged the order to show cause.

Oscar P. Gustafson Co. v. Minneapolis


No. 34,824


Supreme Court of Minnesota


231 Minn. 271; 42 N.W.2d 809; 1950 Minn. LEXIS 690



May 26, 1950 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the district court for Hennepin county for a judgment restraining defendant city and its inspector of buildings from enforcing an ordinance requiring plaintiff to remove an advertising sign overhanging the sidewalk in front of its place of business in the city of Minneapolis, and decreeing said ordinance to be invalid. From an order, Arthur W. Selover, Judge, sustaining defendants' separate demurrers to the complaint, plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff company appealed an order of the District Court for Hennepin County (Minnesota), which sustained separate demurrers to the complaint by defendants, a city and its building inspector, in the company's action for a judgment restraining the city and its building inspector from enforcing an ordinance requiring the company to remove an advertising sign.


OVERVIEW: The company operated a retail jewelry and optical business and under the terms of its lease, the company had the right to hang and display an advertising sign over the sidewalk in front of the business. The common council of the city adopted an ordinance by the terms of which the company was required to remove the sign from the building. The city and the building inspector demurred to the complaint. The trial court denied relief to the company and sustained the demurrers to the complaint. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the ordinance was passed in the exercise of the city's police power and was valid.

728 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


North Star Army & Navy Store, Inc. v. Clark


No. 35,029


Supreme Court of Minnesota


231 Minn. 55; 42 N.W.2d 414; 1950 Minn. LEXIS 659; 85 U.S.P.Q. (BNA) 218



April 28, 1950 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the district court for Ramsey county under the declaratory judgments act to have M.S.A. 333.17 (L. 1945, c. 212) declared unconstitutional, and for certain other relief. From an order sustaining a demurrer to the complaint, Royden S. Dane, Judge, plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff business owners appealed an order from the District Court for Ramsey County sustaining a demurrer to the complaint. The action was brought under the declaratory judgments act to have Minn. Stat. § 333.17 declared unconstitutional, and for certain other relief.


OVERVIEW: The business owners alleged they were engaged in the selling of merchandise known as army and navy goods as well as war surplus goods. They alleged that the attorney general was threatening to terminate their corporate existence and to bring criminal prosecutions against them unless they deleted from the business names the words "Army" and "Navy." They contended that Minn. Stat. § 333.17 was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the sustaining of the demurrer to the business owners' complaint. The corporations were organized after the adoption of the statute that was here attacked. There was no basis for a claim by them of invalidity of the statute on the ground that it impaired contract obligations. The statute prohibited the use of the words "Army," "Navy," and other words that were officially used to designate the United States government as the name or designation of any business. A violation of the Fourteenth Amendment would depend upon whether there was any rational basis for the action of the legislature. The court held that there was a rational basis for the enactment of the statute involved, and that the provisions of the act were not unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order sustaining the demurrer to the business owners' complaint in an action brought under the declaratory judgments act to have a statute declared unconstitutional.

 

729 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Northern P. R. Co. v. Rush City


No. 35,015


Supreme Court of Minnesota


230 Minn. 144; 40 N.W.2d 886; 1950 Minn. LEXIS 593



January 27, 1950 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by plaintiff from a judgment of the district court for Chisago county, Alfred P. Stolberg, Judge, setting aside an order of the railroad and warehouse commission granting the petition of plaintiff for authority to abandon a grade crossing over its tracks in defendant village.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff railroad sought review of a judgment from the District Court for Chisago County (Minnesota),which set aside an order of the railroad and warehouse commission that granted the railroad petition to abandon a grade crossing over its tracks in defendant village.


OVERVIEW: The village, with a population around 1,000 people, was located on the main line of the railroad, which ran in a north-south direction through the village. There were three highway grade crossings over the tracks, one of which the railroad sought to eliminate. At the district court hearing, the village representatives unanimously testified against elimination of the track, pointing out that the track divided the village in half and would have a substantial effect on traffic and business. The railroad argued that the crossing was a hazard. The district court reversed the commission's order allowing the elimination of the crossing. The court held that the district court's finding, that the evidence did not support the commission's decision, was not arbitrary or capricious. The court agreed that the bulk of the evidence argued against the elimination and the claim of a safety hazard could be applied to any railroad crossing in a city center.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's decision that set aside the commission's order.

 

730 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Minneapolis S. R. Co. v. Minneapolis


No. 34,935


Supreme Court of Minnesota


229 Minn. 502; 40 N.W.2d 353; 1949 Minn. LEXIS 636



December 16, 1949 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal Dismissed by U.S. Supreme Court March 13, 1950.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action in the district court for Hennepin county under the declaratory judgments act to determine the validity of an amendatory ordinance of the city of Minneapolis increasing the annual license fee for each of plaintiff's streetcars from $ 25 to $ 100. From a judgment on the pleadings in favor of plaintiff, Levi M. Hall, Judge, defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city sought review of the decision of the District Court for Hennepin County (Minnesota), which entered judgment on the pleadings in favor of plaintiff street railway and held that an ordinance that purported to amend an earlier street railway franchise grant by increasing the annual license fee for each streetcar was invalid and void.


OVERVIEW: The street railway argued that the ordinance was unconstitutional because it impaired the obligation of a contract alleged to have arisen out of the original grant by the city and in that it worked a deprivation of property without due process of law. The court first held that the amendment to the ordinance constituted a valid amendment of the contractual relation between the city and the street railway. The necessary question was what powers, if any, the city possessed and which could have been exercised without impairing the obligations of the contract embodied in two prior ordinances. The court concluded that the city was possessed of police powers sufficiently broad to authorize the regulation of all forms of vehicular traffic upon its streets. The court also found no merit in the implied assumption that the exercise by the city of a licensing power for police regulation was necessarily inconsistent with the preservation of the street railway's franchise privileges. The legislative intent was to provide the city with the right to make the regulation. Therefore, the ordinance constituted a valid exercise of the city's police power.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that had held that the ordinance was invalid and void.

 

731 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Wojahn v. Halter


No. 35,060


Supreme Court of Minnesota


229 Minn. 374; 39 N.W.2d 545; 1949 Minn. LEXIS 620



November 4, 1949 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application to this court by order to show cause upon the relation of Harry Faul, directed to the Honorable Albert H. Enersen, judge of the district court for Cottonwood county, and to Nick J. Bell, sheriff of said county, why a writ of habeas corpus should not issue to secure relator's release from imprisonment for contempt of court.



DISPOSITION: Ordered that writ of habeas corpus issue and that relator be forthwith discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Realtor seller filed a petition seeking a writ of habeas corpus on the grounds that the lower court erred by imprisoning the seller for failure to pay a debt as ordered by the lower court.


OVERVIEW: The seller entered into an agreement whereby he would pay the buyers the sum of $ 800 in settlement of a suit. The seller failed to make the deposit and was found in contempt of court. The seller was imprisoned. The seller filed a petition seeking a writ of habeas corpus. The buyers and the judge argued that the court lacked jurisdiction because the seller was required to bring the writ in the lower court first. It was also alleged that the court lacked jurisdiction because the seller had a remedy available to him. First, the court held that it had original jurisdiction over writs of habeas corpus. Second, the court held that the seller was not required to sit in prison waiting on the slow appeal process. Next, the court held that the seller's incarceration was unlawful because Minn. Const. art. 1, § 12, prohibited incarceration for the failure to pay a debt on a contract. The court noted that the seller's action did not constitute disobedience of the lower court's order because a lawful order or decree presupposed authority on the part of the court to make it. The order imprisoning the seller was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of habeas corpus and discharged the seller.

 

732 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Dayton Co. v. Carpet, L. & R. F. D. Union


No. 34,893


Supreme Court of Minnesota


229 Minn. 87; 39 N.W.2d 183; 1949 Minn. LEXIS 595; 24 L.R.R.M. 2228; 16 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P65,252



June 24, 1949 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal Dismissed by U.S. Supreme Court March 13, 1950.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action in the district court for Hennepin county to enjoin defendants from engaging in a strike as the result of a labor dispute between defendants and their employer, The Dayton Company. After findings for plaintiff, Paul W. Guilford, Judge, defendants appealed from the judgment.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant union sought review of a judgment by the District Court for Hennepin County (Minnesota) that awarded plaintiff employer permanent injunctive relief in the employer's action to enjoin the union from engaging in a strike as a result of a labor dispute.


OVERVIEW: The employer hired three non-union employees but refused to compel them to apply for membership in the union. Union representatives threatened to strike, and the employer sought injunctive relief to avoid a complete shutdown. Upon trial a permanent injunction was granted. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment and held that the employer was entitled to injunctive relief because the union threatened to violate and would have violated Minn. Stat. § 179.42, which declared that it was an unfair labor practice for a union to strike for the purpose of coercing an employer to persuade employees to join or refrain from joining any labor union. The court further determined that § 179.42 did not violate Minn. Const. art. I, §§ 2, 3 and U.S. Const. amends. XIII, XIV. The court reasoned that there was no constitutional reason why the State was not entitled to provide laws for enjoining a strike that had for its purpose a plan to compel or coerce an employer to violate the law. Furthermore, the court reasoned that Minn. Stat. § 179.42 did not violate free speech protections because the statute preserved free speech for all employees, not only those who chose to join a union.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment enjoining the union from engaging in a strike.

Gale v. Commissioner of Taxation


No. 34,889


Supreme Court of Minnesota


228 Minn. 345; 37 N.W.2d 711; 1949 Minn. LEXIS 651



May 27, 1949 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Reported at: 228 Minn. 345 at 352.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of April 29, 1949, Reported at: 1949 Minn. LEXIS 559.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A motion for rehearing was filed in a case that challenged the constitutionality of Minn. Stat. § 290.67.


OVERVIEW: The court's previous opinion failed to include a consideration of respondent's argument that 1945 Minn. Laws ch. 596, § 4, Minn. Stat. § 290.67, which deferred the application of the tax formula contained in Minn. Stat. § 290.33 to those taxable years that actually began after December 31, 1944, resulted in discrimination between taxpayers in violation of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Minn. Const. art. IX, § 1. The court noted that respondent also sought to invoke the provisions of 1945 Minn. Laws ch. 596, § 1, subd. 4 to secure the benefit of a tax computation based on a 50 percent long-term capital assets income gain rather than one of 100 percent. The court held that: (1) the Legislature could prescribe a condition or limitation governing the time when a right to a more advantageous basis of tax computation became available; and (2) respondent could not assail the constitutionality of one provision of an act and rely the validity of another portion of the act in the same proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion for rehearing.

State ex rel. Stanchfield v. Salisbury

Supreme Court of Minnesota


228 Minn. 367; 37 N.W.2d 444; 1949 Minn. LEXIS 562



April 29, 1949 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information in the nature of quo warranto in this court upon the relation of Dale M. Stanchfield and others, as residents and taxpayers of the city of Minneapolis and duly elected aldermen and members of the city council, on behalf of themselves and others similarly situated, directed to respondent, Emmett D. Salisbury, to test his right to hold the position of director of the board of education of the city, to which he had been appointed by the board.



DISPOSITION: Writ of ouster issued.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, members of the Minneapolis city council, sought a writ of quo warranto to determine the right of respondent school director to sit as a member of the school board where he was not appointed to that position by the city council in compliance with the city charter.


OVERVIEW: After being elected to congress, the new congressman resigned his position as a member of the school board. Thereafter, the board of education held an election to fill the vacancy, and the newly-elected member took his position as a school director on the board. Thereafter, members of the city council instituted a proceeding in quo warranto to determine the right of the school director to sit as a member of the city board of education, contending that Minn. Ann. § 125.03 was not applicable to the board of education of the City of Minneapolis so as to authorize it to fill vacancies on its school board because the school district was organized under special laws, the provisions of which were incorporated into the city charter. Under 1887 Minn. Sp. Laws ch. 10 and Minneapolis, Minn., Charter ch. 2, § 19 (1920), the power to fill vacancies on the school board was vested in the city council.


OUTCOME: A writ of ouster was issued.

 

735 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Meyer


No. 34,969


Supreme Court of Minnesota


228 Minn. 286; 37 N.W.2d 3; 1949 Minn. LEXIS 552



April 14, 1949 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Upon information filed in the district court for Sibley county, defendant was charged with the crime of burglary in the third degree and pleaded guilty thereto. Counsel for defendant objected to the imposition of sentence pursuant to L. 1947, c. 595 (M.S.A. 260.125), the Youth Conservation Act, on the ground of its unconstitutionality, and the court, Joseph J. Moriarty, Judge, with the consent of defendant and the state, certified the question involved to the supreme court pursuant to M.S.A. 632.10.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions to impose sentence in accordance with the law.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, pleaded guilty to a charge of burglary in the third degree. Defendant objected to having a sentence imposed pursuant to the Youth Conservation Act, Minn. Stat. § 260.125 (1947) contending that the Act was unconstitutional. The trial court held that the Act was unconstitutional and certified the issue of the Act's constitutionality to the court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that the Youth Conservation Act was unconstitutional. The Act created a Youth Conservation Commission and required trial courts to commit juvenile offenders to the Commission. The Commission had the right to control juveniles committed to it, to place juveniles on probation, and to decide when juveniles would be discharged. On appeal, the court held that the Act was constitutional. The court held: (1) the Act did not violate Minn. Const. art. 4, § 27, which provided that no law shall embrace more than one subject which shall be expressed in its title; (2) the Act did not violate the separation of powers of the three branches of government, did not invade the judicial powers vested in the courts, and did not deprive the courts of their inherent powers; (3) defendant could not challenge a provision of the Act that provided that a discharge by the Commission had the effect of setting aside the conviction because defendant had not been discharged; (4) the Act did not infringe upon the constitutional powers of the state board of pardons; and (5) the Act did not violate defendant's due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and remanded the cause with directions to impose sentence in accordance with the Act.

Lee v. Delmont


No. 34,735


Supreme Court of Minnesota


228 Minn. 101; 36 N.W.2d 530; 1949 Minn. LEXIS 531



March 18, 1949

Streeter, and George Anctil, constituting the state board of barber examiners, from a judgment of the district court for Ramsey county, Clayton Parks, Judge, declaring M.S.A. 154.065 and 154.07 unconstitutional and enjoining the enforcement thereof by said defendants.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant members of the State Board of Barber Examiners appealed a judgment of the District Court for Ramsey County (Minnesota) that was made in favor of plaintiffs, an operator of a barbering school and an operator of a barber college. The trial court enjoined enforcement by the Board of Minn. Stat. Ann. §§ 154.065, 154.07 and declared those laws to be unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Of two instructors employed by the owner of the barbering school, one was not certified per the qualifications enumerated in Minn. Stat. Ann. § 154.065. Minn. Stat. Ann. § 154.07 provided that in barbering schools there was to be one certified instructor to every 15 students. The Board demanded that he limit enrollment to 15 students. The trial court ruled that when taken together the two statutes were not necessary or appropriate to protect public health, safety, or welfare and were not substantially related to the protection of public health, safety, or welfare. The court did not agree with the trial court's ruling that the statutes at issue were unconstitutional. The court held that Minn. Stat. Ann. §§ 154.07, 154.065 reasonably tended to accomplish safeguarding public health and welfare without going beyond the reasonable demands of the occasion and did not contravene the U.S. Const. amend. XIV or Minn. Const. art. I, §§ 2, 7. The court also ruled the regulatory power given to the Board was not a delegation of legislative power that violated the Minn. Const. art. III.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

Bowman v. Moorhead


No. 34,873


Supreme Court of Minnesota


228 Minn. 35; 36 N.W.2d 7; 1949 Minn. LEXIS 522; 7 A.L.R.2d 1401



February 18, 1949 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Taxpayer's action in the district court for Clay county to have the revised charter of defendant city declared void and to enjoin and restrain the city from issuing certain bonds in excess of the debt limit prescribed by the original charter. From a judgment for defendant on the pleadings declaring the revised charter valid, Byron R. Wilson, Judge, plaintiff appealed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of a judgment from the District Court for Clay County (Minnesota), which granted judgment for appellee city on the pleadings in an action brought by the taxpayer to declare the revised city charter void. IV, § 36 in the adoption of the amended charter invalidated it when challenged in this action by the taxpayer.


OVERVIEW: The board of freeholders presented a proposed revision of the original charter. The taxpayer sought to distinguish between defects caused by failure to fulfill requirements of incorporation contained in art. IV, § 36, and mere failure to comply with the statutory prerequisite as the "color of law" under which the revision took place. The court held that the City was at least a valid de facto government and the City had made a bona fide attempt to revise its charter. The court held that the attempted distinction by the taxpayer was not borne out by the cases.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
