Breimhorst v. Beckman


Nos. 34,723, 34,727


Supreme Court of Minnesota


227 Minn. 409; 35 N.W.2d 719; 1949 Minn. LEXIS 496



January 14, 1949 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the district court for Scott county to recover damages for disfigurement suffered by plaintiff as the result of an explosion in the course of her part-time employment as a waitress by defendant John G. Andrist on premises rented by him from the defendant William Beckman. The case was tried before Joseph J. Moriarty, Judge, and a jury. At the close of the evidence the court granted the motion of defendant Beckman for a directed verdict, and the jury returned a verdict for plaintiff against defendant Andrist for $ 3,577.80. Plaintiff appealed from an order denying her motion for a new trial as to defendant Beckman (No. 34,727), and defendant Andrist appealed from an order denying his alternative motion for judgment or a new trial (No. 34,723).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as to defendant Beckman; reversed as to appeal of defendant Andrist with directions to enter judgment in his favor.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee instituted an action against defendant employer and landowner for personal injuries. The employee and the employer appealed from the decision of the Scott County District Court (Minnesota), which entered a judgment in favor of the employee in her action against the employer and granted the landowner's motion for a directed verdict.


OVERVIEW: The employee sought to recover for injuries she received as the result of an explosion in the course of her part-time employment as a waitress on the premises of the landowner. The court held that the trial court was not in error in directing a verdict for the landlord or in denying the employee's motion for a new trial because there is no evidence that the landowner had any actual knowledge of the existence of the spring gun as an instrumentality for the discharge of a dangerous explosive or shell. The court further held that there was no basis for a finding that the landowner ought reasonably to have known or suspected a concealed danger.The court also held that because the employment clearly was the sole factor in exposing the employee to the blast of the shotgun shell when she accidentally tripped the firing mechanism in reaching for a towel, this was a compensable workmen's compensation injury. The court concluded that because the employee had a remedy available under workmen's compensation, the employer was entitled to a judgment in his favor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision denying the employee's motion for a new trial as against the landowner and the court reversed the trial court's decision denying the employer's motion for judgment non obstante or a new trial is reversed with directions to enter judgment in the employer's favor.

Bengtson v. Setterberg


No. 34,382


Supreme Court of Minnesota


227 Minn. 337; 35 N.W.2d 623; 1949 Minn. LEXIS 490



January 7, 1949 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the district court for Lyon county under the declaratory judgments act for a determination of the respective rights of plaintiffs and defendant Esther Bengtson Setterberg in certain homestead property, the fee to which had been assigned to their mother by the final decree of distribution in the matter of the estate of Carl Gustaf Bengtson, their father. After findings, A. B. Gislason, Judge, that the final decree of the probate court was conclusive on all the parties and that the district court was without jurisdiction of the parties and the subject matter of the litigation, plaintiffs appealed from an order denying their motion for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff children appealed a judgment from the District Court, in Lyon County (Minnesota), which denied their petition for a declaratory judgment against defendant daughter and defendant husband to correct the final decree of the probate court of their father's estate that gave to his wife the homestead in fee. No appeal was ever taken from the probate court's order.


OVERVIEW: The probate court by its order erroneously in its decree of distribution assigned to the widow of the intestate the homestead in fee when it should have been decreed to her only for life, and by the current action the children sought to set aside that decree of the probate court. On the other hand they claimed that the real estate of the intestate under the laws of descent and distribution vested in the heirs immediately upon the death of the intestate and that the probate court had no power to change the descent of such property by its decree. The daughter and husband contended that the decree, even though erroneous, was binding on all parties interested in the estate. The court affirmed the denial of the declaratory judgment. The probate court's final decree assigning the fee to the wife, even though erroneous, was binding and conclusive on all those interested in the estate. The probate court's decree was entitled to res judicata because it had jurisdiction over the homestead.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that had denied the petition by the children for a declaratory judgment against the daughter and the husband to correct the final decree of the probate court of their father's estate that gave to his wife the homestead in fee.

 

740 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. One Oldsmobile Two-Door Sedan


No. 34,709


Supreme Court of Minnesota


227 Minn. 280; 35 N.W.2d 525; 1948 Minn. LEXIS 671



December 31, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Proceeding by the state in the district court for Morrison county to confiscate an automobile used by one Marvin Bollig to spot deer contrary to law, wherein Lake Region Beverage Company, a copartnership, by J. N. Bollig, as one of the partners and individually, intervened. There were findings, Byron R. Wilson, Judge, that Marvin Bollig was the owner of the car in question; that interveners had no title thereto and no lien thereon; that the car was used in violation of law to spot deer; and that it be confiscated. From the judgment entered, Marvin Bollig and the intervening defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a driver and a partnership, sought review of the judgment of the District Court for Morrison County (Minnesota), which granted the State's in rem application under Minn. Stat. Ann. § 97.50, subd. 2 (1945) to confiscate the driver's car upon findings that he was the owner of the vehicle and that he had used the car to spot deer at night in violation of Minn. Stat. § 100.29, subd. 1(10) (1945).


OVERVIEW: On appeal from the adverse judgment, the driver and the partnership argued that the driver was not the owner of the vehicle and that Minn. Stat. Ann. §§ 97.50, subd. 2 and 100.29 subd. 1(10) (1945) were unconstitutional because the statute was altered between its enactment and approval by the governor. In affirming, the court ruled that registration of a motor vehicle to the driver was prima facie, but not conclusive, evidence that he was the owner thereof. The court found that, although the purchase money came from one of the partners, it was presumed to have been donated to the driver, who was the partner's minor son. The court also found from the circumstances of the vehicle's purchase and registration that the intent of all involved was for the driver to own the vehicle. The court declined to decide the constitutionality of the statute involved but noted that the statute had repealed Minn. Stat. § 100.057 (1941), which had provided a procedure for confiscation of automobiles used for spotlighting deer similar to Minn. Stat. Ann. § 97.50, subd. 2 (1945), and that the repeal would have been ineffective if § 97.50, subd. 2 was unconstitutionally enacted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

741 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Bridgie v. Koochiching County


No. 34,785


Supreme Court of Minnesota


227 Minn. 320; 35 N.W.2d 537; 1948 Minn. LEXIS 675



December 31, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the district court for Koochiching county by the towns of Bridgie, Evergreen, Pine Top, and Engelwood and by W. G. Ungerecht, a resident and taxpayer of the town of Bridgie and chairman of its board of supervisors, to enjoin the county of Koochiching, its board of county commissioners, and its auditor and treasurer from putting into effect a resolution passed by the board dissolving the plaintiff towns. From an order, J. J. Hadler, Judge, sustaining defendants' demurrer to the complaint, plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court for Koochiching County (Minnesota) sustained the demurrer of defendants, county and county officers, to plaintiff towns' action to enjoin defendants from implementing a resolution to dissolve the towns. The towns appealed.


OVERVIEW: The towns challenged the power of the legislature to enact Minn. Stat. §§ 368.47 to 368.49 upon the grounds that the legislature exceeded its authority and violated Minn. Const., art. 1, § 7 due process clause. The towns alleged that the statutes providing for the dissolution of towns whose assessed value was below $ 40,000 violated Minn. Const. art. 4 §§ 33 and 34 prohibitions against special legislation and Minn. Const. art. 3, § 1 prohibition of delegation of power. The court held that the challenged statutes did not violate any provisions of the Minnesota Constitution and that the legislature did not exceed its authority in enacting the legislation. The legislature was authorized to delegate to county legislative bodies the power to act in connection with the dissolution of towns falling below certain standards of classification. The classification based upon assessed valuation bore a direct relationship to the objects of the legislation. The towns had no rights, privileges, or immunities against legislative interference or control.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that sustained the demurrer of the county and the county officials to the towns' action to enjoin the implementation of a resolution to dissolve the towns.

 

742 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Bergin v. Fitzsimmons


No. 34,802


Supreme Court of Minnesota


226 Minn. 557; 33 N.W.2d 854; 1948 Minn. LEXIS 631



August 3, 1948 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Appeal from Clerk's Taxation of Costs Affirmed.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application to the district court for Hennepin county by Tom Bergin, directed to Robert F. Fitzsimmons as county auditor, requiring the latter to accept the filing of petitioner as a candidate for the office of court commissioner of Hennepin county at the November 1948 general election or show cause why he should not do so. The auditor refused to accept petitioner's filing fee, contending that there was no election for court commissioner in the year 1948, and he and intervener, the incumbent of the office, prayed that the order to show cause be discharged. Upon hearing, the court, Levi M. Hall, Judge, discharged the order to show cause, and petitioner appealed from the order.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator applicant obtained an order to show cause directing respondent county auditor to accept his affidavit of candidacy for the office of court commissioner. The county auditor and intervenor, the incumbent, prayed that the order to show cause be discharged. The District Court for Hennepin County (Minnesota) discharged the order to show cause. The applicant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A court commissioner was elected at the 1946 general election. He died while holding office and the district court appointed intervenor to fill the vacancy. Relator presented an affidavit of candidacy for the office to the county auditor and tendered the filing fee. The auditor refused to accept the affidavit or fee on the ground that there was no election for court commissioner in 1948 and that the intervenor's successor had to be elected at the general election in the year 1950 for the regular four-year term. Relator obtained an order to show cause directing the auditor to accept his affidavit and fee or to show cause why he should not do so. After a hearing, the district court denied the relief sought. On appeal, the court affirmed. The election of court commissioners and the mode of filling vacancies in that office were governed by Minn. Stat. Ann. §§ 489.01 and 489.05. The court noted that the legislature carried into Minn. Stat. Ann. § 489.01 the provisions of an earlier enactment stating that 1918 served as the base year for determining the four-year intervals at which county officers would be elected. Thus, there could be no election of such officers during the year 1948.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying relator the relief sought and dismissing the proceeding.

 

743 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


George Benz Sons v. Ericson


No. 34,703


Supreme Court of Minnesota


227 Minn. 1; 34 N.W.2d 725; 1948 Minn. LEXIS 634



July 30, 1948 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied 227 Minn. 1 at 21.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action in the district court for Ramsey county to restrain defendant as state liquor control commissioner from enforcing the provisions of L. 1947, c. 528, § 1, clause (c), as applied to plaintiff and interveners, manufacturers and wholesalers of intoxicating liquor, pending decision of the constitutionality of said statute. From an order, Gustavus Loevinger, Judge, denying their motion for a temporary injunction and vacating a restraining order theretofore issued, plaintiff and interveners appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff and intervenors, all liquor manufacturers and wholesalers, appealed from an order of the District Court for Ramsey County (Minnesota) that denied their motion for a temporary injunction and vacated a restraining order theretofore issued. The liquor manufacturers and wholesalers sought to restrain defendant state liquor control commissioner from enforcing the provisions of Minn. Stat. § 340.11, subd. 12(c).


OVERVIEW: The liquor manufacturers and wholesalers asserted that the statutory amendment, Minn. Stat. § 340.11, subd. 12(c), was unconstitutional because it violated the due process clause of Minn. Const. art. 1, § 7 and of Minn. Const. art. 4, § 33, insofar as that section prohibited class or special legislation. The statute separated wholesale dealers in wine from wholesale dealers in hard liquor and did not permit any wholesale dealer in either of these types of liquor from dealing in the other. On appeal, the court reversed the order below. The court noted that the mere fact that the legislature had created a classification in the liquor industry did not in itself make the law constitutionally offensive. However, the court ruled that a statute which attempted to regulate and control the liquor industry by merely separating the wine and liquor businesses at the manufacturing or wholesale level, and which did nothing about separating the same businesses at the retail level, was both arbitrary and unreasonable. The court held that the amendment violated the equal protection clauses of the state and federal constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that denied the motion of the liquor manufacturers and wholesalers for a temporary injunction and vacated a restraining order issued against the state liquor control commissioner.

 

744 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Loew v. Hagerle Bros.


No. 34,668


Supreme Court of Minnesota


226 Minn. 485; 33 N.W.2d 598; 1948 Minn. LEXIS 621



July 2, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari upon the relation of Julius Schmahl, state treasurer, as custodian of the special compensation fund, to review an order of the industrial commission awarding compensation to Peter Loew, employe, payable out of such fund.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator state treasurer, as custodian of a special compensation fund, sought certiorari to review an order of the Industrial Commission (Minnesota), which awarded compensation to respondent employee payable out of the special compensation fund pursuant to Minn. Stat. Ann. § 176.13, as amended by 1947 Minn. Laws, ch. 247.


OVERVIEW: The employee suffered a compensable accident that resulted in permanent total disability. He was paid compensation up to the maximum amount. The legislature then enacted 1941 Minn. Laws, ch. 247, which modified Minn. Stat. Ann. § 176.13(b) by providing that all employees who were totally and permanently disabled for a period of 20 years prior to passage but whose weekly compensation payments terminated in a certain six-month period were entitled to payments from a special compensation fund. The amendment was admittedly drawn to extend the benefits of § 176.13 to the employee and it applied to no other person. The state treasurer challenged the Industrial Commission's order allowing the employee compensation from the fund. The court reversed the order. The treasurer had standing to challenge the amendment, as it was a matter of public interest. The amendment violated the prohibition against special legislation set forth in Minn. Const. art. IV, § 33. The classification created by the amendment was fanciful, arbitrary, and wholly lacking in substance. It was so exacting and arbitrary as to constitute nothing more than an effort to identify the employee without using his name.


OUTCOME: The court discharged the writ and reversed the order of the Industrial Commission.

 

745 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Anderson v. St. Paul


Nos. 34,163, 34,436


Supreme Court of Minnesota


226 Minn. 186; 32 N.W.2d 538; 1948 Minn. LEXIS 585



May 7, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the district court for Ramsey county against the city of St. Paul, its mayor, commissioner of public safety, and chief of police to restrain, on the ground of unconstitutionality, the enforcement of a city ordinance prohibiting women from acting as bartenders in "on sale" liquor establishments. From an order (No. 34,163), Carlton McNally, Judge, denying plaintiff's motion for a temporary injunction and dissolving a temporary restraining order, and from a judgment dismissing the action (No. 34,436), Albin S. Pearson, Judge, plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff female bartender appealed the order of the District Court for Ramsey County (Minnesota), which denied her motion for a temporary injunction and dissolved a temporary restraining order she had obtained. The female bartender challenged St. Paul, Minn., Ordinance No. 8604(e)(1945), which prohibited women, who were not licensee, wives of licensee's, or bar managers, from being bartenders.


OVERVIEW: The female bartender worked in a the bar at a hotel. She challenged the city's ordinance on constitutional grounds. The trial court held that the ordinance was valid and denied her motion for a temporary injunction and dissolved her temporary restraining order. On appeal, the court affirmed the order of the trial court. The court held that prohibiting employment of women as bartenders was not unconstitutional as depriving them of liberty or property in violation of the due process clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. The ordinance was a police regulation on the retail "on sale" liquor business adopted to preserve the public peace. Legislation may exclude women from certain employments. The court believed there was a factual difference between the ability of men and women to function as bartenders. Permitting the employment of women as bartenders encouraged the presence of women in drinking places and that drinking by women would be encouraged and that result was against the public interest. There was difference in the relationships between a woman who was a licensee or whose husband was a licensee and other women.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court and held the ordinance valid.

 

746 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Stevens v. Federal Cartridge Corp.


No. 34,617


Supreme Court of Minnesota


226 Minn. 148; 32 N.W.2d 312; 1948 Minn. LEXIS 581



April 23, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the district court for Hennepin county to recover on a common count for services rendered and material furnished by plaintiffs, a copartnership, to defendant. From an order, Lars O. Rue, Judge, overruling plaintiffs' demurrer to the answer, plaintiffs appealed, the court having certified the question involved as important and doubtful.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff subcontractor sought review of the order of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) overruling plaintiff's demure to defendant contractor's answer that the court lacked jurisdiction because plaintiff had not exhausted the administrative remedies provided in the Contract Settlement Act of 1944, 41 U.S.C.S. §§ 101 to 125.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a prime government contractor during World War II. Plaintiff was a subcontractor that reconditioned ammunition boxes for defendant. In October 1944, defendant terminated their contract and plaintiff sued to recover for services rendered. Defendant contended that plaintiff was required by the Contract Settlement Act 1944 (Act), 41 U.S.C.S. §§ 101-125 to file a claim and exhaust its administrative remedies before suing on the contract. The plaintiff demurred contending that the Act did not apply to it as a subcontractor. The trial court overruled the demure and certified the question for appeal. Since the court found the Act was ambiguous, the court looked to the congressional intent in passing the Act. The court concluded that to protect the post-war economy, congress provided the procedures of the Act to expedite the settlement of government contracts and intended it to apply to contractors and subcontractors. Therefore, the court affirmed the order.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed because plaintiff, as a subcontractor on defendant contractor's government contract, was required to attempt to settle using statutory administrative procedures before suing on a contract.

 

747 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Leighton v. Abell


Nos. 34,691, 34,692


Supreme Court of Minnesota


225 Minn. 565; 31 N.W.2d 646; 1948 Minn. LEXIS 557



March 15, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Taxpayer's action in the district court for Hennepin county for a declaratory judgment that the charter proposed by the Minneapolis Charter Commission for submission to the voters at a special election is violative of Minn. Const. art. 4, § 36, and that M.S.A. 410.23, 410.24, and 410.25 is unconstitutional insofar as it authorizes the submission of any home rule charter or amendment thereto contrary to said constitutional provisions. The matter was heard before Albert H. Enersen, judge of the ninth judicial district acting for the judges of the fourth judicial district. After adverse findings, plaintiff, defendants Stanley Anderson and others as members of the Minneapolis city council, and Charles C. Swanson as city clerk appealed from the judgment.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, taxpayer, the city, members of the city council, and the city clerk, sought review of the decision by the district court for Hennepin county (Minnesota), which entered judgment for respondent city charter commission in the taxpayer's action for a declaratory judgment that the proposed charter was violative of Minn. Const. art. 4, § 36, and that Minn. Stat. Ann. §§ 410.23, 410.24, and 410.25 were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer alleged that §§ 410.23, 410.24, and 410.25 was unconstitutional insofar as it authorized the submission of any home rule charter or amendment thereto contrary to Minn. Const. art. 4, § 36. On appeal, the court reversed. The court found that so long as § 36 remained in force, the city charter, as originally adopted and subsequently amended, was the charter of the city; the process of adoption did not start over, nor could the legislature have started it over. The court reasoned that the phrase "and not otherwise" in § 36 emphasized the intent to foreclose and prohibit any other method of modifying the home rule charter; it must be by amendment only. The court further reasoned that the charter commission was endowed with no other power or authority to modify or change "the charter," nor did § 36 permit the legislature so to endow it; the provisions for formulating and submitting the original charter and, after its adoption, for formulating and submitting amendments constituted the total extent of power of proposal vested in the charter commission by the constitution. The court also held that Minn. Stat. Ann. §§ 410.23, 410.24, and 410.25 were unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision which entered judgment for the city charter commission in the taxpayer's action for a declaratory judgment.

Land O'Lakes Dairy Co. v. Sebeka Village


No. 34,519


Supreme Court of Minnesota


225 Minn. 540; 31 N.W.2d 660; 1948 Minn. LEXIS 555



March 12, 1948 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied by U.S. Supreme Court June 14, 1948.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action in the district court for Wadena county against the village of Sebeka, the county of Wadena, and the officers thereof, the state auditor and treasurer, the state commissioner of taxation, and the attorney general for a declaratory judgment that certain property in the village of Sebeka be adjudged exempt from taxation as property of the United States. From an order, D. M. Cameron, Judge, sustaining the separate demurrers of defendants to the amended complaint, plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed the judgment of the District Court for Wadena County (Minnesota), which found in favor of defendants, a village and others, in the taxpayer's action for declaratory judgment that certain property in the village was exempt from taxation as property of the United States. The taxpayer argued that the trial court erred in sustaining defendants' demurrers.


OVERVIEW: During Wold War II, the taxpayer, a dairy company, entered into an agreement with the United States under which the dairy company acquired the necessary real estate to develop a plant for the manufacture of dried milk products. The United States agreed to buy the plant from the taxpayer and then lease it back. The agreement was to terminate, and the dairy was to repurchase the facility, when the war emergency was over. The taxpayer filed an action under Minn. Stat. Ann. § 278.03 against the village and others arguing that the property was exempt from real and personal property tax as property of the United States. The action was dismissed, so the taxpayer filed an action for a declaratory judgment that the property was exempt from taxation. The trial court sustained defendants' demurrers, and the taxpayer appealed. The court affirmed. The court held that although the declaratory judgment act was available for the purpose of testing the validity of the personal property tax levy and assessment, the taxpayer was not entitled to this relief. The taxpayer voluntarily assumed to pay the tax, so it was not entitled to a judgment declaring its promise meaningless.


OUTCOME: In the taxpayer's action for declaratory judgment, the court sustained defendants' demurrers to the taxpayer's complaint.

Sazenski v. O'Keefe

COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 1357



December 21, 1999, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Judicial Appeal Panel. File No. 115-C.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, patient who had been committed as mentally ill and dangerous, sought review of decision of the Judicial Appeal Panel denying appellant's request for a transfer from a security hospital to an open hospital.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, patient who was committed as mentally ill and dangerous for an indeterminate period, petitioned for a transfer from security hospital to an open hospital. OUTCOME: Court held that decision of the appeal panel to deny appellant's transfer to an open hospital because of safety concerns was supported by clear and convincing evidence.

 

750 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rewitzer


C4-99-807


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 1370



December 21, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Brown County District Court. File No. K4-97-0625. Hon. Terri Stonburner.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal appellant sought review of an order from the Brown County District Court (Minnesota) denying his petition for postconviction relief, arguing on appeal that the district court abused its discretion by imposing excessive fines for three counts of a second-degree controlled substance crime.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed an order denying appellant's petition to vacate or reduce fines imposed for three drug sales offenses. Minn. Stat. § 609.101(5)(b) permitted, but did not require, a court to reduce fines at its discretion. The gravity of drug-related offenses was not determinable solely by the value of drugs sold. Appellant's admitted profit motive and enjoyment in selling drugs for money, his recidivism despite prior judicial intervention, and the regularity of his drug dealing demonstrated that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by imposing the fines. Based on the same findings, as well as the fact that appellant was permitted to make installment payments, was young, employed, and had long-term earning potential, the court also held that the fines did not violate the Excessive Fines Clauses of Minn. Const. art. I, § 3 or U.S. Const. amend. VIII.


OUTCOME: An order denying defendant's postconviction petition to reduce fines imposed for three drug sale offenses was affirmed, because the trial court did not abuse its discretion by imposing the fines, in light of appellant's admitted profit motive and enjoyment in selling drugs, his prior offenses, and his repeated drug dealing.

 

751 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


In re L.A.M.


C6-99-792


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 1371



December 21, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court. File No. J7-98-064143. Hon. Herbert P. Lefler, III.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; motion denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision by the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) terminating her parental rights, arguing on appeal that the district court erred in admitting evidence of prior chemical dependency and that it did not have clear and convincing evidence to support its decision to terminate her parental rights.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed a decision to terminate appellant's parental rights. The trial court did not err by admitting evidence of appellant's past conduct, involving repeated failures to successfully defeat an alcohol addiction, because, while the court had to consider the parent's present ability to care for the child, there was no authority that rendered the parent's past conduct irrelevant. Issues raised in prior administrative proceedings were not identical to the petition for termination of parental rights and were therefore not barred from consideration by collateral estoppel. Based on evidence that appellant's relapses into alcoholism endangered the child and that she failed to correct the conditions that led to the prior out-of-home placement, the decision to terminate parental rights was supported by substantial evidence and was not clearly erroneous, and the conclusion that termination of parental rights was in the child's best interests was supported by clear and convincing evidence.


OUTCOME: Decision to terminate appellant's parental rights was affirmed, because it was supported by substantial evidence and was not clearly erroneous, and the conclusion that termination was in the best interests of the child was supported by clear and convincing evidence.

Muhar v. One (1) 1997 Harley-Davidson Motorcycle


C6-99-1053


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 1372



December 21, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Itasca County District Court. File No. C0971273. Hon. Lois J. Lang.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from Itasca County District Court (Minnesota) in which the court granted summary judgment to respondent in the action for the forfeiture of appellant's motorcycle under Minn. Stat. § 169.1217.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was arrested and convicted of driving while under the influence. At the time of appellant's arrest, his driving privileges had been canceled and he had three prior driving while under the influence convictions. The court then granted respondent summary judgment in the action for the forfeiture of appellant's motorcycle. Appellant challenged the district court's order and argued the forfeiture was "grossly disproportionate" to the offense committed. On appeal, the court held that an in personam forfeiture was unconstitutional if the amount of the forfeiture was grossly disproportional to the gravity of appellant's offense. Here, the court held appellant fell within the category of individuals the forfeiture was intended to reach, namely repeat intoxicated drivers. Moreover, appellant's underlying criminal conduct was not "harmless" because he was arrested after the police witnessed him forcing other drivers onto the shoulder of a highway because of his erratic drunk driving. Judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision because it held that the forfeiture of appellant's motorcycle was not "grossly disproportionate" to the offense appellant committed.

State v. Spear


C5-99-427


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 1317



December 14, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied February 15, 2000.
Review denied by State v. Spear, 2000 Minn. LEXIS 99 (Minn., Feb. 15, 2000)


PRIOR HISTORY: Ramsey County District Court. File No. K1982385. Hon. Gary W. Bastian.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought to reverse his Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) conviction of second-degree sale of methamphetamine.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his second-degree sale of methamphetamine conviction, contending that evidence seized from a vehicle should have been suppressed. The court held that appellant had standing to challenge the search and seizure because he had a possessory interest in the vehicle, although it was registered to another person, and affirmed the conviction. The vehicle was impounded because it was on a public street and improperly registered. There was no evidence that police procedures were not followed in conducting the inventory search, and the fact that the search was conducted at the scene by an officer involved in the criminal investigation did not invalidate the search. Appellant's contention that admission of a prior drug conviction was error also was rejected because the conviction was clear and convincing proof of appellant's participation in a prior similar crime, was relevant and material to the State's case, and was more probative than prejudicial.


OUTCOME: Conviction was affirmed; evidence was seized from a properly impounded vehicle and an inventory search was authorized. A prior drug conviction was admissible because it was proof of a prior similar crime, was relevant and material to the State's case, and was more probative than prejudicial.

 

754 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Programmed Land, Inc. v. O'Connor


CX-99-777, C7-99-1210


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


602 N.W.2d 895; 1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 1311



December 7, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Hennepin County District Court. Dakota County District Court. File No. 9810713. File No. C4979320.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Consolidated appeals were taken from the Hennepin and Dakota County District Courts (Minnesota), which denied appellant's motion for summary judgment and held for appellees on the merits, respectively, appellants arguing that the statute of limitations barred recovery for overpayment of property taxes.


OVERVIEW: A consolidated appeal was based on the miscalculation of property taxes by appellant counties and the subsequent overpayment of taxes. One county was denied summary judgment by the district court, and in the other action, appellee was awarded judgment on the merits. Both counties appealed, arguing that an exclusive remedy existed for recovery of overpayments, and that the statute of limitations had passed. The court held that Minn. Stat. § 278.01 was not the exclusive remedy. However, although the lower court erred in providing relief for a violation of due process, equity could grant relief from a unilateral mistake of law by the auditor. Therefore, the district court in one case properly granted relief, and in the other, properly refused to dismiss equitable claims. Furthermore, appellees could recover under the abatement statute if they could establish that the mistake was the result of a clerical error.


OUTCOME: Affirmed, because an equitable remedy was available for a mutual mistake of law, and the statutory remedy was not exclusive.

COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his indeterminate commitment as a sexually dangerous person and a sexual psychopathic personality pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 253B.02 (18b, -18c) (1998) from the Steele County District Court (Minnesota).


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his indeterminate commitment as a sexually dangerous person and a sexual psychopathic personality pursuant to Minn. Stat. 253B.02 (18b,-18c) (1998). The court affirmed, finding: that the notice requirement was directory and the commitment was not invalid because the department of corrections (DOC) failed to notify the county attorney 12 months prior to release; that the admission of DOC assessment reports, including opinion information, under Minn. Hawes v. 1997 Jeep Wrangler


C3-99-782


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


602 N.W.2d 874; 1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 1241



November 23, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Hennepin County District Court. File No. 98-4520.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of an order of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which denied its motion for summary judgment and granted judgment in favor of respondent, in a vehicle forfeiture proceeding under Minn. Stat. § 169.1217 (1998).


OVERVIEW: Respondent was arrested for driving under the influence of alcohol. Because he had two separate impaired driving convictions or license revocations, appellant state seized his vehicle and began forfeiture proceedings under Minn. Stat. § 169.1217(c) (1988). Respondent filed a civil complaint, alleging that the seizure was improper and violated double jeopardy. After respondent pleaded guilty to the driving under the influence charge, appellant state moved for summary judgment. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's denial of appellant's motion for summary judgment and the court's sua sponte grant of judgment for respondent. The trial court erred in concluding that the statute violated constitutional prohibitions against double jeopardy and excessive fines. The statute did not violate equal protection rights, since it was rationally related to the statute's remedial purpose. Once the court determined that appellant met all the statutory requirements, an order for forfeiture was mandatory.


OUTCOME: Reversed the denial of appellant state's motion for summary judgment and the trial court's sua sponte grant of judgment in favor of respondent in vehicle forfeiture proceedings, since the trial court erred in concluding that the forfeiture violated respondent's constitutional rights.

Ebin v. City of S. St. Paul


CX-99-584


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 1249



November 23, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied February 15, 2000.
Review denied by, Request denied by Ebin v. City of S. St. Paul, 2000 Minn. LEXIS 102 (Minn., Feb. 15, 2000)


PRIOR HISTORY: Dakota County District Court. File No. C0967280. Hon. Duane R. Harves.
In re Lafayette Dev. Corp., 567 N.W.2d 743, 1997 Minn. App. LEXIS 925 (Minn. Ct. App., 1997)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent appealed the judgment of the Dakota County District Court (Minnesota) finding respondent city liable for the tort and statutory claims filed by appellant against respondent.


OVERVIEW: Respondent city denied access of a street to appellant who wanted to improve land abutting city street. As a result, appellant brought an action to recover damages for tortious interference with a contract, unconstitutional taking, violation of the Minnesota Open Meeting Law, Minn. Stat. § 471.705, and violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The trial court entered judgment for appellant, and respondent appealed. On appeal, the court found that respondent did not have official immunity from the tort action because respondent's actions were malicious, and not discretionary or individual. Furthermore, the court found that respondent was not statutorily immune from the tort because such immunity did not extend to municipalities. Additionally, the court found that legislative immunity did not protect respondent from liability under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and the state court had jurisdiction to hear the federal claim. Consequently, the judgment finding respondent liable was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment finding respondent city liable for the tort and statutory claims appellant filed against respondent was affirmed because respondent was not immune from the suit and the state court had jurisdiction.

 

758 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Kremer v. Commissioner of Pub. Safety


C3-99-1026


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 1217



November 16, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court. File No. 476 578. Hon. Allen Oleisky.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the order of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which rescinded the revocation of respondent's driver's license after concluding that the implied consent statute's, Minn. Stat. § 169.123, (5c)(d) (1998), limited-discovery provisions violated the separation of powers doctrine.


OVERVIEW: Respondent was arrested for driving while under the influence. Respondent's driver's license was subsequently revoked. The district court rescinded the revocation of respondent's license, however, after determining that the limited-discovery provisions of the implied consent statute, Minn. Stat. § 169.123, (5c)(d) (1998), violated the separation of powers doctrine. Appellant, Minnesota Commissioner of Public Safety, challenged the order. On appeal, the court reversed the order. Respondent did not have standing to challenge the constitutionality of the statutory discovery provisions, because respondent did not show that he was harmed, or that he was in imminent danger of being harmed, by the limited-discovery provisions. Respondent failed to demonstrate that the statutory discovery limitations were the direct cause of any inability to obtain the requested information. Further, respondent did not attempt to establish that, absent the information, he could not proceed and did not attempt to conduct any other discovery.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed. Respondent did not have standing to challenge the constitutionality of the statutory discovery provisions, because respondent did not show that he was harmed, or that he was in imminent danger of being harmed, by the limited-discovery provisions.

State v. Dolan


C5-99-86


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 1197



November 9, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied January 25, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Minn. LEXIS 40.


PRIOR HISTORY: Dakota County District Court. File No. K19849. Hon. Karen Asphaug.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Dakota County District Court (Minnesota), which denied his motion to suppress evidence, excluded expert testimony, included a jury instruction on the revival of an aggressor's right to self-defense, and imposed a 39 month, executed sentence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of second-degree assault, fleeing an officer, fourth-degree assault, criminal vehicular operation resulting in bodily harm, driving after cancellation, fifth-degree controlled substance crimes, and possession of a legend drug. Appellant challenged the trial court's denial of his motion to suppress evidence, claiming an unconstitutional search and seizure of his person, his blood and urine, and items in his car. Appellant also challenged exclusion of expert testimony, the use of a jury instruction on the revival of an aggressor's right to self-defense, and the trial court's imposition of a 39 month sentence. The court rejected all appellant's challenges, finding the police articulated facts sufficient to justify an investigatory seizure of appellant, and the trial court did not abuse its discretion in excluding expert testimony, giving an instruction on the revival of an aggressor's right of self-defense, or concluding appellant's offenses were not a single behavioral incident for sentencing purposes.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; there were sufficient facts to justify an investigatory seizure of appellant, and the trial court did not abuse its discretion in excluding expert testimony, giving certain jury instructions, or concluding appellant's offenses were not a single behavioral incident for sentencing purposes.

State v. Majka


C7-99-168


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 1176



November 2, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied January 18, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Minn. LEXIS 24.


PRIOR HISTORY: Crow Wing County District Court. File No. K0972758. Hon. Fredrick J. Casey.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted appellant discretionary review of the denial by the Crow Wing County District Court (Minnesota) of appellant's pretrial suppression motion alleging the evidence obtained against him was the fruit of an unconstitutional seizure.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was lawfully parked, but on a dead-end one-lane road, in the dark with the headlights off and the engine running, in an area where teenagers frequently congregated for illegal drinking and smoking, when an officer, who was aware that offenses characteristic of these facts were frequently committed at that location, parked behind him. Appellant was seized when the officer instructed him to remain in his car. A search of the car turned up a plastic bag containing one gram of methamphetamine. Prior to trial appellant moved to suppress the evidence. The trial court denied the motion. On review, appellant contended his seizure, for merely being present in the area, was unconstitutional. The court disagreed, holding that appellant was not merely present or passing through a high-crime area, but that, on the facts below, there was a valid investigatory seizure, and the trial court properly denied appellant's motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of appellant's motion to suppress, rejecting appellant's claim that he was arrested merely for being in the area, when he parked in an area frequented by teenagers who engaged in illegal activities at that location and the officer was aware of these facts.

 

761 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Sutherlin v. State


C7-99-915, C9-99-916


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 1201



November 2, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Granted January 18, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Minn. LEXIS 18.
Review denied by, Motion granted by Sutherlin v. State, 2000 Minn. LEXIS 18 (Minn., Jan. 18, 2000)


PRIOR HISTORY: Washington County District Court. File No. C4991676. Hon. Thomas G. Armstrong.
State v. Folden, 1994 Minn. LEXIS 220 (Minn., Mar. 15, 1994)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoners challenged the judgment of the Washington County District Court (Minnesota) dismissing a writ of habeas corpus, arguing that (1) wage deductions violated the Fifth Amendment and the prohibition against bills of attainder, and (2) being forced to work constituted involuntary servitude violating the Thirteenth Amendment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant prisoners were incarcerated at state correctional facilities. After they were sentenced, the state Department of Corrections implemented a statewide policy of deducting room and board costs from inmates' wages to offset the costs of incarceration. The court held that: (1) habeas corpus proceedings were proper because appellants were challenging changes in the conditions of their confinement on constitutional grounds; (2) requiring prisoners to work for private industry was constitutional and did not violate the U.S. Const. amend. XIII; (3) deducting money from prisoners' wages to offset incarceration costs was not so punitive either in purpose or effect as to constitute additional criminal punishments for the same offense; and (4) because deducting costs from prisoners' wages was civil in nature, appellants' argument that it violated the constitutional prohibition against bills of attainder was without merit.


OUTCOME: Dismissal affirmed; requiring appellants to work for private industry was constitutional; deducting money from appellants' wages to offset incarceration costs was not so punitive in purpose or effect as to constitute additional criminal punishments for the same offense; and was civil in nature, and thus not a bill of attainder.

 

762 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Whitley


C4-99-726


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 1135



October 12, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court. File No. 99013403. Hon. Harvey C. Ginsberg.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged judgment of Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) which dismissed misdemeanor citation against respondent for driving after suspension and accepted respondent's plea of guilty to petty misdemeanor speeding citation.


OVERVIEW: Respondent was charged with driving after suspension (DAS) and speeding. When the judge asked respondent if his license had been suspended for failure to pay a fine, respondent replied he had paid the fine before he received the DAS citation, but was told there was a delay in processing payment. The court accepted this explanation and dismissed the DAS citation. Appellant objected on the ground that there were facts in the file substantiating the charge. Respondent then pleaded guilty to the speeding violation and was fined. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment noting that the power of the district court to accept respondent's plea to a lesser offense, over the state's objection, should only be invoked in rare instances of "manifest injustice." The court determined that the facts of this case did not present a manifest injustice; therefore, the district court abused its discretion in dismissing respondent's DAS citation.


OUTCOME: Court reversed judgment noting that power of district court to accept respondent's plea to lesser offense, over state's objection, should only be invoked in rare instances of manifest injustice. Court determined that facts did not present manifest injustice, thus, the district court abused its discretion in dismissing respondent's citation.

 

763 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Coffee v. O'Keefe


C0-99-707


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 1110



October 5, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Judicial Appeal Panel. File No. 148-A.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the Judicial Appeal Panel's (Minnesota) denial of his petition for transfer pursuant to the Interstate Compact on Mental Health or full discharge pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 253B.18(15) (1998) from his indeterminate commitment as mentally ill and dangerous.


OVERVIEW: Appellant committed second-degree murder, but was found not guilty by reason of mental illness. Appellant was committed for an indeterminate period and appellant's symptoms improved. Following appellant's petition for transfer or discharge, the court-appointed examiner and appellant's case manager stated that appellant lacked insight into his chemical dependency and needed to make further progress to prevent a relapse. The court held found clear and convincing evidence to deny appellant's full discharge. Continued commitment was not unconstitutional because it bore a reasonable relation to the original reasons for his commitment. The court denied the transfer because appellant would not be subject to state monitoring making the transfer tantamount to a discharge. The Interstate Compact on Mental Health, Minn. Stat. § 245.51 (1998), did not apply because appellant was institutionalized for the commission of an offense for which, in the absence of mental illness, he would be incarcerated.


OUTCOME: Denial of petition affirmed; full discharge denied because there was clear and convincing evidence appellant needed continued commitment. Transfer denied because appellant would not be monitored in another state, and the Interstate Compact on Mental Health did not apply because in the absence of mental illness appellant would be incarcerated.

 

764 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Hendrickson v. City of Duluth


C2-99-272


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 1116



October 5, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: St. Louis County District Court. File No. CX97600347. Hon. Gerald E. Maher.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed St. Louis County District Court's (Minnesota) directed verdict for defendants on Minn. Stat. § 626.89 (1998), part of the Peace Officer Discipline Procedures Act, and summary judgments for defendants on plaintiff's claims for libel, violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and unlawful discharge.


OVERVIEW: In a libel and wrongful discharge case, the court affirmed summary judgment against the plaintiff on his libel claims, because he failed to prove malice on the part of the public official defendants. Because the underlying individual defamation claims failed, defendant employers had no respondeat superior liability. Summary judgment for defendants on plaintiff's 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 due process claims was affirmed because plaintiff failed to prove that individual defendants deprived him of due process or that municipal policy contributed to a constitutional deprivation. Investigation of plaintiff's personal life did not violate plaintiff's right to privacy, since it involved on-duty behavior. Defendants investigating plaintiff's misconduct were protected by qualified immunity because they were performing a discretionary function. Collateral estoppel precluded plaintiff's previously arbitrated wrongful discharge claim. Directed verdict for defendants on plaintiff's Minn. Stat. § 626.89 claims was proper because no evidence suggested that a contrary verdict could be reached.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment for defendants affirmed because of qualified immunity and plaintiff's failure to prove public official defendants' actual malice or that defendants' actions or municipal policy constituted a constitutional deprivation. Directed verdict affirmed because of insufficient evidence to prove retaliatory discipline or denial of plaintiff's right to counsel.

State v. Goode

COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA

PRIOR HISTORY: Ramsey County District Court. File No. K3962450. Hon. Lawrence D. Cohen.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant appealed from a Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) determination that he was ineligible to receive jail credit for time served in an alternative correctional program, by challenging the constitutionality of Minn. Stat. § 241.277(5) (1998) on equal protection grounds under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1 and the Minnesota Constitution.

App. P. 103.04, because his arguments could not be decided on the present record, which was a consequence of the fact that the statute was not raised or considered in the trial court proceedings.

766 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Nynas v. Commissioner of Pub. Safety


C9-99-74


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 1096



September 28, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court. File No. IC476354. Hon. Harry S. Cramp.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver appealed an order in favor of appellee commissioner, entered by the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), in a case where appellant sought to challenge the constitutionality of the discovery limitations of Minnesota's implied consent statute, Minn. Stat. § 169.123, subd. 5c(d) (1998).


OVERVIEW: Appellant driver had his driver's license revoked by appellee commissioner. The revocation arose out of his arrest for driving under the influence of alcohol. Appellant petitioned for judicial review of the revocation order. Also, he obtained police reports and the identity of witnesses, but requested no additional discovery. Appellant alleged the implied consent law's discovery limitations were an unconstitutional violation of the separation of powers doctrine. The trial court held appellant had no standing to raise the discovery issue because he had received all requested discovery. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that state statutes were presumed to be constitutional and that appellant bore the burden of establishing the constitutional infirmity beyond a reasonable doubt. The court held appellant did not meet the burden because he sought no discovery beyond that permitted by the implied consent statute, and thus, suffered no harm from the statute's limitations.


OUTCOME: Order of the trial court affirmed because appellant driver failed to seek discovery beyond that permitted by the implied consent statute, and thus, he suffered no harm from the discovery limitations imposed by the statute which meant he had no standing to challenge the limitations.

In re Woodruff


C2-99-689


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 1097



September 28, 1999, Filed

Review denied by In re Woodruff, 1999 Minn. LEXIS 776 (Minn., Nov. 23, 1999)


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court. File No. P79760079. Hon. Ann Leslie Alton.
Woodruff v. State, 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 565 (Minn. Ct. App., June 1, 1993)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) decision, which committed him as a sexual psychopathic personality or as a sexually dangerous person under Minn. Stat. § 253B.18, subd. 1 (1998).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was committed by the trial court as a sexual psychopathic personality or as a sexually dangerous person under Minn. Stat. § 253B.18, subd. 1 (1998). Defendant appealed, claiming the evidence was insufficient to commit him and Minn. Stat. § 253B.18, subd. 1 (1998) was unconstitutional. The court affirmed because although the medical expert relied on her notes at trial, it was defendant's refusal to cooperate that necessitated reliance on notes; the medical expert testimony recommended further treatment; and the state supreme court recently held that Minn. Stat. § 253B.18, subd. 1 (1998) was constitutional.


OUTCOME: Defendant's commitment affirmed because the medical expert at hearing was obliged to use notes due to defendant's lack of cooperation; the medical expert recommended further treatment; and the sexually dangerous person statute was held to be constitutional.

State v. Camp


C8-99-20


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 1071



September 21, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied November 23, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Minn. LEXIS 778.


PRIOR HISTORY: Ramsey County District Court. File No. K6-97-3859. Hon. Walter A. Bowser.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) of possession of a controlled substance in violation of Minn. Stat. § 152.022, subd. 2(1) (1996), based on alleged violations of his rights under U.S. Const. amend. IV.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction of possession of a controlled substance under Minn. Stat. § 152.022, subd. 2(1) (1996), alleging that his right to be free from warrantless searches and seizures under U.S. Const. amend. IV had been violated. The court affirmed because the arresting officer had an objective, articulable suspicion that defendant participated in a drug transaction. The officer observed that the defendant was in a house, immediately prior to the execution of a search warrant for drug trafficking, for five to ten minutes, the average time required for such activity, based on the officer's experience. Also, a Miranda warning was not required prior to searching defendant's truck because defendant was not seized to the degree associated with a formal arrest, making his statements about drugs in his truck voluntary and sufficient to generate probable cause for the search.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed because arresting officer had an objective, articulable suspicion that defendant participated in a drug transaction; a Miranda warning was not required prior to searching defendant's truck since defendant was not seized to the degree associated with a formal arrest at the time of his statements to police.

State v. Kerling


C9-98-1733


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 1010



August 31, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court. File No. 97079854. Hon. Denise D. Reilly.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged her conviction by the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) for prostitution, in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.324(3)(1) (1996).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of prostitution, in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.324(3)(1) (1996). On appeal, she claimed that the statute violated her constitutional right to privacy, was unconstitutionally vague, was an unconstitutional establishment of religion, and violated equal protection. She also contended that the evidence was insufficient to support the conviction, and that the jury instructions were erroneous. The appellate court reversed holding that the trial court gave erroneous jury instructions. The court found that the erroneous instruction failed to charge that the proof of guilt must be beyond a reasonable doubt and instead charged that it could merely be a reasonable construction of the evidence. The court found that there was sufficient evidence to support a conviction, so it remanded for a new trial. The court rejected appellant's challenge to the constitutionality of Minn. Stat. § 609.324(3)(1) (1996).


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed appellant's conviction for prostitution and remanded the case for a new trial where it found that, although there was sufficient evidence to support a conviction, the trial court gave jury instructions that failed to charge that the proof of guilt must be beyond a reasonable doubt.

State v. Cabrera


C4-99-192


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 1012



August 31, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Further Review Denied November 17, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Minn. LEXIS 764.


PRIOR HISTORY: Benton County District Court. File No. K1-98-825. Hon. James W. Hoolihan.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the Benton County District Court (Minnesota) denial of his motion to suppress evidence of a weapon found on his person during a traffic stop.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with carrying a concealed weapon without a license and obstructing legal process. After the district court denied his motion to suppress, appellant entered a Lothenbach plea, explicitly reserving his right to appeal the district court's ruling. Appellant argued that he was subjected to an unconstitutional stop and frisk. The appellate court held that a warrantless pat down search could be justified if the officer had a valid reason to believe the motorist was engaged in the commission of a more serious crime. On reviewing the facts, the court concluded that the totality of the factors led the police officer reasonably to believe that appellant was engaged in criminal activity and that he may have been armed and dangerous. Thus, the pat down was justified. Accordingly, the denial of the motion to suppress was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Denial of motion to suppress affirmed because warrantless pat down search was justified if officer had a valid reason to believe motorist was engaged in the commission of a more serious crime, and the totality of the factors led the police officer to reasonably so believe.

State v. Lyman


CX-98-2311


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 985



August 24, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied October 26, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Minn. LEXIS 725.
Review denied by State v. Lyman, 1999 Minn. LEXIS 725 (Minn., Oct. 26, 1999)


PRIOR HISTORY: Anoka County District Court. File No. K89714880. Hon. Donald J. Venne.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction of criminal damage to property from the Anoka County District Court (Minnesota), contending that there was insufficient evidence to convict him, and that he received ineffective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction of criminal damage to property, contending that there was insufficient evidence to convict him, and that he received ineffective assistance of counsel. On appeal, conviction was affirmed. In support of its ruling, the court held that there was ample evidence placing appellant at the scene of the crime and indicating that even if he did not directly cause the damage to the vehicles, by fleeing the scene and later trying to conceal his partner's true identity from the police, his actions contributed to the crime. The court further held that appellant's counsel's performance could not have been deemed to have fallen below an objective standard of reasonableness. The court also noted that there was no reasonable probability that, but for counsel's unprofessional errors, the result of the proceeding would have been different.


OUTCOME: Conviction was affirmed, as there was ample evidence to support the conviction. Appellant's counsel's performance could not have been deemed to have fallen below an objective standard of reasonableness, while there was no reasonable probability that, but for counsel's unprofessional errors, the result of the proceeding would have been different.

 

772 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mangan


CX-98-2325


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 986



August 24, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Further Review Denied November 17, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Minn. LEXIS 755.


PRIOR HISTORY: Anoka County District Court. File No. KX-96-15230. Hon. Stephen J. Askew.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the Anoka County District Court (Minnesota), convicting him of failure to obey a lawful police order in violation of Minn. Stat. § 169.02, subd. 2 (1996). Appellant claimed that his rights under the U.S. Const. amend I were violated because he was prevented from passing out political literature during a Halloween parade.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with failure to obey a lawful police order and two other misdemeanor offenses after he ignored a police officer's order to move onto the sidewalk and out of the street, where he had been campaigning as a candidate for public office during the 1996 Halloween Parade. Appellant filed a motion to dismiss the charges on grounds of a lack of probable cause and a challenge to the police order, and to the parade committee rule on which it was based, as a violation of the U.S. Const. amend I. The district court denied the motion to dismiss. Appellant waived a jury trial and submitted the case to the court based on stipulated facts. The court found appellant guilty as charged and concluded that the exclusion of political candidates was a reasonable, content-neutral "time, place, and manner" restriction on speech. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction and held that while a public street is a traditional public forum where free speech is protected, if it is closed and dedicated to a parade, such activity can be prevented by police action and no violation of the U.S. Const. amend. I obtains from such action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for failure to obey a lawful police order and concluded that the regulation that kept appellant from distributing campaign literature in the street was a reasonable time, place, and manner restriction, and did not violate appellant's First Amendment rights.

Otis v. W.W. Holes Mfg. Co.


C4-99-273


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 995



August 24, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Sherburne County District Court. File No. C6971018. Hon. Robert B. Danforth.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant retailer sought review of an order of the Sherburne County District Court (Minnesota) that the funds held in an escrow account for appellant retailer be transferred into an account in the name of respondent state.


OVERVIEW: Respondent state and respondent consumers brought an action against appellant retailer for consumer fraud and violations of the consumer protection laws. Appellant sold its business prior to the trial, and the parties entered into an agreement to place the proceeds of the sale into an escrow account. Upon granting the state's summary judgment motion, the court ordered that the escrow account be attached and that the funds be transferred into another account in the name of the state. Appellant challenged the trial court's order placing the escrow account in the name of the state. The court found that the attachment laws of Minnesota did not prevent the court from placing the escrow account in the name of the state. In affirming the trial court's order, the court noted that the language of attachment statute, Minn. Stat. § 570.051(1), was discretionary, and that it did not find that the court abused its discretion.


OUTCOME: The court noted that attachments were constitutional as long as they followed narrow guidelines and the defendant had an opportunity for a hearing. Appellant retailer was offered a hearing at respondent state's request. The funds in escrow were not released and were subject to the original escrow agreement; thus, the trial court's order transferring the funds to an account in the state's name was proper.
