Schaps v. Anderson-Schaps


C2-99-157


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 946



August 17, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Further Review Denied November 17, 1999.
Review denied by Schaps v. Anderson-Schaps, 1999 Minn. LEXIS 763 (Minn., Nov. 17, 1999)


PRIOR HISTORY: Meeker County District Court. File No. F78444. Michael G. Blee, ALJ.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and dismissed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged a decision of the Meeker County, (Minnesota) District Court contending that he rebutted the statutory presumption that changed circumstances made his support obligation unreasonable and unfair and that his support obligation should not have been increased.


OVERVIEW: Appellant had filed a motion to dismiss an administrative child support proceeding, arguing that the administrative support process was unconstitutional. An ALJ (administrative law judge) had increased appellant's child support obligation then reduced the increase pursuant to a post-hearing motion, and rejected appellant's constitutional claims. Appellant challenged the ALJ ruling. The court reviewed the ALJ findings applying a clearly erroneous standard of review. The court applied existing statutes on child support modification. Child support was not to be modified if the moving party showed a substantial change in circumstances making the existing award unreasonable and unfair. An existing support award was presumptively unreasonable and unfair if applying the guidelines to the parties' current circumstances would produce a support award at least 20% and $ 50 different than the existing award. The court found the ALJ had not abused his discretion in finding appellant had not rebutted the presumption to show the support modification was unfair. Appellant's constitutional claims were dismissed.


OUTCOME: ALJ findings were affirmed in part and dismissed in part by the court as appellant had failed to rebut the presumption the child support award was presumptively unreasonable and unfair, and the state supreme court had already determined the constitutionality of the administrative child support statute.

 

775 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. Commissioner of Pub. Safety


CX-99-245


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 956



August 17, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied October 21, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Minn. LEXIS 718.


PRIOR HISTORY: Washington County District Court. File No. C6-98-1393. Hon. Elizabeth H. Martin.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the Washington County District Court (Minnesota) denying his petition to rescind the revocation of his driver's license following an implied consent hearing. Defendant was arrested for driving while intoxicated with a blood alcohol level of .16.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was arrested for driving while intoxicated (DWI). After a test indicated he had an alcohol concentration of .16, his driving privileges were revoked. Appellant sought judicial review of the license revocation order and served a subpoena on the arresting officer that was subsequently quashed. Appellant challenged the denial of his petition to rescind the revocation of his driver's license following an implied consent hearing. Appellant contended the 1997 amendments to the Minnesota implied consent statute were unconstitutional. The trial court reviewed the license revocation order and sustained the commissioner's order of revocation. The court, on appeal, reviewed appellant's contentions of unconstitutionality of the implied consent statute de novo. The court ruled that in order to challenge the constitutionality of a statute, a party must have had a direct and personal harm resulting from the alleged denial of constitutional rights. The court determined appellant lacked standing to assert any of his claims as he had no previous DWI convictions and had not suffered any harm because he had been afforded a hearing. The trial court judgment against appellant was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the trial court denying appellant's petition was affirmed because appellant lacked standing to pursue a constitutional challenge of the DWI enhancement provisions in the statutes.

 

776 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Schmidt


C5-99-346


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 958



August 17, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Rehearing Denied July 24, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Minn. LEXIS 422.
Petition for Review Granted October 26, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Minn. LEXIS 737.


PRIOR HISTORY: Kandiyohi County District Court. File No. K497847. Hon. Kathryn N. Smith.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a judgment from Kandiyohi County District Court (Minnesota), which dismissed two charges of an amended complaint charging violations of stalking and harassment under Minn. Stat. § 609.749 (1996), because they constituted serialized prosecution under Minn. Stat. § 609.305 (1998).


OVERVIEW: The court granted an appeal by appellant from an order that dismissed two charges in an amended complaint. The court held that the lower court erred in concluding that Minn. Stat. § 609.035(1)(1998), barred appellant from retrying respondent on those charges. Respondent was originally charged and convicted of five counts under the Minnesota harassment/stalking law, Minn. Stat. § 609.749 (1996). Certain provisions of that law were declared unconstitutional. As a result, on appeal, the court granted respondent's motion to dismiss two counts. While this appeal was pending, appellant filed an amended complaint, based on the same conduct that charged respondent with two counts of harassment under Minn. Stat. § 609.749, subd. 2(2), which had not been declared unconstitutional. The court held that this amended complaint did not violate the statute prohibiting serialized prosecution, Minn. Stat. § 609.035, subd. 1 (1998). The court held that these charges were subject to retrial, as they did not result in a conviction or acquittal. Therefore, the court concluded that the same conduct could be the source of a new charge. The court remanded for trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that dismissed the counts, and held that the charges did not violate the Minnesota statute prohibiting serialized prosecution, because the original charges had never resulted in a conviction or acquittal. The court remanded for trial on the amended complaint.

 

777 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Aavang v. Commissioner of Pub. Safety


C6-99-50


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 935



August 10, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court. File No. 476252. Hon. Deborah Hedlund.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) that sustained the revocation of his driver's license, alleging that he was deprived of his right to consult an attorney of his choice and that the implied consent law was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged an order sustaining the revocation of his driver's license and argued that his right to counsel was violated. The record showed that after appellant was detained for driving while under the influence of alcohol and taken to a county hospital, appellant was given a telephone, two phone books, and 43 minutes to locate and consult with an attorney. The court held these actions vindicated appellant's limited right to consult with counsel under the circumstances. Appellant also argued his U.S. Const. amend. V rights were violated by the factual pleading of the implied consent statute. The court disagreed because the statute imposed a notice pleading requirement but did not compel incriminating statements. In addition, the self-incrimination right could be invoked in a civil proceeding only if the compelled statements were inherently self-incriminating. Finally, the court refused to consider appellant's premature argument that he should have been afforded the procedural protections due a criminal defendant since the civil revocation of his license could be used in the future as a criminal sentencing enhancement and affirmed the revocation of appellant's license.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order sustaining the revocation of appellant's driver's license for driving while under the influence of alcohol because appellant had been given an opportunity to consult with counsel before testing and had not been compelled to make incriminating statements.

 

778 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Philipps v. Commissioner of Pub. Safety


C1-99-408


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 855



July 27, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Anoka County District Court. File No. C4989671. Hon. Stephen J. Askew.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner challenged the denial by the Anoka County District Court (Minnesota), of his request for reinstatement of his driving privileges pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 171.19, arguing that, as the result of an unconstitutional search, the exclusionary rule should apply to suppress his identity and the fact that he had a restricted driver's license.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner had a driver's license subject to a "B card" restriction requiring him to abstain entirely from alcohol and controlled substances. He was a passenger in a car that was stopped by police. Petitioner refused to identify himself, and police administered a test and determined petitioner's blood alcohol content was .21. When police asked if he had any weapons, he gave them a knife. Police then conducted a pat down search and found petitioner's identification. A computer search revealed his B card restriction. The commissioner of public safety canceled and denied reinstatement of petitioner's driving privileges. Petitioner filed an application in district court for reinstatement of his driving privileges, pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 171.19, arguing the officer conducted an unconstitutional search that revealed his identity and the fact that he had a restricted driver's license. The district court denied the request. The court of appeals affirmed the denial, holding that petitioner's identity and license restriction were not suppressible, regardless of whether the search was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals affirmed the district court's denial of reinstatement of petitioner's driving privileges because evidence of his identity and the fact that he had a restricted driver's license were not suppressible as the fruits of the police's unconstitutional search. Therefore, the district court properly denied petitioner's request for reinstatement of his driving privileges.

Anoka County v. Countryman


C8-99-213


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 881



July 27, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Anoka County District Court. File No. FX-97-12841. Colia Ciesel, ALJ.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order entered in the Anoka County District Court (Minnesota), by an administrative law judge, that set appellant's monthly child-support obligation at $ 413 and refused to hold appellee liable for reimbursement of public assistance benefits.


OVERVIEW: Appellant father and appellee mother were married. Since the parties' separation, appellee mother had physical custody of the parties' minor children and received public assistance for the children. Appellant did not provide support and appellee county, as assignee of appellee mother's right to support, filed an administrative action against appellant seeking reimbursement for the public assistance provided the children. The administrative law judge (ALJ) set another temporary support obligation, and scheduled a second review hearing. Before the second review hearing, appellant moved to hold appellee mother jointly responsible for repayment of the public assistance After the second hearing, the ALJ raised father's monthly support obligation from $ 186 to $ 413 and denied father's motion to make mother jointly liable for reimbursement of public assistance benefits. Appellant sought review of that order. The court reversed and remanded regarding the increase in support, as appellant was unable to meet the increased level of support. But, the court affirmed the refusal to order reimbursement, because the receipt of the assistance was conditioned upon the inability to meet expenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the part of the order refusing to hold appellee jointly liable for reimbursement of public assistance, because appellee's receipt of public assistance for the children was conditioned on her inability to meet her own expenses. The court reversed the part of the order requiring appellant to pay $ 413 per month, and remanded for a redetermination of child support, as appellant lacked the ability to pay that amount of support.

State v. Rodriguez


C8-99-292


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 885



July 27, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Polk County District Court. File No. KX-98-1170. Hon. Michael J. Kraker.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the District Court, Polk County (Minnesota), denying his petition for a writ of habeas corpus to vacate his conviction on two counts of enhanced gross misdemeanor driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with two counts of enhanced gross misdemeanor driving while intoxicated and two counts of enhanced gross misdemeanor refusal to test. After waiving an omnibus hearing, appellant pleaded guilty. The enhanced gross misdemeanor statutes were adjudged unconstitutional by the state supreme court, and appellant filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus, claiming that his detention was illegal because that decision nullified the statutes under which he was convicted. Appellant's petition was denied. The court ruled that appellant made no challenge to the enhanced gross misdemeanor statute before the decision on the constitutionality of the statutes was released, and therefore, appellant's case was not a currently pending case in which the constitutionality of the statutes had been challenged. Further, the court held that although appellant filed a habeas petition challenging the statute before the amended opinion was released, that did not entitle him to prospective relief. The court affirmed the denial of appellant's petition.


OUTCOME: Order denying appellant's habeas corpus petition was affirmed where appellant did nothing to challenge the constitutionality of the enhanced gross misdemeanor statute until after the decision rendering the statute unconstitutional was released, and although he filed a habeas petition challenging the statute before the amended opinion was released, that did not entitle him to prospective relief.

Kruger v. O'Keefe


CX-99-360

PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court. File No. PP-68556. Hon. Kenneth J. Maas.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which refused to order respondent, Commissioner of Human Services, to transfer appellant from prison to a sexual psychopathic personality treatment center, on the grounds that it did not have the jurisdiction to order the transfer.

The court also held that appellant had no right to the treatment and the state law concerning the sexual dangerous person commitment act was constitutional.

In re Welfare of J.L.Y.


C6-98-2211


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


596 N.W.2d 692; 1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 825



July 20, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Ottertail County District Court. File No. J39850652.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, parents of a juvenile offender, sought review of an order of the Ottertail County District Court (Minnesota) that adjudicated their son delinquent, placed him on indefinite probation, and ordered that he participate in counseling, render community service, and take any medications prescribed after consultation with a physician.


OVERVIEW: Appellants' son had a history of hyperactivity and was adjudicated delinquent after he constructed and exploded a bottle bomb. The court placed him on indefinite probation and ordered him to participate in counseling, render community service, and take all prescribed medications after consultation with a physician. Appellants questioned the appropriateness of the court's adjudication of delinquency without a detailed explanation, but the court held the adjudication was imposed within the limits set by the legislature and was not an abuse of discretion. Appellants also challenged the court's order that their son take medications if prescribed by a physician. The court stated the court below had the authority to order parents to provide special care and treatment for a child in need of such under Minn. Stat. § 260.185(1)(g), but only within constitutional limits. The court held that absent consideration of the Jarvis factors, the order infringed unconstitutionally on the juvenile's right to privacy. The court reversed the order regarding the medications, affirmed the adjudication of delinquency, and reversed and remanded the remaining provisions for written findings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the adjudication of delinquency, reversed the provision relating to medication because it was an unconstitutional infringement of the juvenile offender's privacy, and reversed and remanded the remaining provisions of the disposition for written findings.

State v. Rader


CX-98-2177


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


597 N.W.2d 321; 1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 846



July 20, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Ramsey County District Court. File No. KX981140.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) convicting appellant of driving under the influence on the ground that the prosecution failed to prove beyond reasonable doubt that his alcohol concentration was above the legal threshold.


OVERVIEW: A state trooper stopped appellant for speeding on a highway. The officer noticed the strong odor of an alcoholic beverage on appellant's breath and appellant failed field sobriety tests administered by the officer. Appellant was arrested and submitted to a breath test, which reported a higher alcohol concentration than the legal threshold. Appellant was convicted of driving under the influence. On appeal, he argued that state did not prove beyond reasonable doubt that the indicated alcohol concentration was beyond the legal limit. The court determined that once state made a prima facie showing of the test's reliability and that it followed the statutory procedures, the burden shifted to appellant to introduce evidence of the test's unreliability. The court asserted that appellant failed to establish that the officer manipulated the tests. The conviction and sentence were affirmed.


OUTCOME: Order of criminal conviction was affirmed because once prosecution made a prima facie showing of the test's reliability, the burden shifted to appellant. Appellant, however, failed to prove that the tests were manipulated.

Roberts v. Commissioner of Pub. Safety


C0-99-75


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 803



July 13, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court. File No. IC476117. Hon. Harry S. Crump.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an unpublished opinion, petitioner sought review of a decision of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which sustained the revocation of his driver's license following an implied consent hearing by respondent, contending his right to counsel was not vindicated.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner' right to counsel was vindicated. Petitioner was provided with a telephone, a directory, and access to the telephone to contact anyone he wanted. Moreover, the officer contacted the police department in petitioner' hometown, and allowed him to discuss his concerns regarding reciprocity with that state. The lower court correctly ruled that petitioner did not have standing to challenge the constitutionality of the discovery provisions of Minn. Stat. § 169.123(5)(c)(d) (1998). By failing to demonstrate that the statutory discovery limitations were the direct cause of his purported inability to obtain the requested records, petitioner failed to demonstrate standing to challenge the provision. Petitioner contended that Minn. Stat. § 169.123(5)(c)(b)(3) (1998) was unconstitutional under the U.S. Const. amend. V. Petitioner received a hearing and his petition disclosed no fact that might be incriminating. The statute's requirement, therefore, did not subject him to any personal harm and he lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of the statute. Petitioner's due process arguments were not argued in the lower court and those arguments were therefore waived on appeal.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was affirmed because petitioner's right to counsel was vindicated, petitioner lacked standing for his constitutional statutory challenges, and petitioner waived his due process challenges.

In re L.O.W.

COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA

PRIOR HISTORY: St. Louis County District Court. File No. J9-98-651106. Hon. Galen Wilson.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his petty-offender adjudication for disorderly conduct from the St. Louis County District Court, (Minnesota) asserting that the district court applied the wrong standard of proof and that the evidence was insufficient to support his adjudication.


OVERVIEW: Police were called to a disturbance and received conflicting reports of an incident. When officers stopped appellant and questioned him, he began yelling and using profanity. An officer informed appellant that if he used profanity again, he would be arrested for disorderly conduct. Appellant again used profanity and was arrested for disorderly conduct in violation of a city ordinance. After a hearing, the district court determined that appellant violated the ordinance and adjudicated him a petty offender. The district court ordered him to pay a $ 100 fine or perform an equivalent amount of community service and placed him on probation until he paid the fine or completed the community service. Appellant challenged his petty-offender adjudication for disorderly conduct asserting that the district court applied the wrong standard of proof and that the evidence was insufficient to support his adjudication. The appellate court reversed finding that although the correct standard was applied, the evidence was insufficient to support an adjudication for disorderly conduct.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was reversed because defendant's statements did not constitute fighting words, and the evidence was insufficient to support an adjudication for disorderly conduct.

 

786 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kingery


C9-99-88, C0-99-92


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 728



June 29, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Nobles County District Court. File Nos. T5974039, T3974038. Hon. Timothy K. Connell.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of the judgment of the Nobles County District Court (Minnesota), which found them guilty of violating Minn. Stat. §§ 160.20(4)(b), and 609.05(3), by conspiring to install a drain tile along a highway right-of-way without a permit.


OVERVIEW: Appellants installed a drain tile running parallel to a highway right-of-way, and ending in an outlet three feet from the right-of-way ditch. As a result, they were convicted of conspiracy to commit the installation of a drain tile along a highway right-of-way without a permit, in violation of Minn. Stat. §§ 160.20(4)(b), and 609.05(3), and fined $ 130 each. On appeal, the court held that although the word "along" was not defined in Minn. Stat. § 160.20(4)(b), the word was commonly understood to mean "parallel" or "beside." Because the words in the statute were commonly understood, the statute was not void for vagueness. The court therefor affirmed the convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions of conspiracy to install drains without a permit, because appellants violated a statute that was clear, unequivocal, easily understood, and constitutional.

In re Maria Ave. Natural Gas Explosion


C5-98-2040


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 690



June 22, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Ramsey County District Court. File No. C3-96-11908. Hon. Kathleen R. Gearin.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a summary judgment in the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which dismissed appellant's claim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 for injuries received when respondent municipality's workers broke a gas line, resulting in an explosion. Appellant argued his injuries were caused by respondent's policy, and challenged the constitutionality of the state's tort liability limit statute.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the district court's summary judgment in favor of respondent municipality that dismissed appellant's action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. Appellant was injured when a gas line was broken by respondent's workers, and brought suit alleging he was injured due to the municipality's policies, and brought an action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, which was dismissed upon motion for summary judgment filed by respondent. On appeal, the court found that the appeal was timely; however, there was no violation of due process because appellant failed to allege any facts establishing an abuse of government power and there was no evidence of a policy, as a single incident did not constitute a policy, and mere negligence was not an actionable deprivation under the due process clause. The district court's refusal to consider the expert affidavit was not an abuse of discretion because the deadline for expert witness discovery had passed. The court rejected appellant's argument that the state's tort liability limit was unconstitutional because application of the rational basis test showed that the limits had a legitimate purpose.


OUTCOME: The district court's summary judgment dismissal of appellant's claim was affirmed because there was no allegation of government abuse, and a single incident did not constitute a policy. The court held that the state's tort liability limit statute had a legitimate purpose under the rational basis test and was not unconstitutional.

State v. Texidor


C3-98-1534


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 657



June 15, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court. File No. 98014441. Hon. Cara Lee Neville.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which, after a jury trial, convicted defendant of being a felon in possession of a pistol in violation of Minn. Stat. § 624.713(1)(b). Defendant argued that the trial court committed reversible error when it refused to suppress the pistol discovered during an unconstitutional search of defendant's fanny pack.


OVERVIEW: The conviction entered against defendant for being a felon in possession of a pistol was affirmed because the officer had a reasonable belief that defendant might gain control of a weapon. Defendant was riding as a passenger in a car that had been stopped by the police. An officer observed defendant leaning forward in a furtive manner. Defendant claimed to have no identification at the time of the stop. The officer knew that type of fanny pack frequently was used to carry weapons. The search of the fanny pack was constitutional based on the totality of the circumstances. The officer had a reasonable belief that it was necessary to search the fanny pack.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction entered against defendant for being a felon in possession of a pistol because, based on the totality of the circumstances, the officer had a reasonable belief that defendant might gain control of a weapon. The officer was justified in searching defendant's fanny pack for his own safety.

State v. Sandve


C6-98-1379


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 627



June 8, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Dakota County District Court. File No. K0971652. Hon. Timothy J. McManus.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a Dakota County District Court (Minnesota) decision that convicted him, after a jury trial, of second-degree criminal sexual conduct in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.343, subd. 1(a) (1998).


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his second-degree criminal sexual conduct in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.343, subd. 1(a) (1998) after a jury trial. The appellate court reversed the trial court decision and remanded. The trial court erred by instructing the jury on two alternate theories of guilt for the single second-degree criminal sexual conduct charge as such an instruction violated appellant's substantial right to a fair trial by requiring an unanimous jury verdict pursuant to Minn. R. Crim. P. 26.01, subd. 1(5). The trial court expanded the original allegations by allowing the jury to consider events that allegedly occurred beyond the complaint scope as the disputed instruction allowed the jury to consider separate crimes to justify one charge. The jury instruction relied on two independent acts and it was impossible to determine for which act appellant was unanimously convicted.


OUTCOME: Appellate court reversed a trial court decision convicting appellant, after a jury trial, of second-degree criminal sexual conduct. The trial court improperly instructed the jury on two alternate theories of guilty for the single crime charged and since it was impossible to determine under which theory the jury found appellant guilty, appellant's substantial fair trial rights were violated.

Danielson v. Commissioner of Pub. Safety


C7-99-73


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 636



June 8, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Pine County District Court. File No. C698693. Hon. Douglas Swenson.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision from the Pine County District Court (Minnesota) sustaining the revocation of appellant's driver's license under Minn. Stat. § 169.123(4).


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 169.123(4), appellant's driving privileges were revoked. Appellant alleged the implied consent statute found at Minn. Stat. § 169.123(5)(c)(d) was unconstitutional because it violated his right against self-incrimination. Appellant also contended the discovery provisions of the statute violated his due process rights and the separation of powers doctrine. The revocation of appellant's driver's license was sustained. On appeal, the court affirmed the order sustaining the revocation because appellant did not have standing to challenge the implied consent statute. Appellant was not harmed by the limited discovery process and thus lacked standing. Appellant was advised by the state of possible witnesses and documents that were available through discovery. The state forwarded all discoverable documents and appellant did not contest the facts contained in the record.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision sustaining the revocation of appellant's driving privileges because appellant lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of the implied consent statute. Appellant was not harmed by the statute's discovery process because he obtained all discoverable documents and elected not to dispute the facts on record.

 

791 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Martin


C6-99-145


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


595 N.W.2d 214; 1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 644



June 8, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Review Denied August 25, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Minn. LEXIS 564.


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court. File No. 97057250.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the ruling of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) which revoked his probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from an order revoking his probation. Defendant argued that the district court erred by admitting evidence obtained during an illegal search. Defendant pleaded guilty to third-degree possession of a controlled substance. He was sentenced to thirty-four months in prison, but execution of the sentence was stayed, and defendant was placed on probation for three years. A condition of his probation was that he not possess any nonprescription drug. A year later, defendant was arrested for careless driving. During a search incident to the arrest, police found crack cocaine in defendant's pocket. Defendant moved to suppress the cocaine and he contended that his arrest was illegal because careless driving was a misdemeanor offense. The court held that because the officer did not know of defendant's probation status, the marginal deterrent effect of the exclusionary rule was outweighed. Therefore, the evidence obtained during the illegal search was admissible at defendant's probation revocation hearing.


OUTCOME: The trial court ruled that even though cocaine had been suppressed in the criminal proceeding against defendant, it was admissible in the probation revocation proceeding to prove that defendant violated a condition of his probation. On appeal, the court affirmed this ruling because the evidence obtained during the illegal search was admissible at the revocation hearing.

 

792 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Murray v. Cisar


C0-98-1507


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


594 N.W.2d 918; 1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 582



May 25, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied November 29, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7911.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Carlton County District Court. File No. C0-98-124.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner sought review of the judgment of the Carlton County District Court (Minnesota) which dismissed his claim against respondent prison officials that had claimed the withholding of a percentage of his prison earnings to pay the court ordered fine, pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 243.23(3), was unconstitutional. Appellant also claimed the court had erred in ordering it to pay respondents' costs and fees under Minn. Stat. § 563.02(4).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was sentenced to prison in 1991 and ordered to pay a fine. In 1997, respondent, the inmate accounts supervisor at the prison where appellant was being held, notified appellant that 50 percent of his prison earnings would be set aside for payment of the court ordered charges pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 243.23(3), which authorized such actions. Appellant sued, claiming that the law, as applied to him, was unconstitutional. Because § 243.23(3) did not make a once innocent act committed by appellant illegal, increase his punishment, or deprive him of a once available defense, it was not an unconstitutional ex post facto law. Similarly, the statute was not retrospective because it did not impair any vested property rights of appellant, create a new obligation or duty, or attach a new disability for a past transaction. Therefore, the lower court's dismissal of those claims was affirmed on appeal. However, because only natural persons may recover under Minn. Stat. § 563.02(4), and because respondents, who were represented by the attorney general's office, incurred no costs, the court below was found to have erred when it ordered appellant to pay respondent's fees and costs.


OUTCOME: Judgment dismissing appellant's constitutional claims was affirmed because the application of earnings withholding statute, which had been passed after appellant's sentence, was not an unconstitutional ex post facto law or an unconstitutional retrospective law. Judgment ordering appellant to pay respondents' costs and fees was reversed because respondents incurred no fees or costs and because they were not natural persons under the statute.

 

793 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Dyrhaug v. Commissioner of Pub. Safety


C2-98-2139


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 587



May 25, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court. File No. 476165. Hon. Roberta K. Levy.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Commissioner of Public Safety challenged the order of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) rescinding the revocation of respondent's driving privileges, contending that the lower court erred in concluding that the factual-statement requirement of Minn. Stat. § 169.123(5)(c)(b)(3) violated respondent's right against self-incrimination.


OVERVIEW: Appellant Commissioner of Public Safety challenged the order rescinding the revocation of respondent's driving privileges, contending that the lower court erred in concluding that the factual-statement requirement of Minn. Stat. § 169.123(5)(c)(b)(3) violated respondent's right against self-incrimination. On appeal, judgment was reversed. In support of its ruling, the court held that the factual-statement requirement did not violate respondent's right against self-incrimination, as he could not reasonably apprehend that his factual statement enhanced the threat of criminal prosecution. The court further held that a party had no standing to challenge the constitutionality of a statute absent a direct and personal harm resulting from the alleged denial of constitutional rights. The court noted that the petition disclosed exculpatory, not incriminating facts. Accordingly, the court concluded that respondent had not demonstrated he sustained a direct and personal harm resulting from the enforcement of the factual-statement requirement.


OUTCOME: Judgment was reversed, as respondent had no standing to sue because he failed to demonstrate he sustained a direct and personal harm resulting from the enforcement of the factual-statement requirement.

 

794 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Kraudy v. Commissioner of Pub. Safety


C3-98-1842


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 574



May 25, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Steele County District Court. File No. C9-98-286. Hon. Lawrence E. Agerter.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from an order by Steele County District Court (Minnesota), sustaining the revocation of his driver's license pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 169.123(5)(a), arguing that the arresting officer conducted an unconstitutional investigative stop.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was stopped by a police officer while operating his snowmobile because he believed appellant was operating his snowmobile in violation of a city ordinance. After stopping appellant, the officer developed probable cause to believe appellant was under the influence of alcohol and arrested him for operating his snowmobile while under the influence of alcohol. Appellant refused to submit to testing and his driver's license was revoked pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 169.123(5)(a). Appellant petitioned for judicial review, and lower court sustained the revocation. Appellant sought review. Court held that the circumstances had provided the officer with a particularized and objective basis to suspect appellant of operating his snowmobile in violation of the ordinance, such that the officer was justified in stopping appellant's snowmobile for further investigation.


OUTCOME: Court affirmed lower court's judgment sustaining revocation of appellant's driver's license, holding that the arresting officer had reasonable suspicion that appellant was violating city ordinance in operating his snowmobile and therefore was justified in stopping appellant's vehicle for further investigation.

 

795 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Joelson v. O'Keefe


C7-98-1973, C9-98-1974, C3-98-2120, C5-98-2121, C3-98-2246


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


594 N.W.2d 905; 1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 543



May 18, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Further Review Denied July 28, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Minn. LEXIS 514.
Review denied by Joelson v. O'Keefe, 1999 Minn. LEXIS 514 (Minn., July 28, 1999)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Washington County District Court. Carlton County District Court. File Nos. C3-98-778, C8-98-775, C4-98-773, C1-98-777, and File No. C2-98-2556.
Caprice v. Gomez, 552 N.W.2d 753, 1996 Minn. App. LEXIS 896 (Minn. Ct. App., 1996)
In re Patterson, 1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 1094 (Minn. Ct. App., Nov. 8, 1994)
In re Mattson, 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 805 (Minn. Ct. App., June 20, 1995)
In re Joelson, 344 N.W.2d 613, 1984 Minn. LEXIS 1267 (Minn., 1984)
In re Duvall, 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 1233 (Minn. Ct. App., Dec. 19, 1991)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; motion granted in part and denied in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, who had been committed indeterminately as psychopathic personalities, sought review of the judgments from the Washington County District Court and the Carlton County District Court (Minnesota). The district courts denied appellants' petitions for writs of habeas corpus to challenge the constitutionality of their commitments.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, committed indeterminately as psychopathic personalities, brought petitions for writs of habeas corpus to challenge the constitutionality of their commitments. The district court denied the petitions. The court affirmed. The court rejected appellants' argument that because Hendricks required evidence of an inability to control sexual impulses as a constitutional predicate to commitment as a sexual predator, appellants' commitments as sexual psychopathic personalities (SPP) violated substantive due process. The court pointed out that Minn. Stat. § 253B.02(18b), part of the Minnesota's Sexual Psychopathic Personality Act (Act), did require utter lack of power to control sexual impulses for an SPP commitment. The Act did not deprive appellants of their right to procedural due process. As long as the application of statutory discharge criteria met the constitutional requirement that the nature of the commitment be reasonably related to the purpose for which the person was committed, due process was satisfied. An SPP commitment did not constitute double jeopardy because it was for purposes of treatment, not preventive detention.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments that denied appellants writs of habeas corpus. Minnesota's Sexual Psychopathic Personality Act did not violate substantive or procedural due process because the Supreme Court had upheld challenges to similar laws. A commitment as a sexual psychopathic personality was for purposes of treatment, not preventive detention, and thus did not constitute double jeopardy.

State v. Danforth


C5-98-2054


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 462



May 4, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Danforth, 1999 Minn. LEXIS 468 (Minn., July 28, 1999)


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court. File No. 95074990. Hon. Richard B. Solum.
State v. Danforth, 573 N.W.2d 369, 1997 Minn. App. LEXIS 1424 (1997)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his sentencing in the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) and contended that the court erred by denying his request for a continuance, and denying his notice of removal of the sentencing judge. In his pro se brief, appellant raised several challenges to his sentencing.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of an offense and his sentencing was delayed pending findings by the court psychologist. Appellant requested a continuance in sentencing claiming he did not receive the report in time to properly challenge it. The court denied appellant's request and sentenced him as a patterned sex offender. Appellant challenged his sentence based on insufficient time to prepare for the hearing, lack of notice of being sentenced as a patterned sex offender, violation of his rights of allocution, increase in the original sentence and violation of his U.S. Const. amend I and amend. V rights. The court, on review, found that the trial court had discretion in allowing the late filing of the psychologist's report, that appellant was not punished for not cooperating in the report, that appellant was not deprived of notice of the intent to impose patterned sex offender sentencing or implementing double durational departure sentencing as ordered by the court on prior appeal, that defendant had ample time to examine the psychologist or obtain his own evaluation, and that appellant's constitutional rights were not violated.


OUTCOME: The court concluded appellant had ample time to prepare for the sentencing hearing, was not denied his First and Fifth Amendment rights, had notice that he would be sentenced as a patterned sex offender with double durational departure from the guidelines, was not denied allocution, and the court did not err in imposing sentence. Accordingly, appellant's sentence was affirmed.

State v. Raddatz


CX-98-2292


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 430



April 27, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Clay County District Court. File No. K1-98-2176. Hon. John E. Pearson.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the trial court's pretrial order setting a cash only bail, alleging that the order was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of the trial court's pretrial order setting a cash only bail after appellant was charged with a gross misdemeanor for failing to properly register as a sex offender. Court affirmed the trial court's judgment and held that appellant waived his right to challenge the constitutionality of the bail order because appellant failed to raise the issue with the trial court. At trial, appellant only argued that the bail was unreasonable. Appellant failed to file a motion for reduction or modification of bail raising the constitutional challenge.


OUTCOME: Court affirmed the trial court's judgment setting cash only bail because appellant failed to preserve the issue of the constitutionality of the trial court's judgment for review. Court concluded that appellant did not raise the issue at trial, and instead, only alleged at trial that the bail was unreasonable. Court held that the interests of justice did not require that it overlook appellant's waiver and reach the issue presented on appeal.

Carlson v. Commissioner of Pub. Safety


C2-98-2044


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 433



April 27, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Hennepin County District Court. File No. 476033. Hon. Isabel Gomez.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which sustained the revocation of her driving privileges. Appellant challenged, on constitutional grounds, the procedure for obtaining judicial review of a license revocation under Minn. Stat. § 169.123 (1998).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was arrested for driving while intoxicated and failed a breath test. Her driver's license was revoked, and she petitioned for judicial review of the revocation under Minn. Stat. § 169.123 (1998). At the hearing appellant argued that Minn. Stat. § 169.123(5c)(b)(3), which provided that a petition for judicial review of a driver's license revocation state the facts underlying each claim asserted as a basis for rescission, violated a petitioner's constitutional right to be free from compelled self-incrimination. The lower court held that appellant did not have standing to challenge the new provisions in the implied consent statute and sustained the revocation of her driving privileges. The court affirmed, finding that to have standing, a party raising a constitutional challenge must establish a direct and personal harm resulting from the denial of constitutional rights. Appellant did not allege that the statements she made were or could be used against her in court, or that she was denied a hearing because of her failure to state facts supporting her claim.


OUTCOME: The decision of the lower court sustaining the revocation of appellant's license was affirmed on the basis that appellant had not established that she had standing to challenge the constitutionality of the statute.

In re Love


C4-98-2076


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 454



April 27, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Rice County District Court. File No. P8-98-331. Hon. William A. Johnson.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the Rice County District Court, (Minnesota) that committed appellant as a sexual psychopathic personality and sexually dangerous person in a criminal sexual conduct action.


OVERVIEW: When appellant was about 18, he sexually assaulted a number of boys and girls between ages 4 and 14. He pleaded guilty to several counts of criminal sexual conduct. His prison sentence was stayed and he was entered into an intensive sex offender treatment program. Over a period of several years appellant had numerous violations while in the treatment program and was returned to prison. The state filed a petition to commit appellant as a psychopathic personality. The trial court committed appellant. The court affirmed holding that clear and convincing evidence decisively supported the conclusion that appellant exhibited an utter lack of power to control his sexual impulses. Commitment as a sexual psychopathic personality required a showing that a person evidenced an utter lack of power to control his sexual impulses under Minn. Stat. § 253B.02(18)(b).


OUTCOME: The commitment of appellant was affirmed because commitment as a sexual psychopathic personality required a showing that he had an utter lack of power to control his sexual impulses. The evidence clearly indicated that appellant exhibited a lack of power to control his sexual impulses.

Tracht v. Commissioner of Pub. Safety


C9-98-1473


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


592 N.W.2d 863; 1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 393



April 20, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Further Review Denied July 28, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Minn. LEXIS 465.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Anoka County District Court. File No. C7983119.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Anoka County District Court (Minnesota) sustaining the revocation of appellant's driver's license. Appellant alleged the police violated his U.S. Const. amend. IV right against unreasonable searches and seizures when they entered the garage and home where appellant was staying.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was arrested and charged with driving while intoxicated after he was involved in an accident. The police, acting on a report of an accident, spotted appellant's pick-up truck in his driveway. The truck was damaged and was parked in front of an open garage door. The garage was attached to a house via a service door. The officers entered the garage door and knocked on the service door. A house guest of appellant allegedly gave the officers consent to enter the home. Thereafter, the officers ascertained that appellant was intoxicated and arrested him. Appellant contended that the police violated his U.S. Const. amend. IV right against unreasonable searches and seizures. The court disagreed. The court found that the police entered the garage to knock on the service door, not to collect evidence, and even if the officers did violate appellant's rights, all evidence collected would have been obtained as a result of the inevitable discovery doctrine. The revocation of appellant's license was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the revocation of appellant's driver's license. The court determined that the police did not violate appellant's rights. The police entered appellant's garage in order to knock on a service door, not to search for evidence. Once the officers knocked, they were given consent to enter the house by appellant's house guest.
